The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Qr, under the effect of all factored applied
loads shall be calculated as follows:
Qr = φ * FCp * Ab * KB * KZcp  

where  
  φ    = 0.8  
  FCp  = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  

  where  
    fcp = specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain, MPa (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9)  

  Ab   = bearing area, mm²  
  KB   = length-of-bearing factor (see Clause 6.5.6.5)  
  KZcp = size factor for bearing (see Clause 6.5.6.4)


Clause 118: 6.5.6.3 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.6.3 Effect of loads applied near a support
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 119: 6.5.6.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.6.3.1 Factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Q’r, under the effect of only those factored
loads applied within a distance from the centre of the support equal to the depth of the member shall
be calculated as follows:

Q' = (2/3) * φ * FCp * Ab' * KB * KZcp  

where  
  φ     = 0.8  
  FCp   = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  
  Ab'   = average bearing area, mm² (see Clause 6.5.6.3.2)  

Note: See Figure 6.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 120: 6.5.6.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.6.3.2 Unequal bearing areas on opposite surfaces of a member
Where unequal bearing areas are used on opposite surfaces (top and bottom) of a member, the average
bearing area, A’b, shall be calculated as follows:
Ab' = b * ((Lb1 + Lb2) / 2) ≤ 1.5 * b * (Lb1)

where  
  b     = average bearing width (perpendicular to grain), mm  
  Lb1   = lesser bearing length, mm  
  Lb2   = larger bearing length, mm  

Note: Where a compression member bears on a continuously supported bearing plate, Ab' may be calculated as 1.5 * b * (Lb1).

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 121: 6.5.6.4 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.6.4 Size factor for bearing, KZcp
When the width of a member (dimension perpendicular to the direction of the load) is greater than the
depth of the member (dimension parallel to the direction of the load), the specified strength in
compression perpendicular to grain may be multiplied by a size factor for bearing, KZcp, in accordance
with Table 6.15.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 122: 6.5.6.5 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.6.5 Length-of-bearing factor, KB
When lengths of bearing or diameters of washers are less than 150 mm, specified strengths in
compression perpendicular to grain may be multiplied by a length-of-bearing factor, KB, in accordance
with Table 6.16, provided that
a) no part of the bearing area is less than 75 mm from the end of the members; and
b) bearing areas do not occur in positions of high bending stresses.
KZcp
Note: Alternatively, KB may be calculated as follows:

  KB = (Lb + 9.525) / Lb   for Lb < 150 mm  
  KB = 1.00                for Lb ≥ 150 mm  

where  
  Lb = bearing length measured parallel to grain or washer diameter, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 123: 6.5.7 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.7 Compressive resistance at an angle to grain
The factored compressive resistance at an angle to grain, Nr, shall be calculated as follows:
Nr = (Pr * Qr) / (Pr * sin²θ + Qr * cos²θ)

where  
  Pr = factored compressive resistance parallel to grain, N (see Clause 6.5.5.2.4, assuming Kc = 1.00)  
  Qr = factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, N (see Clause 6.5.6.2)  
  θ  = angle between direction of grain and direction of load, degrees

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 124: 6.5.8 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.8 Tensile resistance parallel to grain
The factored tensile resistance, Tr, parallel to grain shall be calculated as follows:

Tr = φ * Ft * An * KZt  

where  
  φ   = 0.9  
  Ft  = ft * (KD * KH * KSt * KT)  

  where  
    ft = specified strength in tension parallel to grain, MPa (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9)  

  An  = net cross-sectional area, mm² (see Clause 5.3.8)  
  KZt = size factor in tension (see Clause 6.4.5)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 125: 6.5.9 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.9 Resistance to combined bending and axial load
Members subject to combined bending and compressive or tensile axial loads shall be designed to
satisfy the following appropriate interaction equation:

        (Pf / Pr)² + (Mf / Mr) * [1 / (1 - Pf / PE)] ≤ 1  
or  
        (Tf / Tr) + (Mf / Mr) ≤ 1  

where  
  Pf   = factored compressive axial load  
  Pr   = factored compressive load resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 6.5.5)  
  Mf   = factored bending moment  
  Mr   = factored bending moment resistance (see Clause 6.5.3)  
  PE   = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied moment  

         PE = (π² * E05 * KSE * KT * I) / (Le²)  

    where  
      E05 = modulus of elasticity for design of compression members, MPa  
      I   = moment of inertia in the plane of the applied moment, mm⁴  
      Le  = effective length in the plane of the applied moment, mm  
           = Ke * L  
        where  
          Ke = effective-length factor (see Clause A.6.5.5.1)  

  Tf   = factored tensile axial load  
  Tr   = factored tensile load resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 6.5.8)  

Note: See Clause A.6.5.9 for a more detailed interaction formula for combined bending and compressive loads.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 126: 6.5.10.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.1 General
To utilize continuity in the design of decking, the conditions specified in Clauses 6.5.10.2 to 6.5.10.5
shall apply.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 127: 6.5.10.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.2.1 Connection requirements
Material shall be 75 mm or more in width and shall be tongued and grooved or splined. Planks 38 mm
or less in thickness shall be nailed to the supporting members with nails not shorter than twice the
thickness of the plank and not less than 63 mm (2-1/2 in). Planks thicker than 38 mm shall be toe-nailed
to the supporting members with one 127 mm (5 in) toe-nail and face-nailed with one or more nails not
less than 152 mm (6 in) in length. Planks 140 mm or less in width shall be nailed with two nails to each
support. Planks more than 140 mm in width shall be nailed with three nails to each support.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 128: 6.5.10.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.2.2 Butt joints
In bridges, each plank shall extend over at least one support. In roofs and floors, planks not extending
over at least one support in any span may be used if they are
a) double tongue-and-groove planks more than 38 mm in thickness;
b) flanked by planks that rest on both supports of that span; and
c) separated by at least six planks in that span, each of which extends over at least one support.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 129: 6.5.10.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.3.1 Connection requirements
Materials shall be 38 mm or more in thickness, 64 mm or more in width, laid on edge, and spiked
together. Nails used to spike the laminations together shall be at least 4 in long for 38 mm thickness
laminations and 6 in long for 64 mm thickness laminations. Decking 140 mm or less in depth shall be
spiked together with a staggered single row of nails at intervals of not more than 450 mm in the row.
One nail shall be placed not more than 100 mm from the end of each lamination. Decking more than
140 mm in depth shall be spiked together with a staggered double row of nails at intervals of not more
than 450 mm in each row. Two nails shall be placed not more than 100 mm from the end of each
lamination. Each lamination shall be toe-nailed to each support with not less than 4 in nails.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 130: 6.5.10.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.3.2 Butt joints
In bridges, each lamination shall extend over at least one support. In roofs and floors, laminations not
extending over at least one support in any span shall be flanked by laminations that rest on both
supports of that span, and shall be separated by at least six laminations in that span, each of which
extends over at least one support.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 131: 6.5.10.4 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.4 Deflection calculations
For uniform design loads, decking deflections for the laying patterns described in Table 6.18 shall be
calculated using the formulas given in Table 6.18. For other loading conditions or laying patterns,
deflections shall be calculated using recognized engineering formulas.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 132: 6.5.10.5 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.10.5 Bending
Bending moments for plank decking laid in a controlled, random pattern, as described in Table 6.18,
shall be calculated based on simple span moments. For other deck patterns, bending moments shall be
calculated based on recognized engineering formulas.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 133: 6.5.11.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.11.1 General
All lumber and plywood in permanent wood foundations shall be treated with a preservative in
accordance with the CAN/CSA-O80 Series, except where exempted from treatment by CAN/CSA-S406.
The provisions for design of permanent wood foundations are predicated on the use of lumber and
plywood identified by a certification mark on the material that confirms that treatment, where
required, has been carried out by a plant certified under CSA O322.
Note: CSA O322 outlines procedures for the certification of treatment plants and for the identification of wood
materials pressure treated for use in permanent wood foundations. See Clause A.6.5.11 for more details about
wood foundations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 134: 6.5.11.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.11.2 Wall footings
In the design of wall footings for permanent wood foundations, the specified strength in bending
perpendicular to grain for wood footing plates that are wider than the bottom plates shall not exceed
one-third the factored shear resistance. A granular layer, under footings, may be assumed capable of
distributing the load transferred by the footing to the undisturbed soil at an angle of not more than 30°
to the vertical.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 135: 6.5.12 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12 Specific truss applications
Note: See Clause A.6.5.12.
All pieces bear on three supports
2 = 0.771
Deflection*
3 = 0.42
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 136: 6.5.12.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.1 Scope
The design methods specified in Clause 6.5.12 apply only to fully triangulated light-gauge metal-plate-connected
wood roof trusses that meet the following conditions:
a) spacing not to exceed 610 mm;
b) clear span between inside face of supports not to exceed 12.20 m;
c) total truss length between outermost panel points not to exceed 18.0m, with no single cantilever length exceeding 25% of the adjacent clear span; and
d) top chord pitch not less than 2 in 12.

Clause 6.5.12 does not apply to girder, bowstring, semi-circular, or attic trusses (which have
non-triangulated sections), or to flat or floor trusses.
Notes:
1) The provisions of Clause 6.5.12 are predicated on the determination of load effects on members and
connections in accordance with recognized methods of analysis such as those in Truss Plate Institute of
Canada (TPIC).
2) The provisions of Clause 6.5.12 are predicated on truss fabrication and erection in accordance with
recognized practices such as those referenced by TPIC.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 137: 6.5.12.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.2 General
Except as modified in Clauses 6.5.12.3 to 6.5.12.5, truss member design shall be in accordance with the
sawn lumber provisions of Clauses 6.5.1 to 6.5.9. Truss plate design shall be in accordance with
Clause 12.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 138: 6.5.12.3 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.3 Compressive resistance parallel to grain
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 139: 6.5.12.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.3.1 Effective length, Le
Unless otherwise required, the effective length, Le = KeLpa, shall be used in determining the slenderness
ratio for truss compression members, where
Le= effective length of truss compression member
Ke= effective-length factor for truss compression member
Lpa= actual length of member between adjacent panel points

Note: Effective-length factors for compression members and conditions under which these factors apply can be
found in TPIC.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 140: 6.5.12.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.3.2 Chord member with a splice
A compression chord member containing a metal-plate-connected splice may be considered continuous
for a specific load case if the splice is located within ±10% of the panel length from an inflection point.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 141: 6.5.12.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.3.3 Size factor, KZc
The member length, L, used in Clause 6.5.5.2.4 to compute the size factor, KZc, shall be the greater of
the panel length or one-half the chord length between pitch breaks.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 142: 6.5.12.4 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.4 Compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
Factored bearing forces shall not exceed the factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
determined in accordance with Clauses 6.5.6.2 and 6.5.6.3.1.
The requirements of Clause 6.5.6.3.1 may be met by providing bearing reinforcement against the effects
of concentrated bearing loads acting near a support.
Note: Bearing reinforcing details using light-gauge metal plates that conform to Clause 12.8.1 can be found in
TPIC.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 143: 6.5.12.5 
--------------------------------------------------
6.5.12.5 Resistance to combined bending and axial load
Members subject to combined bending and compressive or tensile axial load shall be designed to satisfy
the appropriate interaction equation:
      (Pf / Pr)² + (Mf / (KM * Mr)) ≤ 1.0  
or  
      (Tf / Tr) + (Mf / Mr) ≤ 1.0  

where  
  Pf   = factored compressive axial load  
  Pr   = factored compressive load resistance parallel to grain calculated in accordance with  
         Clauses 6.5.5 and 6.5.12.3  
  Mf   = factored bending moment  
         (unless mid-panel deflection of truss chords is limited to criteria such as are specified in TPIC,  
         moments shall be multiplied by [1 / (1 – Pf / PE)], where PE is defined in Clause 6.5.9)  
  KM   = bending capacity modification factor as defined in Table 6.19  
  Mr   = factored bending moment resistance (see Clause 6.5.3)  
  Tf   = factored tensile axial load  
  Tr   = factored tensile load resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 6.5.8)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 144: 6.6 
--------------------------------------------------
6.6 Serviceability limit states
The design of sawn lumber members for serviceability limit states shall be in accordance with
Clauses 5.1.3 and 5.4.
--------------------------------------------------
7 Glued-laminated timber (glulam)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 145: 7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.1 Scope
The design data and methods specified in Clause 7 apply only to glued-laminated timber manufactured
in accordance with CAN/CSA-O122.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 146: 7.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.2.1 Stress grades
Design in accordance with Clause 7 is based on the use of the stress grades of glued-laminated timber
given in Table 7.1.
Note: Part 4 of the National Building Code of Canada requires that glued-laminated timber be fabricated in plants
conforming to CSA O177. A list of certified manufacturers can be obtained from the certifying agency or agencies
providing certification service.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 147: 7.2.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.2.2.1 General
Except as noted in Clause 7.2.2.2, appearance grades as defined in CAN/CSA-O122 do not affect the
specified strength.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 148: 7.2.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.2.2.2 Textured finishes
Some manufacturers offer a variety of textured finishes. Designers should check the availability of
textured finishes before specifying.
Such finishes can change the finished sizes and tolerances given in CAN/CSA-O122. Depending on the
degree of texturing, the designer might need to compensate for any resulting reduction of cross-section
and/or specified strength of the member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 149: 7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.3 Specified strengths and moduli of elasticity
The specified strengths and moduli of elasticity for glued-laminated timber are given in Table 7.2.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 150: 7.4
--------------------------------------------------
7.4 Modification factors
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 151: 7.4.1
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.1 Load-duration factor, KD  
The specified strength of glued-laminated timber shall be multiplied by a load-duration factor, KD, in accordance with Clause 5.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 152: 7.4.2
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.2 Service-condition factor, KS
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 153: 7.4.2.1
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.2.1 General  
The specified strength and modulus of elasticity of glued-laminated timber shall be multiplied by service-condition factor, KS, in accordance with Table 7.3.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 154: 7.4.2.2
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.2.2 Semi-wet-service conditions  
Where glued-laminated timber members that could be exposed to free moisture are adequately protected, an intermediate value of KS between 1.00 and that listed in Table 7.3 may be used.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 155: 7.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.3.1 General
For preservative-treated, non-incised glued-laminated timber, the treatment factor, KT, may be taken as
unity.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 156: 7.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.3.2 Other treatments
For glued-laminated timber treated with fire-retardant or other potentially strength-reducing chemicals,
strength and stiffness capacities shall be based on documented results of tests that shall take into
account the effects of time, temperature, and moisture content in accordance with Clause 4.3.2. Glued-laminated
members shall not be treated with water-borne chemicals after gluing.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 157: 7.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
7.4.4 System factor, KH
The specified strength for glued-laminated timber members in a system consisting of three or more
essentially parallel members spaced not more than 610 mm apart and so arranged that they mutually
support the applied load may be multiplied by a system factor, KH, equal to 1.00 for tension parallel to
grain, shear strength at locations with compression side notches, and fracture shear strength at a notch,
and 1.10 for all other strength properties.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 158: 7.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.1 Scope
Clause 7.5 provides design information and design formulas for glued-laminated timber members of
rectangular cross-section.
Dry-service
conditions
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 159: 7.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.2 Orientation
The design data for bending members specified in Clause 7.5 apply to horizontally laminated members,
the wide faces of whose laminations are normal to the direction of load.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 160: 7.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.3 Vertically glued-laminated beams
Vertically glued-laminated timber beams, where the narrow faces of laminations are normal to the
direction of load, shall be designed as a built-up system of sawn lumber members of No. 2 grade, in
accordance with Clause 6.4.4.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 161: 7.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.4 Net section
The net section, obtained by deducting from the gross cross-section the area of all material removed by
boring, grooving, dapping, notching, or other means, shall be checked by calculating the resistance of a
member. The net section shall not be less than 75% of the gross section.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 162: 7.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.5 Size
For design purposes, the actual dry size rounded to the nearest millimetre (net dimension) shall be used
for both dry-and wet-service conditions.
Note: Standard sizes rounded to the nearest millimetre are given in Clause A.7.5.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 163: 7.5.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.1 Members of constant cross-section
The factored bending moment resistance of glued-laminated timber members of constant cross-section
shall be determined in accordance with Clause 7.5.6.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 164: 7.5.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.2 Curved and/or double-tapered members
In addition to meeting the requirements of Clause 7.5.6.5, the factored bending moment resistance of
rectangular curved and/or tapered glued-laminated timber members shall not exceed the value
determined in accordance with Clause 7.5.6.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 165: 7.5.6.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.3.1 General
For laterally-unsupported glued-laminated timber bending members, the lateral-stability factor, KL, may
be taken as unity, provided that the maximum depth-to-width ratio of the member does not exceed
2.5:1. If the ratio is greater than 2.5:1, lateral support shall be provided at points of bearing to prevent
lateral displacement and rotation and KL shall be determined in accordance with Clause 7.5.6.4, except
as otherwise permitted in Clause 7.5.6.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 166: 7.5.6.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.3.2 Combined bending and axial loads
In the case of glued-laminated members of rectangular cross-section subjected to combined bending
and axial loads, the provisions of Clause 6.5.3.2.3 may be applied.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 167: 7.5.6.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.3.3 Built-up beams
For built-up beams consisting of two or more individual members of the same depth, the maximum
ratio permitted in Clause 7.5.6.3.1 for laterally-unsupported members may be based on the total width

of the beam, provided that the individual members are fastened together securely at intervals not
exceeding four times the depth.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 168: 7.5.6.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.4.1 Unsupported length, lu
When no additional intermediate support is provided, the unsupported length, lu, shall be the distance
between points of bearing or the length of the cantilever. When intermediate support is provided by
purlins so connected that they prevent lateral displacement of the compressive edge of the bending
member, the unsupported length shall be taken as the maximum purlin spacing, a (see Table 7.4).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 169: 7.5.6.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.4.2 Prevention of lateral displacement
When the compressive edge of the bending member is supported throughout its length to prevent
lateral displacement, the unsupported length may be taken as zero. For decking to provide such
support, it shall be fastened securely to the bending member and adjacent framing to provide a rigid
diaphragm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 170: 7.5.6.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.4.3 Slenderness ratio, CB
The slenderness ratio of a bending member shall not exceed 50 and shall be calculated as follows:
where
CB = √(Le * d / b²)

where  
  Le = effective length, mm (from Table 7.4)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 171: 7.5.6.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.4.4 Calculation of lateral-stability factor, KL
a) When CB does not exceed 10:  
   KL = 1.0

b) When CB is greater than 10 but does not exceed CK:  
   KL = 1 - (1/3) * (CB / CK)⁴  

   where  
     CK = ⁴√(0.97 * E * KSE * KT / Fb)  
     E  = specified modulus of elasticity, MPa (see Table 7.2)  
     Fb = specified strength in bending (see part c)

c) When CB is greater than CK but does not exceed 50:  
   KL = (0.65 * E * KSE * KT) / (CB² * Fb * KX)  

   where  
     Fb = fb * (KD * KH * KSb * KT)  
       where  
         fb = specified strength in bending, MPa (see Table 7.2)  

     KX = curvature factor (see Clause 7.5.6.5.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 172: 7.5.6.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.5.1 General
Except as provided for in Clauses 7.5.6.5.3 and 7.5.6.6, the factored bending moment resistance, Mr, of
glued-laminated timber members shall be taken as the lesser of Mr1 or Mr2 as follows:
M1 = φ * Fb * SKx * KZbg  
M2 = φ * Fb * SKx * KL  

where  
  φ  = 0.9  
  Fb = fb * (KD * KH * KSb * KT)  

  where  
    fb = specified strength in bending, MPa (see Table 7.2)  

  Kx = curvature factor (see Clause 7.5.6.5.2)
    KZbg = (130 / b)^(1/10) * (610 / d)^(1/10) * (9100 / L)^(1/10) * KL ≤ 1.3  
where  
  b  = beam width (for single-piece laminations) or the width of widest piece (for multiple-piece laminations), mm  
  d  = beam depth, mm  
  L  = length of beam segment between points of zero moment, mm  
  KL = lateral-stability factor (see Clause 7.5.6.4)

Note:  
For beams with one or more points of inflection (i.e., multi-span beams and cantilevered beams), the size factor is calculated for each beam segment.  
The moment resistance for each beam segment, as modified by the appropriate size factor, is then compared to the maximum factored moment within that segment.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 173: 7.5.6.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.5.2 Curvature factor, KX
For the curved portion only of glued-laminated timber members, the specified strength in bending shall
be multiplied by the curvature factor, KX, calculated as follows:
KX = 1 - 2000 * (t / R)²

where  
  t = lamination thickness, mm  
  R = radius of curvature of the innermost lamination, mm  

The minimum radius of curvature permitted for a given thickness of lamination shall meet the requirements of CAN/CSA-O122 (see Table A.7).

Note: KX = 1.0 for straight members and the straight portion of curved members.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 174: 7.5.6.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.5.3 Curved double-tapered members
At the apex of curved double-tapered members (pitched cambered beams), the factored bending
moment resistance, Mr, shall be taken as the value obtained from the formula in Clause 7.5.6.5.1
divided by the factor [1 + 2.7 tan], where = the slope of upper surface of member (roof slope) in
degrees.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 175: 7.5.6.6 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.6 Radial resistance
Notes:
1) Radial stresses occur in curved and/or double-tapered glued-laminated members and can limit their factored
bending moment resistance.
2) When the bending moment tends to decrease curvature (increase the radius), the corresponding radial stress
is tension perpendicular to grain. When the bending moment tends to increase curvature (decrease the
radius), the corresponding radial stress is compression perpendicular to grain.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 176: 7.5.6.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.6.1 General
The factored bending moment resistance as governed by tension perpendicular to grain, Mr, shall be
calculated using the following formula, but shall not be greater than the value determined in
accordance with Clauses 7.5.6.5.1 and 7.5.6.5.3. For double-tapered members, the additional
requirement of Clause 7.5.6.6.2 shall also be satisfied.
Mr = φ * Ftp * (2A / 3) * R * KZtp

where  
  φ     = 0.9  
  Ftp   = ftp * (KD * KH * KStp * KT)  

    where  
      ftp = specified strength in tension perpendicular to grain, MPa (see Table 7.2)

  R     = radius of curvature at centreline of member, mm  
  KZtp  = size factor in tension perpendicular to grain (see Table 7.5)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 177: 7.5.6.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.6.2 Double-tapered members
For double-tapered members subjected to radial tension perpendicular to grain, the following additional
requirement shall be satisfied:
Mr = φ * Ftp * S * KZtp * KR  

where  
  φ     = 0.9  
  Ftp   = ftp * (KD * KH * KStp * KT)  

    where  
      ftp = specified strength in tension perpendicular to grain, MPa (see Table 7.2)

  S     = section modulus at apex, mm³  
  KZtp  = size factor in tension perpendicular to grain (see Table 7.5)  
  KR    = radial-stress factor (see Clause 7.5.6.6.3)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 178: 7.5.6.6.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.6.6.3 7.5.6.6.3 Radial-stress factor, KR
The radial-stress factor, KR, shall be calculated as follows:
KR = [A + B * (d / R) + C * (d / R)²]⁻¹

where  
  A, B, C = constants specified in Table 7.6  
  d       = maximum depth at apex, mm  
  R       = radius of curvature at centreline of member, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 179: 7.5.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.1 General
Members without notches shall be checked for shear resistance in accordance with Clause 7.5.7.3.
Members with notches on the compression side shall be checked for shear resistance in accordance
with Clause 7.5.7.4. Members with notches on the tension side shall also be verified for shear resistance
at locations other than end notches in accordance with Clause 7.5.7.5.1 and for fracture shear
resistance at notch in accordance with Clause 7.5.7.5.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 180: 7.5.7.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.2.1 Loads for shear resistance
In Item b) of Clause 7.5.7.3, and in Clauses 7.5.7.4 and 7.5.7.5.1, the effect of loads acting within a
distance from a support equal to the depth of the member may be omitted from consideration.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 181: 7.5.7.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.2.2 Loads for fracture shear resistance at notch
In Clause 7.5.7.3 a) and Clause 7.5.7.5.2, the effect of all loads acting on the member shall be
considered, including the loads acting within a distance from the support equal to the depth of the
member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 182: 7.5.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.3 Shear resistance at locations other than end notches
The factored shear resistance of glued-laminated timber members shall be determined as follows:
a) For beams of any volume, the total factored load,Wf , acting normal to a member shall not exceed
the total factored shear resistance,Wr, calculated as follows:
Wr = Fv 0.48AgCVZ –0.18 Wf
Note: As an alternative for beams less than 2.0 m3 in volume, the factored shear resistance may be calculated
using the equation in Item b).
b) For members other than beams, the factored shear resistance, Vr, shall not be less than the
maximum factored shear force, Vf, and shall be calculated as follows:
Vr = φ * FV * (2Ag / 3)

where  
  φ   = 0.9  
  FV  = fv * (KD * KH * KSv * KT)  

    where  
      fv = specified strength in shear, MPa (see Table 7.2)  

  Ag  = b × d = gross cross-sectional area of member, mm²  
  Cv  = shear load coefficient (see Clause 7.5.7.6)  
  Z   = beam volume, m³

Note: The shear resistance requirements of this Clause are additional to those applicable to notched members (see
Clauses 7.5.7.4 and 7.5.7.5).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 183: 7.5.7.4 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.4 Shear resistance at locations with compression side notches
The factored shear resistance, Vr, shall not be less than the maximum factored shear force, Vf, and shall
be calculated as follows:
a) For ec > (d - dn):  
   Vr = φ * FV * (2Ag / 3)

b) For ec < (d - dn):  
   Vr = φ * FV * (2Ag / 3) * (1 - (dn * ec) / (d * (d - dn)))

where  
  φ   = 0.9  
  FV  = fv * (KD * KH * KSv * KT)  

    where  
      fv = specified strength in shear, MPa (see Table 7.2)

  An  = b * (d - dn) = net cross-sectional area of member, mm² (see Clause 7.5.4)  
  Ag  = b * d = gross cross-sectional area of member, mm²  
  b   = member width, mm  
  d   = member depth, mm  
  dn  = notch depth, mm (shall not exceed 0.25d)  
  ec  = notch length, mm (from inner edge of closest support to farthest edge of notch)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 184: 7.5.7.5 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.5 Shear resistance at locations with tension side end notches
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 185: 7.5.7.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.5.1 Shear resistance of residual member above notch
Tension side notches not exceeding 0.25d may be within a distance ‘d’ from the inner edge of the
closest support to the farthest edge of the notch without a reduction in shear resistance as calculated in
accordance with Clause 7.5.7.3 using the gross cross-sectional area of member, Ag. Members with
tension side notches beyond a distance ‘d’ from the inner edge of the closest support to the farthest
edge of the notch shall be designed using the net section, An, in accordance with Clause 5.3.8.1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 186: 7.5.7.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.5.2 Fracture shear resistance at notch
The factored fracture shear resistance at a notch on the tension side at a support, Fr, shall not be less
than the maximum factored shear force, Vf, and shall be calculated as follows:
Fr = φ * Ff * Ag * KN

where  
  φ   = 0.9  
  Ff  = ff * (KD * KH * KSf * KT)  

    where  
      ff = specified fracture shear strength at a notch, MPa  
         = 2.5 * beff^(-0.2) or 0.9 MPa, whichever is greater  

      beff = effective lamination width (mm)  
           = beam width (for single-piece laminations)  
           = width of widest piece (for multiple-piece laminations)

  Ag  = b × d = gross cross-sectional area, mm²  
  KN  = notch factor
    = [0.006 * d * (1.6 * (1/α - 1) + η² * (1/α³ - 1))]^(1/2)

where  
  d   = member depth (unreduced), mm  
  α   = 1 - (dn / d)  

        where  
          dn = notch depth, mm (see Figure 6.1, shall not exceed 0.25d)

  η   = e / d  

        where  
          e = notch length, mm (see Figure 6.1)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 187: 7.5.7.6 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.7.6 Shear-load coefficient, CV
For any load condition not specified in Tables 7.7 to 7.12, the shear-load coefficient, CV, for simple span,
continuous, or cantilevered beams of constant depth may be determined using the following procedure
(the principle of superposition of loads does not apply):
a) Construct the shear force diagram for the beam. If the beam is under moving concentrated loads,
construct the diagram of the maximum shear forces occurring along the full length of the beam
without regard to sign convention. (Positive and negative maximum shear forces both show
positive.)
b) Divide the total beam length, L, into n segments of variable lengths, la, such that within each
segment there are neither abrupt changes nor changes from negative to positive in the shear force.
c) For each segment determine
i) VA = factored shear force at beginning of segment, N;
ii) VB = factored shear force at end of segment, N; and
iii) VC = factored shear force at centre of segment, N
and calculate the factor G as follows:
G = ℓ₀ * [VAs⁴ + VBs⁴ + 4VCs⁴]

d) Determine the coefficient, Cv, as follows:

i) For stationary loads:  
   Cv = 1.825 * Wf * (L / ΣG)^0.2

   where  
     Wf = the total of all factored loads applied to the beam, N

ii) For moving loads:  
   Cv = 1.825 * Wf * (L / ΣG)^0.2

   where  
     Wf = the total of all factored moving loads and all factored distributed loads applied to the beam, N

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 188: 7.5.8 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8 Compressive resistance parallel to grain
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 189: 7.5.8.1 
--------------------------------------------------
 7.5.8.1 Effective length, Le
Unless otherwise noted in this Standard, the effective length, Le = KeL, shall be used in determining the
slenderness ratio of compression members.
Note: Recommended effective-length factors, Ke, for compression members are given in Table A.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 190: 7.5.8.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.2 Slenderness ratio, CC
The slenderness ratio, CC, of simple compression members of constant rectangular section shall not
exceed 50 and shall be calculated as the greater of
or
Cc = (effective length associated with width) / (member width)  

or  

Cc = (effective length associated with depth) / (member depth)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 191: 7.5.8.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.3 Variable rectangular cross-section
Tapered rectangular compression members shall be designed for an effective width or depth equal to
the minimum width or depth plus 0.45 times the difference between the maximum and minimum
widths or depths. The factored compressive resistance determined in this manner shall not exceed the
factored resistance based on the minimum dimensions in conjunction with a slenderness factor
KC = 1.00.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 192: 7.5.8.4 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.4 Eccentrically applied loads
Bending moments due to eccentrically applied axial loads shall be considered in accordance with
Clause 7.5.12.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 193: 7.5.8.5 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.5 Factored compressive resistance under axial load
The factored compressive resistance parallel to grain, Pr, shall be calculated as follows:
Pr = φ * Fc * A * KZcg * KC

where  
  φ     = 0.8  
  Fc    = fc * (KD * KH * KSc * KT)  

    where  
      fc = specified strength in compression parallel to grain, MPa (see Table 7.2)

  A     = cross-sectional area, mm²  
  KZcg  = 0.68 * Z^(-0.13) ≤ 1.0  

    where  
      Z = member volume, m³

  KC    = slenderness factor (see Clause 7.5.8.6)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 194: 7.5.8.6 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.6 Slenderness factor, KC
The slenderness factor, KC, shall be calculated as follows:

KC = [1.0 + (F * KZcg * Cc³) / (35 * E05 * KSE * KT)]⁻¹

where  
  E05 = 0.87 * E  

    where  
      E = specified modulus of elasticity, MPa (see Table 7.2)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 195: 7.5.8.7 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.7 Spaced compression members
Spaced compression members shall be designed using the specified strengths and modification factors
appropriate for glued-laminated timber.
Note: Spaced compression members may be designed in accordance with the provisions of Clause A.6.5.5.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 196: 7.5.8.8 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.8.8 Built-up compression members
Built-up compression members shall be designed in accordance with Clause 6.5.5.4 using the specified
strengths and modification factors appropriate for glued-laminated timber.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 197: 7.5.9 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9 Compressive resistance perpendicular to grain (bearing)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 198: 7.5.9.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9.1 General
Factored bearing forces shall not exceed the factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
determined in accordance with Clauses 7.5.9.2 and 7.5.9.3.
Note: See Figure 6.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 199: 7.5.9.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9.2 7.5.9.2 Effect of all applied loads
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Qr, under the effect of all applied loads
shall be calculated as follows:
Qr = φ * FCp * Ab * KB * KZcp

where  
  φ    = 0.8  
  FCp  = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  

    where  
      fcp = specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain, MPa (see Table 7.2)

  Ab   = bearing area, mm²  
  KB   = length-of-bearing factor (see Clause 6.5.6.5)  
  KZcp = size factor for bearing, where the depth is the thickness of lamination  
         (see Clause 6.5.6.4)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 200: 7.5.9.3 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9.3 Effect of loads applied near a support
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 201: 7.5.9.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9.3.1 Factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Q’
Q’r = (2/3) φ Fcp A’b KB KZcp
φ    = 0.8  
FCp  = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  

  where  
    fcp = f-E grade value from Table 7.2 for compression face bearing strength, MPa  
Ab'   = average bearing area, mm² (see Clause 7.5.9.3.2)

Note: See Figure 6.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 202: 7.5.9.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.9.3.2 Unequal bearing areas on opposite surfaces of a member
Where unequal bearing areas are used on opposite surfaces (top and bottom) of a member, the average
bearing area, A’b, shall be calculated as follows:
Ab' = b * ((Lb1 + Lb2) / 2) ≤ 1.5 * b * (Lb1)

where  
  b    = average bearing width (perpendicular to grain), mm  
  Lb1  = lesser bearing length, mm  
  Lb2  = larger bearing length, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 203: 7.5.10 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.10 Compressive resistance at an angle to grain
The factored compressive resistance at an angle to grain shall be calculated in accordance with
Clause 6.5.7 using the appropriate specified strengths and modification factors for glued-laminated
timber.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 204: 7.5.11 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.11 Tensile resistance parallel to grain
The factored tensile resistance parallel to grain, Tr, shall not be less than the maximum factored tensile
force, Tf, and shall be calculated as the lesser of
Tr = φ * Ftn * An  
or  
Tr = φ * Ftg * Ag  

where  
  φ    = 0.9  

  Ftn  = ftn * (KD * KH * KSt * KT)  
    where  
      ftn = specified strength in tension parallel to grain at net section, MPa (see Table 7.2)  
  An   = net cross-sectional area, mm²  

  Ftg  = ftg * (KD * KH * KSt * KT)  
    where  
      ftg = specified strength in tension parallel to grain at gross section, MPa (see Table 7.2)  
  Ag   = gross cross-sectional area, mm²

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 205: 7.5.12 
--------------------------------------------------
7.5.12 Resistance to combined bending and axial load
Members subject to combined bending and compressive or tensile axial loads shall be designed to
satisfy the appropriate interaction equation:

(Pf / Pr)² + (Mf / Mr) * [1 / (1 - Pf / PE)] ≤ 1  
or  
(Tf / Tr) + (Mf / Mr) ≤ 1  

where  
  Pf   = factored compressive axial load  
  Pr   = factored compressive load resistance parallel to grain calculated in accordance with  
         Clause 7.5.8.5 using Fcb = fcb * (KD * KH * KSc * KT)  
  Mf   = factored bending moment  
  Mr   = factored bending moment resistance (see Clause 7.5.6.5.1)  
  Tf   = factored tensile axial load  
  Tr   = factored tensile load resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 7.5.11)  
  PE   = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied moment  

         PE = (π² * E05 * KSE * KT * I) / (Le²)

  where  
    E05 = modulus of elasticity for design of compression members  
        = 0.87 * E (MPa)  
        where  
          E = specified modulus of elasticity, MPa  

    I   = moment of inertia in the plane of the applied moment, mm⁴  
    Le  = effective length in the plane of the applied moment  
        = Ke * L  
        where  
          Ke = effective-length factor (see Clause A.6.5.5.1)

Note: See Clause A.6.5.9 for a more detailed interaction formula for combined bending and compressive loads.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 206: 7.6 
--------------------------------------------------
7.6 Serviceability limit states
The design of glued-laminated timber lumber members for serviceability limit states shall be in
accordance with Clauses 5.1.3 and 5.4.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 207: 8.1 Cross-laminated timber (CLT)
--------------------------------------------------
8.1 Scope
The design data and methods specified in Clause 8 apply only to panels of the primary and custom CLT
grades, in layups as defined in Clause 8.2, manufactured and certified in accordance with ANSI/APA PRG
320. Panels with alternative CLT layups shall be designed in accordance with Clause 4.3.2.
Note: The provisions contained within Clause 8 are intended for use of CLT in compression and flatwise bending
applications.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 208: 8.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.2.1 General
Design of CLT panels in accordance with this Standard is based on the use of the primary and custom
CLT grades and layups approved by the certification organization.
Note: Designers should check the availability of CLT grades and layups before specifying. A list of certified
manufacturers can be obtained from the certification organization.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 209: 8.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.2.2 CLT layups
In this Standard, the CLT layup shall be a balanced combination of orthogonal layers where all
laminations oriented in the same direction are made of sawn lumber of the same grade and species
combination.
Note: CLT panels may be designed with adjacent layers oriented in the same direction using the section properties
provided by the product manufacturer (see Clause 8.4.3.2).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 210: 8.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.2.3 Primary CLT grades
The primary CLT grades shall be as specified in Table 8.1. Custom CLT grades shall be specified by the
product manufacturer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 211: 8.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
8.2.4 Specified strengths and moduli of elasticity of laminations
Specified strength values and moduli of elasticity for the laminations in longitudinal and transverse
layers of the primary CLT grades are given in Table 8.2. Those properties for custom CLT grades shall be
as published by the product manufacturer.

Clause 212: 8.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
8.2.5 Appearance grades  
Appearance grades as defined in ANSI/APA PRG 320 do not affect the structural performance of CLT panels.

Clause 213: 8.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.3.1 Load-duration factor, KD
The specified strength of CLT shall be multiplied by a load-duration factor, KD, in accordance with
Clause 5.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 214: 8.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.3.2 Service-condition factors, KS
CLT shall only be used in dry-service conditions for all service-condition factors, KS = 1.0.
Note: CLT structures may be used in wet-service conditions only if specifically permitted by the manufacturer based
on documented test data in accordance with Clause 4.3.2 and if approved by the certification organization.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 215: 8.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.3.3 Treatment factor, KT
For CLT treated with fire-retardant or other potentially strength-reducing chemicals, strength and
stiffness shall be based on documented results of tests that shall take into account the effects of time,
temperature, and moisture content in accordance with Clause 5.3.4; otherwise, KT shall be equal to 1.0.
CLT shall not be treated with water-borne preservatives after gluing.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 216: 8.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
8.3.4 System factor, KH
KH shall be equal to 1.0 for all strength properties of CLT.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 217: 8.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.1 Scope
Clause 8.4 provides design formulas and information for CLT panels of constant width. Factored
resistances of CLT panels shall be calculated in accordance with Clause 8.4 using the specified strengths
and moduli of elasticity of laminations (see Clause 8.2.4), modification factors (see Clause 8.3), and
section properties determined in accordance with Clause 8.4.3.2 or as provided by the product
manufacturer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 218: 8.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.2 Sizes
For design purposes, the actual dry sizes of the panel rounded to the nearest millimetre (net dimension)
shall be used. Depending on the layup, the actual sizes and tolerances of CLT panels may deviate from
those specified in ANSI/APA PRG 320 and shall be accounted for in calculations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 219: 8.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.3 Flatwise bending moment resistance
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 220: 8.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.3.1 General
The factored flatwise bending moment resistance, Mr,f, of a CLT panels shall be calculated as follows:
a) in the major strength direction [see Figure 8.2 a)]:
Mr,f,0 = φ * Fb * Seff,0 * Krb,0

Seff,f,0 = ((EI)eff,f,0 / E) * (2 / h)

where  
  (EI)eff,f,0 = effective flatwise bending stiffness of the panel in the major strength direction, N•mm² (see Clause 8.4.3.2)  
  E           = specified modulus of elasticity of laminations in the longitudinal layers, MPa (see Clause 8.2.4 and Figure 8.2 a))  
  h           = thickness of the panel, mm (see Figure 8.2 a))  

Krb,0 = 0.85


b) In the minor strength direction [see Figure 8.2 b)]:

Mr,f,90 = φ * Fb * Seff,f,90 * Krb,90  

where  
  φ  = 0.9  
  Fb = fb * (KD * KH * KSb * KT)  

    where  
      fb = specified bending strength of laminations in the transverse layers, MPa (see Clause 8.2.4)  

Seff,f,90 = ((EI)eff,f,90 / E) * (2 / h90)

where  
  (EI)eff,f,90 = effective flatwise bending stiffness of the panel in the minor strength direction, N•mm² (see Clause 8.4.3.2)  
  E            = specified modulus of elasticity of laminations in the transverse layers, MPa (see Clause 8.2.4 and Figure 8.2 b))  
  h90          = thickness of the panel without the outer longitudinal layers, mm (see Figure 8.2 b))  

Krb,90 = 1.0
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 221: 8.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.3.2 Effective stiffness in flatwise bending
Formulas given in this Clause shall apply to the section properties of CLT panels with alternating
orthogonal layers only. The section properties of CLT panels with adjacent layers oriented in the same
direction shall be provided by the product manufacturer.
Effective flatwise bending stiffness, (EI)eff,f, and effective shear stiffness in flatwise bending , (GA)eff,f, of
a CLT panel with alternating orthogonal layers shall be calculated as follows:
a) In the major strength direction [see Figure 8.2 a)]:

(EI)eff,f,0 = Σ (Ei * b0 * ti³ / 12) + Σ (Ei * b0 * ti * zi²)
             i=1 to n             i=1 to n

(GA)eff,f,0 = ((h - t1/2 - tn/2)²) / [ (t1 / (2 * G1 * b0)) + Σ (ti / (Gi * b0)) + (tn / (2 * Gn * b0)) ]
                                       i=2 to n-1


b) In the minor strength direction [see Figure 8.2 b)]:

(EI)eff,f,90 = Σ (Ei * b90 * ti³ / 12) + Σ (Ei * b90 * ti * zi²)
               i=2 to n-1             i=2 to n-1

(GA)eff,f,90 = ((h - t1/2 - tn/2)²) / [ (t1 / (2 * G1 * b90)) + Σ (ti / (Gi * b90)) + (tn / (2 * Gn * b90)) ]
                                          i=2 to n-1


Definitions:

n    = number of layers in the panel  
Ei   = modulus of elasticity of laminations in the ith layer, MPa  
     = E  for laminations in longitudinal layers  
     = E⊥ for laminations in transverse layers  

b0   = width of the panel measured perpendicular to the major strength direction (Figure 8.2 a))  
b90  = width of the panel measured perpendicular to the minor strength direction (Figure 8.2 b))  

ti   = thickness of laminations in the ith layer, mm  
zi   = distance between the centre point of the ith layer and the neutral axis (Figure 8.2 a))  

h    = thickness of the panel, mm (Figure 8.2 a or b)  

Gi   = shear modulus of laminations in the ith layer, MPa  
     = G  for laminations in longitudinal layers  
     = G⊥ for laminations in transverse layers


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 222: 8.4.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.4.1 Loads near supports
In Clause 8.4.4.2, the effect of loads acting within a distance from a support equal to the thickness of
the panel may be omitted from consideration.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 223: 8.4.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.4.2 Factored flatwise shear resistance
The factored flatwise shear resistance, Vr,f, of a CLT panel shall be calculated as follows:
a) in the major strength direction:
Vr,f,0 = φ * Fs * (2Ag,0 / 3)

where  
  φ   = 0.9  
  Fs  = fs * (KD * KH * KSv * KT)  

    where  
      fs = specified strength in rolling shear of laminations in the transverse layers, MPa  
           (see Clause 8.2.4)
    Ag,0 = gross cross-sectional area of the panel measured perpendicular to the major strength direction, mm²  
       = b0 * h  
       [see Figure 8.2 a)]

b) In the minor strength direction:

Vr,f,90 = φ * Fs * (2Ag,90 / 3)

where  
  φ     = 0.9  
  Fs    = fs * (KD * KH * KSv * KT)  

    where  
      fs = specified strength in rolling shear of laminations in the longitudinal layers, MPa  
           (see Clause 8.2.4)

  Ag,90 = gross cross-sectional area of the panel measured perpendicular to the minor strength direction, mm²,  
          excluding the outermost longitudinal layers [see Figure 8.2 b)]  
        = b90 * h90

Note: For a CLT panel with multiple longitudinal outermost layers, all these layers are excluded from the gross cross-sectional area, Ag,90.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 224: 8.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5 Compressive resistance under axial load
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 225: 8.4.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5.1 General
Only the layers with laminations oriented parallel to the applied axial load shall be assumed to carry
that load.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 226: 8.4.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5.2 Effective length, Le
The effective length, Le = Ke L, shall be used in determining the slenderness ratio of CLT panels.
Recommended effective-length factors, Ke, for compression members are given in Table A.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 227: 8.4.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5.3 Slenderness ratio, CC
The slenderness ratio, CC , of CLT panels of constant rectangular cross-section shall not exceed 43
(i.e., Le/reff 150) and shall be calculated as follows:
Cc = Le / √(12 * reff)

where  
  reff = √(Ieff / Aeff)

    where  
      Ieff  = effective out-of-plane moment of inertia of the panel, accounting only for the layers with  
              laminations oriented parallel to the applied axial load, mm⁴  
      Aeff  = effective cross-sectional area of the panel, accounting only for the layers with  
              laminations oriented parallel to the applied axial load, mm²

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 228: 8.4.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5.4 Eccentrically applied loads
Bending moments due to eccentrically applied axial loads shall be considered in accordance with
Clause 8.4.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 229: 8.4.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.5.5 Factored compressive resistance under axial load
The factored compressive resistance of CLT panels under axial load shall be calculated as follows:
Pr = φ * Fc * Aeff * KZc * KC

where  
  φ   = 0.8  
  Fc  = fc * (KD * KH * KSc * KT)  

    where  
      fc = specified strength in compression parallel to grain of the laminations  
           oriented parallel to the axial load, MPa (see Clause 8.2.4)

  KZc = 6.3 * (√(12 * reff) / L)^(-0.13) ≤ 1.3  

    where  
      L = height of the panel, mm  

  KC  = [1.0 + (Fc * KZc * Cc³) / (35 * E05 * KSE * KT)]^(-1)

    where  
      E05 = modulus of elasticity for design of compression members, only for the laminations  
            oriented parallel to the applied axial load, MPa (see Clause 8.2.4)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 230: 8.4.6 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.6 Resistance to combined bending and axial compressive load
CLT panels subject to combined flatwise bending and compressive axial load shall be designed to satisfy
the interaction equation:
(Pf / Pr) + (Mf / Mr,f) * [1 / (1 - (Pf / PE,v))] ≤ 1  

where  
  Pf     = factored compressive axial load  
  Pr     = factored compressive resistance under axial load (see Clause 8.4.5.5)  
  Mf     = factored bending moment  
  Mr,f   = factored flatwise bending moment resistance (see Clause 8.4.3)  
  PE,v   = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied bending moment, adjusted for shear deformation  

          PE,v = PE / [1 + (π² / (GA)eff,f)]

    where  
      PE         = Euler buckling load (see Clause 7.5.12)  
                   using E05 and Ieff for layers oriented parallel to the axial load  
                   (see Clauses 8.2.4 and 8.4.5.3)  

      (GA)eff,f  = effective shear stiffness in flatwise bending accounting for all layers, N  
                   (see Clause 8.4.3.2)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 231: 8.4.7 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7 Compressive resistance perpendicular to the face of the panel (bearing)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 232: 8.4.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7.1 General
Factored bearing forces shall not exceed the factored compressive resistance of CLT panels
perpendicular to grain as determined in accordance with Clauses 8.4.7.2 and 8.4.7.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 233: 8.4.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7.2 Effect of all applied loads
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Qr, of CLT panels under the effect of all
applied loads shall be calculated as follows:
Qr' = (2/3) * φ * FCp * Ab' * KB * KZcp

where  
  φ     = 0.8  
  FCp   = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  

    where  
      fcp = specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain of laminations  
            in the outer layers (see Clause 8.2.4), MPa  

  Ab'   = average bearing area, mm² (see Clause 8.4.7.3.2)  
  KB    = length-of-bearing factor  
  KZcp  = size factor for bearing

Note: See Figure 6.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 234: 8.4.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7.3 8.4.7.3 Effect of loads applied near a support
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 235: 8.4.7.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7.3.1 Factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Qr
Qr' = (2/3) * φ * FCp * Ab' * KB * KZcp

where  
  φ     = 0.8  
  FCp   = fcp * (KD * KScp * KT)  

    where  
      fcp = specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain of laminations in the outer layers  
            (see Clause 8.2.4), MPa  

  Ab'   = average bearing area, mm² (see Clause 8.4.7.3.2)

Note: See Figure 6.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 236: 8.4.7.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.7.3.2 Unequal bearing areas on opposite surfaces of a panel
In cases where unequal bearing areas are used on opposite surfaces (top and bottom) of a panel, the
average bearing area, Ab, shall be calculated as follows:
Ab' = b * ((Lb1 + Lb2) / 2) ≤ 1.5 * b * (Lb1)

where  
  b = average bearing width, mm
Lb1 = lesser bearing length, mm
Lb2 = larger bearing length, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 237: 8.4.8 
--------------------------------------------------
8.4.8 Compressive resistance at an angle to the face of a panel
The factored compressive resistance at an angle to the face of CLT panel shall be calculated in
accordance with Clause 6.5.7 using the factored resistance values calculated in Clause 8.4.5 with
KZc = KC = 1.0 and Clause 8.4.7.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 238: 8.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
8.5.1 General
The design of CLT panels for serviceability limit states shall be in accordance with Clauses 5.1.3 and 5.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 239: 8.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
8.5.2 Deflection of CLT panels
The maximum deflection under a specified load acting perpendicular to the plane of the panel shall be
calculated as a sum of the deflections due to moment and shear using the effective flatwise bending
stiffness (EI)eff,f, and the effective shear stiffness in flatwise bending, (GA)eff,f, as defined in
Clause 8.4.3.2, with consideration for creep effects.
Note: A method for calculating deflection under static uniform or concentrated load is provided in Clause A.8.5.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 240: 8.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
8.5.3 Vibration performance of CLT floors
A method for calculating vibration-controlled spans for CLT floors is provided in Clause A.8.5.3.
9 Structural panels
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 241: 9.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.1 Scope
The design data, methods, and construction requirements specified in Clause 9 apply to the materials
specified in Clause 9.2.
Design methods and construction requirements for glued building components manufactured using
structural panels are provided in Clause 10.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 242: 9.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.2.1 Plywood
Clauses 9.3 to 9.5 apply to standard constructions of regular grades of unsanded
a) Douglas fir plywood manufactured and identified in accordance with CSA O121; and
b) Canadian softwood plywood manufactured and identified in accordance with CSA O151.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 243: 9.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.2.2 OSB
Clauses 9.3 to 9.5 also apply to OSB panels that are qualified and identified in accordance with
CSA O325, which pertains to wood-based panel products designed and manufactured for protected
construction uses such as roof sheathing, wall sheathing, and floor sheathing in light frame construction
applications. For applications where OSB is primary load-bearing element, other tests and criteria shall
be considered.
Note: Construction sheathing OSB is distinguished from other mat-formed panels by a mark showing the direction
of face alignment. See Clause A.9.2.2 for additional information.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 244: 9.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
9.2.3 Adhesives for stress joints
Adhesives for stress joints for structural panels shall meet the requirements of CSA O112.7.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 245: 9.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.3.1 Plywood
The specified capacities for minimum veneer layup for each plywood thickness are given for Douglas fir
plywood in Table 9.1 and for Canadian softwood plywood in Table 9.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 246: 9.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.3.2 OSB
The specified capacities for construction sheathing OSB conforming to CSA O325 are given in Table 9.3.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 247: 9.4 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4 Modification factors
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 248: 9.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.1 Load-duration factor,Kd
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 249: 9.4.1.
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.1.1 General  
Except as specified in Clause 9.4.1.2, the specified strength capacity values for structural panels shall be multiplied by a load-duration factor, KD, as specified in Table 5.1.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 250: 9.4.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.1.2 Long-term loads
For OSB used in structures subject to long-term loads greater than 50% of design capacity that are
protected from direct exposure to moisture but exposed to intermittent high temperature and/or
humidity conditions, the load-duration factor shall be 0.45.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 251: 9.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.2 Service-condition factor, KS
The specified strength capacity values for structural panels shall be multiplied by a service-condition
factor, KS, as specified in Table 9.4.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 252: 9.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.3 Treatment factor, KT
For preservative-treated plywood, the treatment factor, KT, shall be equal to 1.0. For other preservative-treated
structural panels and structural panels treated with fire-retardant or other potentially strength-reducing
chemicals, strength and stiffness capacities shall be based on the documented results of tests
considering the effects of time, temperature, and moisture content in accordance with Clause 4.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 253: 9.4.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.4.1 Scarf joints
Where scarf joints transmit forces from one panel to another, the specified strength capacity shall be
multiplied by a stress-joint factor, XJ, as specified in Table 9.5. Construction requirements for scarf joints
are given in Clause 10.3.3.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 254: 9.4.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.4.2 Butt joints
Where structural panels are used as glued splice plates in butt joints to transmit forces from one panel
to another or from one lumber piece to another, the specified strength of splice plates shall be
multiplied by a stress-joint factor, XJ, as specified in Table 9.6. Construction requirements for butt joints
are given in Clause 10.3.4.

Clause 255: 9.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
9.4.5 End-use factor, KF, for permanent wood foundations
For plywood in permanent wood foundations supported at intervals not exceeding 815 mm, the end-use
factor for panel bending and planar shear, KF, shall be 1.15. For all other properties, KF shall be 1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 256: 9.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.1 Stress orientation
Structural panels are orthotropic materials. The specified strength capacities used in calculations shall
be those for the orientation of the major axis of the panel intended in the design.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 257: 9.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.2 Flatwise bending
The factored flatwise bending moment resistance, Mr, of a structural panel shall be calculated as
follows:
Mr = φ * Mp * bp

where  
  φ    = 0.95  
  Mp   = mp * (KD * KS * KT * KF) for plywood  
       = mp * (KD * KS * KT) for OSB  

    where  
      mp = specified strength capacity in bending, N•mm/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood, Table 9.3 for OSB)

  bp   = width of panel, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 258: 9.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.3 Edgewise bending
The factored edgewise bending moment resistance, Mr, of a structural panel that is adequately braced
to prevent lateral buckling shall be calculated as follows:
Mr = φ * Tp * (dp² / 6)

where  
  φ    = 0.95  
  Tp   = tp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      tp = specified strength capacity in tension, N/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)

  dp   = depth of panel in plane of bending, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 259: 9.5.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.4.1 Planar shear due to bending
The factored resistance in planar shear, Vrp, for structural panels subjected to bending shall be
calculated as follows:
Vrp = φ * Vpsb * bp

Vpsb = vpsb * (KD * KS * KT * KF) for plywood  
     = vpsb * (KD * KS * KT) for OSB  

where  
  vpsb = specified strength capacity in planar shear (due to bending), N/mm  
         (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 260: 9.5.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.4.2 Planar shear in structural panel splice or gusset plate
The factored resistance in planar shear, Vrp, developed by a glued structural panel splice or gusset plate,
or by the splice plates at a structural panel butt joint, shall be calculated as follows:
Vrp = φ * Vpf * Ac

where  
  φ   = 0.95  
  Vpf = vpf * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      vpf = specified strength capacity in planar shear (due to in-plane forces), MPa  
            (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)  

  Ac  = contact area of splice or gusset plate on one side of joint, mm²

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 261: 9.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.5 9.5.5 Shear-through-thickness of structural panel
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 262: 9.5.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.5.1 9.5.5.1 Shear due to edgewise bending of structural panel
The factored resistance in shear, Vr, through the thickness of a structural panel due to edgewise bending
shall be calculated as follows:
Vr = φ * Vp * (2dp / 3)

where  
  φ  = 0.95  
  Vp = vp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      vp = specified strength capacity in shear-through-thickness, N/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 263: 9.5.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.5.2 9.5.5.2 Shear-through-thickness in structural panel splice or gusset plate
The factored shear-through-thickness resistance, Vr, developed by a structural panel splice or gusset
plate shall be calculated as follows:
Vr = φ * Vp * LG

where  
  φ  = 0.95  
  Vp = vp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      vp = specified strength capacity in shear-through-thickness, N/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)  

  LG = length of splice or gusset plate subjected to shear, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 264: 9.5.6 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.6 Compression parallel to panel edge
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, parallel to a laterally supported panel edge shall be calculated
as follows:
Pr = φ * Pp * bp

where  
  φ  = 0.95  
  Pp = pp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      pp = specified strength capacity in axial compression, N/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 265: 9.5.7 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.7 Tension parallel to panel edge
The factored tensile resistance, Tr, parallel to a panel edge shall be calculated as follows:
Tr = φ * Tp * bn

where  
  φ  = 0.95 for all plywood thicknesses and numbers of plies except 3- and 4-ply layups stressed perpendicular to face grain  
     = 0.60 for 3- and 4-ply plywood layups stressed perpendicular to face grain  
     = 0.95 for OSB  

  Tp = tp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      tp = specified strength capacity in axial tension, N/mm  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)

  bn = net width of panel after cutting of holes, etc., mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 266: 9.5.8 
--------------------------------------------------
9.5.8 9.5.8 Compressive resistance perpendicular to face (bearing)
The factored bearing resistance, Qr, normal to the plane of panel shall be calculated as follows:
Qr = φ * Qp * Ab

where  
  φ  = 0.95  
  Qp = qp * (KD * KS * KT)  

    where  
      qp = specified strength capacity in bearing normal to plane of panel, MPa  
           (see Tables 9.1 and 9.2 for plywood and Table 9.3 for OSB)  

  Ab = bearing area, mm²

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 267: 10.1 10 Composite building components
--------------------------------------------------
10.1 Scope
Design data, methods, and construction requirements specified in Clause 10 apply to glued composite
building components using plywood, OSB, and lumber or glued-laminated timber specified in this
Standard. The design requirements of Clause 10 apply if the glue joints are made in strict compliance

with the requirements of the manufacturer of the adhesive used in fabricating the composite building
components.
Note: Clause 10 does not apply to proprietary structural wood products.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 268: 10.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.2.1 General
Clauses 10.3 to 10.6 apply to the materials specified in Clause 6 for lumber, Clause 7 for
glued-laminated timber, Clause 9 for plywood and OSB, and Clause 10.2.2 for adhesives.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 269: 10.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.2.2 Adhesives for structural components
Adhesives for the assembly of structural components shall meet the requirements of CSA O112.7,
CSA O112.9, or CSA O112.10.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 270: 10.3 
--------------------------------------------------
