10.3 Construction requirements for stress joints
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 271: 10.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.1 Types of stress joints
Joints transmitting forces from one panel to another may be either scarf joints or butt joints.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 272: 10.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.2 Adhesives for stress joints
Adhesives for the assembly of stress joints shall meet the requirements of Clause 10.2.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 273: 10.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.3.1 Scarf joints in shear
The slope of plywood scarf joints shall not be steeper than 1:8. The slope of OSB scarf joints shall not be
steeper than 1:4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 274: 10.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.3.2 Scarf joints in tension, compression, or bending
The slope of plywood scarf joints shall not be steeper than 1:5. The slope of OSB scarf joints shall not be
steeper than 1:4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 275: 10.3.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.4.1 Splice plates for butt joints
Butt joints shall be backed on one or both sides of the panel by a panel splice plate of a type and grade
at least equal to the panel being spliced. The splice plate shall be centred on the joints and glued to
both panels meeting at the joint. The splice plate shall be oriented with its major axis perpendicular to
the joint.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 276: 10.3.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.4.2 Splice plate thickness
Splice plates shall have a minimum thickness equal to that of the panel being spliced.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 277: 10.3.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.4.3 Butt joints in shear
Splice plates stressed in shear shall have a length in the direction perpendicular to the joint equal to
12 times the thickness of the butt-jointed panel and shall have a width equal to the full depth or width
of the panel between framing members.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 278: 10.3.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.4.4 Butt joints in tension
Splice plates stressed in tension shall have a minimum length as specified in Table 9.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 279: 10.3.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
10.3.4.5 Butt joints in compression
Splice plates stressed in compression may have a length as specified in Table 9.6. For plywood joints, if
shorter lengths are used, the strength of the joint shall be reduced as specified in Clause 10.4.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 280: 10.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.4.1 Joint requirements
The stress-joint factors, XJ, specified in Clauses 10.4.2 and 10.4.3 apply to glued plywood and OSB stress
joints fabricated in accordance with Clause 10.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 281: 10.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.4.2 Scarf joints
The stress-joint factor for scarf joints across the major axis of plywood or OSB stressed in tension,
compression, or shear-through-thickness shall be as specified in Table 9.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 282: 10.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.4.3.1 General
For the length of splice plates perpendicular to the joint, the stress-joint factors for butt joints across
the major axis of plywood or OSB stressed in tension, compression, or shear-through-thickness shall be
as specified in Table 9.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 283: 10.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.4.3.2 Butt joints with short plywood plates in compression
For plywood butt joints with splice plates shorter than the minimum length specified in Table 9.6, the
stress-joint factor for compression shall be reduced in direct proportion to such reduction in length.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 284: 10.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.1 General
A panel-web beam shall have one or more plywood or OSB webs glued or nailed at upper and lower
edges to sawn lumber or glued-laminated timber flanges, with lumber stiffeners at intervals along the
web to prevent buckling (see Figure 10.1).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 285: 10.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.2 Effective stiffness
The effective stiffness, (EI)e, of a panel-web beam shall be calculated as follows:
(EI)fc = (ΣBo * KS * ((c1² + c2²)/3)) + (EI)f * KSE

where  
  (ΣBo) = sum of axial stiffness of panel webs, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
  KS    = service-condition factor for web material (see Table 9.4)  
  (EI)f = stiffness of flanges with respect to neutral axis of composite section, N•mm²  
  KSE   = service-condition factor for modulus of elasticity of flange  
          (see Table 6.10 for sawn lumber and Table 7.3 for glulam)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 286: 10.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.3 Bending moment resistance
The factored bending moment resistance, Mr, of a panel-web beam shall be the lesser of the factored
resistance of the tension or compression flanges, calculated as follows:
a) compression flange:
Mr = φ * Fc * Kzc * (EI)e / (EKSE * cc)

where  
  φ = 0.8 for sawn lumber  
    = 0.9 for glued-laminated timber

    Fc = fc * (KD * KSC * KT * KH)

  where  
    fc  = specified strength of flange in compression, MPa  
          (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
    KH  = system factor (see Clause 6.4.4 for sawn lumber and Clause 7.4.4 for glulam)  
    KZC = size factor for compression for sawn lumber (see Clause 6.5.5.2.4)  
    E   = modulus of elasticity of flange, MPa  
          (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
    KSE = service-condition factor for modulus of elasticity of flange  
          (see Table 6.10 for sawn lumber and Table 7.3 for glulam)  
    cc  = distance from neutral axis to compression face (see Figure 10.1)

b) Tension flange:

Mr = φ * Ft * Kzt * (EI)e / (EKSE * ct)

  where  
    φ   = 0.9  
    Ft  = ft * (KD * KST * KT * KH)  

      where  
        ft = specified strength of flange in tension, MPa  
             (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
        Kzt = size factor for tension for sawn lumber (see Table 6.13)  
        E   = modulus of elasticity of flange, MPa  
              (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
        ct  = distance from neutral axis to tension face (see Figure 10.1)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 287: 10.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.4 Web shear-through-thickness
The factored shear resistance, Vr, of the web of a panel-web beam at its neutral axis shall be calculated
as follows:
Vr = φ * Vp * XJ * (EI)e / (EKSE * Qf + 0.5 * (ΣBo) * KSC * cw²)

where  
  φ    = 0.95  
  Vp   = (Σvp) * (KD * KS * KT)

    where  
      Σvp = sum of specified strengths of all panel webs in shear-through-thickness, N/mm  
            (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  

  XJ   = stress-joint factor (see Clause 10.4)  
  E    = modulus of elasticity of flange, MPa  
         (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
  Qf   = moment of area of flange about neutral axis, mm³  
  ΣBo  = sum of specified axial stiffness for all panel webs, N/mm  
         (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
  cw   = greatest distance from neutral axis to outer edge of web, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 288: 10.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.5 Flange-web shear
The factored shear resistance, Vrp, of the glued area between the flange and web of a panel-web beam
shall be the lesser of the shear capacities of the web or flange components, calculated as follows:
Vp = φ * Vg * (Σbg * Xv) * (EI)e / (EKSE * Qf)

where  
  Σbg = sum of contact widths between flange and web  
  E   = modulus of elasticity of flange, MPa (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
  Qf  = moment of area of flange about neutral axis, mm³

a) for web:  
  φ   = 0.95  
  Vg  = Vpf (KD * KS * KT)  
    where  
      Vpf = specified strength in planar shear, MPa (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
  Xv  = shear-modification factor (see Figure 10.2)

b) for flange:  
  φ   = 0.9  
  Vg  = fv (KD * KSV * KT)  
    where  
      fv = specified strength in shear, MPa (see Clauses 6.3.1 and 6.3.2 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)  
  Xv  = 2.00

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 289: 10.5.6 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.6 Deflection calculation
Deflection shall be calculated as the sum of the deflections due to moment, using the effective stiffness,
(EI)e, determined in accordance with Clause 10.5.2, and due to shear, s, calculated as follows:
Δs = (Ba * Mh² * Xs) / (Bv * (EI)e)

where  
  Ba = specified axial stiffness of the web, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
  M  = maximum bending moment due to specified loads, N•mm  
  h  = height of web beam, mm (see Figure 10.1)  
  Xs = section-shear coefficient (see Figure 10.3)  
  Bv = specified shear-through-thickness rigidity of the web, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 290: 10.5.7 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.7 Lateral stability of panel-web beams
Lateral stability of a panel-web beam shall be determined by considering the flange as a column that
tends to deflect sideways between points of support or by application of one of the following rules:
a) If the ratio of the moment of inertia of the cross-section about the neutral axis to the moment of
inertia about the axis perpendicular to the neutral axis does not exceed 5:1, lateral support shall
not be required.
b) If the ratio of the moments of inertia is greater than 5:1 but does not exceed 10:1, the ends of the
beam shall be held in position at the bottom flange at supports.
c) If the ratio of the moments of inertia is greater than 10:1 but does not exceed 20:1, the beam shall
be held in line at the ends.
d) If the ratio of the moments of inertia is greater than 20:1 but does not exceed 30:1, one edge shall
be held in line.
e) If the ratio of the moments of inertia is greater than 30:1 but does not exceed 40:1, the beam shall
be restrained by bridging or other bracing at intervals of not more than 2400 mm.
f) If the ratio of the moments of inertia is greater than 40:1, the compression flanges shall be fully
restrained.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 291: 10.5.8 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.8 Stiffeners
Load distribution stiffeners shall be provided at reaction points and at the location of heavy
concentrated loads. The stiffeners shall be securely fastened to the webs, bear on the inner surfaces of
the top and bottom flanges, and be made as wide as the flanges. Their dimensions parallel to the span
shall be adequate to support the applied concentrated loads or reactions. The cross-sectional area of a
load-bearing stiffener shall be such that the factored resistance of the flange material perpendicular to
grain is not less than the concentrated load or the reaction due to the factored loads.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 292: 10.5.9 
--------------------------------------------------
10.5.9 Web stabilizers
Web-stabilizing stiffeners shall be provided as necessary to prevent buckling of the webs.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 293: 10.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.1 General
A stressed skin panel shall have continuous or spliced longitudinal web members and continuous or
spliced panel flanges on one or both panel faces, with the flanges glued to the web members (see
Figure 10.4).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 294: 10.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.2 Effective stiffness
The effective stiffness, (EI)e, of a stressed skin panel shall be calculated as follows:
(EI)e = (EI)w * KSE + bf * (Bat * γt² + Bac * γc²) * KS

where  
  (EI)w = stiffness of lumber webs, N•mm²  
  Bat  = specified axial stiffness of tension flange, N/mm (Bo for appropriate panel thickness in Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
  Bac  = specified axial stiffness of compression flange, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
    bf, γt, γc = panel dimensions, mm, in accordance with Figure 10.4

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 295: 10.6.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.1 Bending along stressed skin panel span
The factored bending moment resistance along the direction of the webs of a stressed skin panel shall
be the least of the factored resistances of the tension or compression flanges or the web, calculated as
follows:
a) tension flange:

Mr = φ Tp XJ XG (EI)e / (Ba KSE ct)

where
φ   = 0.95
Tp  = tp (KD KS KT)
    where
    tp = specified strength capacity of flange in axial tension, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
XJ  = stress-joint factor (see Clause 10.4)
XG  = panel geometry reduction factor (see Clause 10.6.3.2)
Ba  = specified axial stiffness of the flange, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)

b) compression flange:

Mr = φ Pp XJ XG (EI)e / (Ba KSE cc)

where
φ   = 0.95
Pp  = pp (KD KS KT)
    where
    pp = specified strength capacity of flange in axial compression, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)

c) web:
Mr = ϕFbKzbXJXG (EI)e / (EKsE cW)

where
ϕ    = 0.9
Fb   = fb (KD KSb KT KH)
       where
       fb = specified strength in bending of webs, MPa
            (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)
E    = modulus of elasticity of web, MPa
       (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)
cW   = greatest distance from neutral axis to outer edge of web, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 296: 10.6.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.2 Panel geometry reduction factor
The panel geometry reduction factor, XG, shall be calculated as follows:
X_G = 1 - 4.8 * (s / l_p)^2

where
  s   = clear spacing between longitudinal web members, mm
  l_p = span of stressed skin panel, mm

Note: This formula accounts for shear lag and is valid for values of s/l_p ranging from 0.05 to 0.25.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 297: 10.6.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.3 Bending perpendicular to panel span
The factored bending resistance of the compression flange between web members shall be calculated
using Clause 9.5.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 298: 10.6.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.4 Buckling of compression flange
The compression flange of a stressed skin panel shall be designed according to principles of engineering
mechanics to prevent elastic buckling failure. If a detailed analysis is not made, such a condition shall be
assumed to be met if
a) s 50hc for panels with their major axis parallel to the span (lp); or
b) s 40hc for panels with their major axis perpendicular to the span (lp)
where s and hc are as shown in Figure 10.4.
Note: See Clause A.10.6.3.4 for additional information on buckling of compression flanges and a detailed analysis
of stressed skin panels with a plywood compression flange.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 299: 10.6.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.5 Shear in-plane of plies
The factored planar shear resistance of the compression flange in a stressed skin panel shall be
calculated in accordance with Clause 9.5.4.1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 300: 10.6.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.6 Shear resistance
The factored shear resistance at the neutral plane of a stressed skin panel, Vr, shall be calculated as
follows:
Vr = ϕ Fv KZv [(EI)e Σbg] / [E KSE ΣQw + Bo Ks bf γ]

where

ϕ   = 0.9

Fv  = fv (KD KSV KT KH)
     where
     fv = specified strength in shear of webs, MPa (see Clauses 6.3.1 and 6.3.2 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)

KZv = size factor in shear (see Clause 6.4.5)

bg  = contact width between flange and web (see Figure 10.4)

E   = modulus of elasticity of web, MPa (see Tables 6.4 to 6.9 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)

ΣQw = sum of moments of area of all webs about neutral plane, mm³

Ba  = specified axial stiffness of the flange, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)

bf  = width of flange, mm

y   = the greater value of yt or yc, mm

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 301: 10.6.3.7 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.7 Flange-web shear
The factored shear resistance, Vrp, of the glued area between the flange and the web of a stressed skin
panel shall be taken as the lesser of the shear capacities based on flange or web components,
calculated as follows:
Vrp = ϕ Vg (EI)e Σ(bg Xv) / (Ba Ks bf y)

where
Ba = specified axial stiffness of the web, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
y  = the greater value of yt or yc, mm

a) for flange:
ϕ  = 0.95
Vg = vpf (KD KS KT)
    where
    vpf = specified strength capacity in planar shear of the web, MPa (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
Xv = shear-modification factor (see Figure 10.2)

b) for web:
ϕ  = 0.9
Vg = fv (KD KS KT)
    where
    fv = specified strength in shear, MPa (see Clauses 6.3.1 and 6.3.2 for sawn lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)
Xv = 2.00

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 302: 10.6.3.8 
--------------------------------------------------
10.6.3.8 Deflection
The deflection of stressed skin panels shall be calculated using the effective stiffness, (EI)e, determined
in accordance with Clause 10.6.2, multiplied by the panel geometry reduction factor, XG, determined in
accordance with Clause 10.6.3.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 303: 11.1 Lateral-load-resisting systems
--------------------------------------------------
11.1 Scope
Clause 11 covers the design of structural systems and assemblies subjected to lateral loads (e.g., wind,
seismic, and earth pressure loads).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 304: 11.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.2.1 General
Clause 11 applies to the structures made with the materials specified in Clause 6 for lumber, Clause 7
for glued-laminated timber, Clause 8 for CLT, Clause 9 for structural panels, Clause 12 for connections,
and Clause 15.3 for proprietary SCL that has been qualified for a specific grade for use in shearwalls
with full-scale cyclic testing.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 305: 11.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
 11.2.2 Additional materials
Clauses 11.3 to 11.8 also apply to gypsum wallboard conforming to Type X (fire-rated) in
ASTM C1396/C1396M.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 306: 11.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3 Design of light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 307: 11.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.1 General
Shearwalls and diaphragms constructed in accordance with requirements specified in Clause 11.3 may
be used to resist lateral forces if they meet the following design requirements:
a) The factored shear resistance determined in accordance with Clauses 11.4 and 11.6.2 for
shearwalls and Clause 11.6.3 for diaphragms shall exceed the factored lateral design forces.
b) Shearwalls and diaphragms shall be designed to resist in-plane bending moments resulting from
the application of lateral design forces in accordance with Clause 11.6.4.
c) Boundary frame members shall be designed to resist axial forces resulting from the application of
lateral design forces. Boundary frame members in single-layer diagonally sheathed shearwalls and
diaphragms shall be designed in accordance with Clause 11.6.
d) All boundary members, chords, and struts of shearwalls and diaphragms shall be designed and
detailed to transmit the induced axial forces.
e) Connections and anchorages capable of resisting the forces to be transferred shall be provided
between the shearwall or diaphragm and the attached components and designed in accordance
with Clause 12.
f) Where applicable, seismic design requirements shall be considered in accordance with Clause 11.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 308: 11.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.2 Shearwalls and diaphragms using wood structural panels
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 309: 11.3.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.2.1 Framing
Framing members shall be at least 38 mm thick in shearwalls and diaphragms. For diaphragms with
multiple rows of fasteners, framing members shall be at least 64 mm thick and 64 mm wide at
boundaries and adjoining panel edges. Boundary members shall be adequately interconnected at corner
intersections and member joints shall be spliced adequately.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 310: 11.3.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.2.2 Sheathing
Shearwalls and diaphragms using plywood or OSB shall be constructed with panels not less than 7.5 mm
in thickness and 1200 × 2400 mm in plane dimensions, except near boundaries and changes in framing,

where up to two short or narrow panels may be used. For construction sheathing OSB, the product
specification shall also include a panel mark identifying an end-use rating. Table A.9 provides an
equivalence between nominal thicknesses of OSB panel and panel marks. For panels that also act as
exterior siding, the minimum panel thickness shall be 9.5 mm.
Sheathing panels for blocked shearwalls and diaphragms shall be arranged as indicated in Figures 11.1
and 11.2, respectively. All panel edges shall bear and be attached to the framing members or blocking
except for unblocked assemblies where the blocking between framing members is omitted as indicated
in Figures 11.5 and 11.6. A gap of not less than 2 mm shall be left between adjacent panel edges. Panels
less than 300 mm wide shall be blocked.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 311: 11.3.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.2.3 Sheathing fastening
Fasteners shall be placed not less than 9 mm from the framing edge and panel edge and shall be spaced
not less than 50 mm and not more than 150 mm along all edges of each panel. Fastener spacing along
all intermediate framing members shall not be greater than 300 mm. Fasteners shall be firmly driven
into framing members but shall not be over-driven into sheathing more than 15% of the panel
thickness.
Where the fastening in a shearwall is a double-shear connection with a panel in the middle and framing
members as side members, the framing members and mid-panel shall be connected using fasteners
with penetration meeting the required lengths given in Figure 12.17, and with the same spacing at all
locations. There shall be a minimum of 3 mm gap between adjacent panels. For studs where panels
meet, additional fasteners not subjected to double shear shall be installed to prevent detachment of the
studs (see Figure 11.3).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 312: 11.3.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.2.4 Additional construction requirements
The following are additional requirements for shearwalls and diaphragms using wood structural panels:
a) Where the fastener spacing at panel edges is 50 mm, framing at adjoining panel edges shall be
64 mm or thicker (or two 38-mm-thick framing members connected to transfer the factored shear
force), and the fasteners shall be staggered.
b) Where the fasteners of 3.66 mm in diameter penetrate more than 41 mm into framing and are
spaced 75 mm or less, framing at adjoining panel edges shall be 64 mm or thicker (or two 38-mm-thick
framing members connected to transfer the factored shear force), and the fasteners shall be
staggered.
c) For shearwalls where panels are applied on both faces of a wall and fastener spacing is less than
150 mm on either side, framing shall be 64 mm or thicker (or two 38-mm-thick framing members
connected to transfer the factored shear force), and fasteners on each side shall be staggered.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 313: 11.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.3 Shearwalls using gypsum wallboard
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 314: 11.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.3.1 Sheathing
Shearwalls using gypsum wallboard shall be constructed with panels not less than 1200 × 2400 mm,
except near boundaries and changes in framing, where up to two short or narrow panels may be used.
The application of gypsum wallboard shall be restricted to platform frame construction where the
height of a storey does not exceed 3.6 m.
Notes:
1) There should exist a balanced spatial distribution of the gypsum wallboard and wood structural panels
resisting shear in each direction in a storey.
2) See Clause 11.8.8 for seismic design requirements for shearwalls using gypsum wallboard.
3) See Clause 11.8.9 for seismic design requirements for load-bearing walls constructed with gypsum wallboard
only.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 315: 11.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.3.2 Sheathing fastening
In gypsum wallboard application nails or screws shall be placed not less than 9 mm from the panel
edge.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 316: 11.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.4 Shearwalls and diaphragms using diagonal lumber sheathing
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 317: 11.3.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.4.1 General
Shearwalls and diaphragms described in Clauses 11.3.4.2 and 11.3.4.3 shall be constructed using a
single layer of diagonally sheathed lumber (see Clause 11.3.4.2) or a double layer of diagonally sheathed
lumber (see Clause 11.3.4.3). More than two layers of diagonal lumber sheathing shall not be
permitted.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 318: 11.3.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.4.2 Single-layer diagonal sheathing
Single-layer diagonal sheathing shall be made up of 19-mm or 38-mm boards laid at an angle of
approximately 45° to supports. The sheathing shall be fastened to each intermediate framing member
with at least two common nails (dF = 3.25 mm or dF = 3.33 mm) for 19 × 140 mm boards and three
common nails (dF = 3.25 mm or dF = 3.33 mm) for 19 × 184 mm or wider boards. One additional nail
shall be used in each board at the boundary framing members. End joints in adjacent rows of boards
shall be staggered by at least one stud or joist space. Joints on the same support shall be separated by
at least two rows of boards. Shearwalls and diaphragms constructed with a 38-mm-thick diagonal
sheathing using common nails (dF = 4.06 mm) may be used at the same shear values and in the same
locations as for 19-mm boards fastened with common nails (dF = 3.25 mm or dF = 3.33 mm), if there are
no splices in adjacent boards on the same support and the supports are not less than 89 mm in depth
or 64 mm in thickness.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 319: 11.3.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.3.4.3 Double-layer diagonal sheathing
Double-layer diagonal sheathing shall meet the requirements of Clause 11.3.4.2 and consist of two
layers of diagonal boards 19 mm in thickness for each layer and at 90° to each other on the same face
of the supporting members. The nails used for fastening the outer layer shall have a minimum
penetration of 8dF into the framing members. Nails in the inner and outer layers shall be staggered
along the framing members.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 320: 11.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4 Design considerations for light-frame shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 321: 11.4.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.1.1 General
Only fully sheathed segments that meet the requirements for maximum aspect ratio limits in
Clause 11.4.1.2 shall be considered in the analysis of shearwalls with openings. The contribution of
sheathing above and below openings shall not be included in the calculation of shearwall resistance.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 322: 11.4.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.1.2 Shearwall segment aspect ratio
The maximum aspect ratio (height-to-length ratio) of a blocked shearwall segment shall be 3.5:1. The
maximum aspect ratio of an unblocked shearwall segment shall be 2:1. The height is defined as the
height from the underside of the bottom shearwall plate to the topside of the top shearwall plate
within a storey.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 323: 11.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.2 Shearwalls with dissimilar materials
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 324: 11.4.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.2.1 Standard method
Except as permitted by Clause 11.4.2.2, shearwalls constructed with dissimilar materials, thicknesses, or
fastener spacings along the length of the shearwall shall be analyzed as the sum of the different
shearwall segments.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 325: 11.4.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.2.2 Alternative method
Shearwalls constructed with dissimilar materials, thicknesses, or fastener spacing along the length of the
shearwall may be analyzed as a shearwall of uniform construction, provided that the least value of the
shearwall segment resistance, determined in accordance with Clause 11.6.2, is applied over the entire
shearwall length.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 326: 11.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.3 Shearwalls with multiple layers
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 327: 11.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.3.1 Shearwalls with two layers of sheathing panels on one side
The factored shear resistance for a shearwall with two layers of the same or different sheathing panels
applied to one side shall be determined by the first (inside) layer of panels. Where the first layer is
gypsum wallboard with thickness not exceeding 15.9 mm and the second layer is a structural panel, the
specified shear resistance of the shearwall may be calculated by assuming that the second layer is
applied directly to framing and using the actual fastener penetration into the framing member, if
minimum fastener penetration in the framing is satisfied.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 328: 11.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.3.2 Shearwalls with sheathing panels on two sides
The factored shear resistance of a shearwall shall be cumulative when sheathing panels of the same or
different materials are applied on each side.
Notes:
1) See Table 11.5 for the appropriate seismic design factors for shearwalls with different sheathing materials.
2) See Clause 11.8.8 for seismic design requirements for shearwalls using gypsum wallboard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 329: 11.4.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.4.1 Shearwall segments with hold-downs
Where the factored dead loads do not prevent shearwall overturning, hold-downs [see Figure 11.4 a)]
shall be designed to resist the factored uplift forces and transfer the forces through a continuous load
path to the foundation.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 330: 11.4.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.4.2 Shearwall segments without hold-downs
Where the factored dead loads do not prevent shearwall overturning and hold-downs are not used,
anchorage [see Figure 11.4 b)] on the bottom plate within 300 mm from each end of the shearwall
segment shall transfer the factored uplift force, Rij (see Figure 11.7), to the supporting structure (i.e., to
the top plate of the shearwall below or to the foundation).

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 331: 11.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.5 Shearwall anchorage
The anchor bolt connections that resist the lateral forces shall be designed in accordance with
Clause 12.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 332: 11.4.6 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.6 Concrete or masonry wall anchorage
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 333: 11.4.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.6.1 Anchorage design
Where wood roofs and floors are used to provide lateral support to concrete and masonry walls, they
shall be anchored to those walls. The anchorage shall provide a direct connection between the walls
and the roof or floor construction. The connections shall be designed to resist the factored lateral force
induced by the wall, but not less than 3 kN/m of the wall.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 334: 11.4.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.4.6.2 Anchorage details
Anchorage to concrete or masonry walls shall not be accomplished by use of toe-nails or nails subject to
withdrawal, nor shall wood ledgers be designed to resist tensile stresses perpendicular to grain.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 335: 11.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5 Strength-adjustment factors for light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 336: 11.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.1 Fastener spacing factor, Js
The shear strength of shearwalls and diaphragms built with wood structural panel and lumber framing
shall be multiplied by the fastener spacing factor, Js, given as follows:
Js = 1.0 for s ≥ 150 mm  
   = 1 − ( (150 − s) / 150 )^4.2 for 50 mm ≤ s < 150 mm  

where  
s = fastener spacing along panel edges, mm  

Note: For proprietary framing material, appropriate adjustment factors can be obtained from the product manufacturer (i.e., proprietary design literature and Product Evaluation Reports in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations).

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 337: 11.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.2 11.5.2 Fastener row factor for diaphragms, Jf
The shear strength of diaphragms sheathed with wood structural panels shall be multiplied by the
fastener row factor, Jf, given in Table 11.1, to account for the number of rows of fasteners attaching the
sheathing to framing in blocked diaphragms.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 338: 11.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.3 Factor for unblocked diaphragms, Jud
The shear strength of unblocked diaphragms sheathed with wood structural panels shall be calculated
by multiplying the specified shear strength of a blocked diaphragm with one row of sheathing fasteners
spaced at 150 mm along panel edges and 300 mm along intermediate framing members by the factor,
Jud, given in Table 11.2.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 339: 11.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.4 Factor for unblocked shearwalls, Jus
The shear strength of unblocked shearwalls sheathed with wood structural panels shall be calculated by
multiplying the specified shear strength of a blocked shearwall with sheathing fasteners spaced at
150 mm along panel edges and 300 mm along intermediate framing members by the factor, Jus, given in
Table 11.3. The maximum height, H, of unblocked shearwalls shall be 4.88 m.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 340: 11.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5 11.5.5 Hold-down-effect factor for shearwall segments, Jhd
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 341: 11.5.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5.1 Shearwall segments with hold-downs
For shearwall segments with hold-downs that are designed to resist all the factored uplift forces due to
overturning, Jhd shall equal 1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 342: 11.5.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5.2 Conditions for shearwall segments with Jhd < 1.0
The conditions for calculating Jhd in Clauses 11.5.5.3 to 11.5.5.5 shall be as follows:
a) the maximum fastener diameter shall be 3.33 mm and the minimum fastener spacing shall be
100 mm;

b) the maximum specified shear strength, including both sides of a shearwall where applicable, shall
be 10.3 kN/m; and
c) the maximum height of the shearwall segment shall be less than 3.6 m.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 343: 11.5.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5.3 Shearwall segments without hold-downs
For shearwall segments
a) without hold-downs at either end;
b) meeting the requirements of Clauses 11.4.4.2 and 11.5.5.2; and
c) with Pij not less than zero,
Jhd shall be calculated as follows:
Jhd = √[1 + 2(Pij / Vhd) + (Hs / Ls)²] − (Hs / Ls) ≤ 1.0

where  
Pij  = factored uplift restraint force for storey i at the bottom of the end stud of a shearwall segment j, kN  
Vhd  = factored shear resistance of the shearwall segment calculated with Jhd equal to 1.0, kN  
Hs   = height of shearwall segment, m  
Ls   = length of shearwall segment, m  

Note: See Figure 11.7.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 344: 11.5.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5.4 11.5.5.4 Shearwall segments with hold-downs only at the bottom of the segment
For a lower-storey shearwall segment with hold-downs at the bottom of the shearwall segment and
without hold-downs at the top, and with P less than zero,
Jhd = (Vhd + P) / Vhd ≤ 1.0

where  
Vhd = factored shear resistance of the shearwall segment calculated with Jhd equal to 1.0, kN  
P   = factored uplift restraint force at the top of the end stud of a shearwall segment, kN

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 345: 11.5.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.5.5.5 11.5.5.5 Shearwall segments with hold-downs only on one end
For a shearwall segment with hold-downs only on one end of the segment, the following shall apply:
a)Jhd shall be determined in accordance with Clause 11.5.5.1 if designed to resist all uplift forces due
to overturning;
b) Jhd shall be determined in accordance with Clause 11.5.5.3 if there is no hold-down on the tension
end of the segment; an
c) Jhd shall be determined in accordance with Clause 11.5.5.4 if there is a hold-down only at the
bottom of the tension end of a lower-storey segment.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 346: 11.6 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6 Strength and resistance of light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 347: 11.6.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.1.1 Standard methods
Provisions in Clauses 11.6 to 11.8 apply to light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms constructed with
shear panels consisting of wood structural panels, gypsum wallboard, or diagonal lumber sheathing
fastened to framing members using nails of diameter 3.76 mm or smaller, unless otherwise stated in
these Clauses.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 348: 11.6.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.1.2 Alternative methods
Factored shear resistance of light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms may be derived from full-scale
testing, provided that the tests are conducted in accordance with recognized test standards.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 349: 11.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.2 Shear resistance of shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 350: 11.6.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.2.1 General
The factored shear resistance, Vr, of shearwalls constructed with wood structural panels, gypsum
wallboard, or diagonal lumber sheathing in accordance with Clauses 11.3.2, 11.3.3, or 11.3.4,
respectively, shall be calculated as follows:
Vr = ΣVrs
where
Vrs = factored shear resistance of each shearwall segment along the length of the shearwall, kN, in
accordance with Clauses 11.6.2.2, 11.6.2.3, or 11.6.2.4, respectively.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 351: 11.6.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.2.2 Shearwall segments with wood structural panels
The factored shear resistance, Vrs, of a shearwall segment with wood structural panels shall be taken as
the smaller shear resistance value determined in Items a) and b) as follows:
a) shear resistance governed by sheathing-to-framing connection strength resistance:
Vrs = ϕ vd Jd ns Jus Js Jhd Ls

where  
ϕ   = 0.8  
vd  = Nu / s, kN/m  

Nu  = lateral strength resistance of sheathing-to-framing connections along panel edges, per shear plane per fastener, N  
      (see Clause 12.9.3.2)  
      For single-shear fastening shearwalls (shearwalls with plywood or OSB panels fastened to framing with single shear connection),  
      the embedment strength of the structural panel in Clause 12.9.3.2, f1, may be calculated using:  
      f1 = 51(1 – 0.1df), MPa  

s   = fastener spacing along panel edges, mm (see Clause 11.3.4)  
Jd  = adjustment factor for diaphragm and shearwall construction (see Clause 12.9.3.1)  
ns  = number of shear planes in sheathing-to-framing connections (see Clause 11.3.2.3)  
Jus = factor for unblocked shearwalls (see Clause 11.5.4)  
Js  = fastener spacing adjustment factor (see Clause 11.5.1)  
Jhd = hold-down-effect factor for shearwall segment (see Clause 11.5.5)  
Ls  = length of shearwall segment parallel to the direction of load, m  
b) shear resistance governed by sheathing panel buckling:
Vrs = ϕ νpb KD KS KT Ls

where  
ϕ     = 0.8  
νpb   = panel buckling strength of the most critical structural panel within the segment, kN/m  
       = Kpb * (π² * t² / 30000) * (Bα,0 * Bα,90)^(3/4)  

where  
Kpb   = panel buckling factor  
       = 1.7(η + 1) * exp(–α / (0.05η + 0.75)) + (0.5η + 0.8)
where

α = (a / b) * (Ba,90 / Ba,0)^(1/4)

η = (2Bv) / √(Ba,0 * Ba,90)

where  
a      = larger dimension of panel, mm  
b      = smaller dimension of panel, mm  
Ba,0   = axial stiffness of panel 0° orientation, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
Ba,90  = axial stiffness of panel 90° orientation, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
Bv     = shear-through-thickness rigidity, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)  
t      = panel thickness, mm  

KS     = service-condition factor (see Table 9.4)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 352: 11.6.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.2.3 Shearwall segments with gypsum wallboard sheathing
The factored shear resistance, Vrs, of a shearwall segment with gypsum wallboard sheathing shall be
calculated as follows:
Vrs =  ϕ vd Jhd Ls
where
 ϕ = 0.7
vd = specified shear strength for shearwall segment sheathed with gypsum wallboard, kN/m (see Clause 11.5.5)
Ls = length of shearwall segmesnt parllel to the direction of load, m
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 353: 11.6.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.2.4 Shearwall segments with diagonal lumber sheathing
The factored shear resistance, V_rs, of a shearwall segment with diagonal lumber sheathing shall be calculated as follows:

    V_rs = φ v_d J_D n_L L_s

where
    φ   = 0.8
    v_d = 2 N_u / (3 √2 s)

where
    N_u = lateral strength resistance of sheathing-to-framing connections along the boundary frame members of single-layer sheathing or the inner layer of double-layer sheathing, per fastener, N (see Clauses 11.3.4.2 and 12.9.3)
    s   = fastener spacing evenly distributed along boundary frame members, but not less than 65 mm (see Clause 11.3.4.2)
    J_D = adjustment factor for diaphragm and shearwall construction (see Clause 12.9.3.1)
    n_L = number of sheathing layers
        = 1 for single-layer lumber sheathing
        = 2 for double-layer lumber sheathing
    L_s = length of shearwall segment parallel to the direction of load, m

--------------------------------------------------
Clause 354: 11.6.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.3 Shear resistance of diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 355: 11.6.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.3.1 General
The factored shear resistance of diaphragms constructed with wood structural panels in accordance
with Clause 11.3.2 shall be calculated in accordance with Clause 11.6.3.2. The factored shear resistance
of diaphragms constructed with diagonal lumber sheathing in accordance with Clause 11.3.4 shall be
calculated in accordance with Clause 11.6.3.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 356: 11.6.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.3.2 Diaphragms with wood structural panels
The factored shear resistance, Vrs, of a diaphragm with wood structural panels shall be taken as the
smaller value determined as follows:
a) shear resistance governed by sheathing-to-framing connection strength resistance:
Vrs = φ vd JD Js Jf Jud LD
where
φ = 0.8
vd = Nu/s, kN/m
where
Nu = lateral strength resistance of sheathing-to-framing connections along panel edges, per
fastener, N (see Clause 12.9.3.2 for nails)
For diaphragms with plywood or OSB panels fastened to framing, the embedment
strength of the structural panel in Clause 12.9.3.2, f1, may be calculated using:
f1 = 51(1 – 0.1dF), MPa
s = fastener spacing along the edges, mm
JD = adjustment factor for diaphragm and shearwall construction (see Clause 12.9.3.1)
Js = fastener spacing factor (see Clause 11.5.1)
Jf = fastener row factor for blocked diaphragms (see Clause 11.5.2)
Jud = factor for unblocked diaphragms (see Clause 11.5.3)
LD = dimension of diaphragm parallel to the direction of load, m

b) Shear resistance governed by sheathing panel buckling:

V_rs = ϕ * ν_pb * K_D * K_S * K_T * L_D

where
ϕ    = 0.8
ν_pb = panel buckling strength of the most critical structural panel within the segment, kN/m
     = |K_pb * (π² * t² / 3000b) * (B_a,0 * B_a,90)^3|^(1/4)

where
K_pb = panel buckling factor
     = 1.7 * (η + 1) * exp(–α / (0.05η + 0.75)) + (0.5η + 0.8)

where
η    = sqrt(2B_v / (B_a,0 * B_a,90))

α = (a / b) × (Ba,90 / Ba,0)^(1/4)

where
a    = larger dimension of panel, mm
b    = smaller dimension of panel, mm
Ba,0  = axial stiffness of panel at 0° orientation, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
Ba,90  = axial stiffness of panel at 90° orientation, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
Bv   = shear-through-thickness rigidity, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
t    = panel thickness, mm
Ks   = service-condition factor (see Table 9.4)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 357: 11.6.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.3.3 Diaphragms with diagonal lumber sheathing
The factored shear resistance, Vrs, of a diaphragm with diagonal lumber sheathing shall be calculated as
follows:
Vrs = φ vd JD nL LD
where
φ = 0.8
vd =2/3 Nu/(2^0.5 s)
where
Nu= lateral strength resistance of sheathing-to-framing connections along the boundary frame
members of single-layer sheathing or the inner layer of double-layer sheathing, per fastener,
N (see Clauses 11.3.4.2, 11.3.4.3, and 12.9.3)
s= fastener spacing evenly distributed along boundary frame members, but not less than
65 mm (see Clause 11.4.3.2)
JD = adjustment factor for diaphragm and shearwall construction (see Clause 12.9.3.1)
nL = number of sheathing layers
    = 1 for single-layer lumber sheathing
    = 2 for double-layer lumber sheathing
LD = dimension of diaphragm parallel to the direction of load, m
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 358: 11.6.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.4 Moment resistance of shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 359: 11.6.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.4.1 General
Except as provided in Clause 11.6.4.2, the factored moment resistance of shearwalls and diaphragms
shall be calculated as follows:
Mr = Pr h
where
Pr= factored axial tension and compression resistance of the elements resisting chord forces (with
due allowance being made for joints), N
h= centre-to-centre distance between moment-resisting elements, mm
    = centre-to-centre distance between diaphragm chords in the design of diaphragms, mm
    = centre-to-centre distance between stud chords in shearwall segments designed with hold-downs
    at both ends of the shearwall segment, mm
    = length of shearwall segment minus 300 mm for shearwall segments designed without hold-downs
    at both ends of the segment, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 360: 11.6.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.4.2 Moment resistance for shearwall segments without hold-downs
For shearwall segments without hold-downs, a moment resistance calculation for the design of the
tension chords shall not be required.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 361: 11.6.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.5 Boundary members in shearwalls and diaphragms with single-layer diagonal
sheathing
Note: See the CWC Commentary on CSA O86.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 362: 11.6.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.5.1 General
Single-layer diagonal sheathing produces a load component acting perpendicular to the boundary frame
members in the plane of the shear panel. Boundary frame members in single-layer diagonally sheathed
shearwalls and diaphragms shall be designed to resist the
a) factored bending moment, Mf, caused by the normal load component, in combination with the
boundary member axial forces; and
b) factored mutual separation force, Pc, at corner intersections.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 363: 11.6.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.5.2 Shearwalls
Mf and Pc shall be calculated for shearwall segments as follows:

Mf = (Fij × Hs²) / (8 × Ls)
Pc = (Fij × Hs) / (2 × Ls)

where
Fij = factored shear force applied to the shearwall segment
Hs = height of the shearwall segment
Ls = length of the shearwall segment


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 364: 11.6.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.6.5.3 Diaphragms
Mf and Pc shall be calculated for diaphragms as follows:
Mf = (Fd x Ld)/8

where
Fd = factored diaphragm shear force at the boundary member
LD = dimension of diaphragm parallel to direction of factored load
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 365: 11.7 
--------------------------------------------------
11.7 Deflection of light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 366: 11.7.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.7.1.1 General
Deflection of single-storey blocked and unblocked shearwall segments may be calculated in accordance
with Clauses 11.7.1.2 and 11.7.1.3 respectively.
In the calculation of deflection of multi-storey shearwalls, multi-storey effects shall be considered.
Note: See Clause A.11.7.1 for additional information on multi-storey effects.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 367: 11.7.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.7.1.2 Blocked shearwall segments
The static deflection at the top of the wall, sw, mm, of a blocked shearwall segment with wood
structural panels and gypsum wallboard constructed in accordance with Clauses 11.3.2 to 11.3.3
respectively, may be calculated as follows:

Δ_sw = (2νHs³) / (3EAL_s) + (νHs) / Bv + 0.0025Hs * en + (Hs / Ls) * do

where
ν = maximum shear due to specified loads at the top of the wall, N/mm
Hs = height of shearwall segment, mm
E = modulus of elasticity of vertical boundary framing members, N/mm²
A = cross-sectional area of the boundary member, mm²
Ls = length of shearwall segment, mm
Bv = shear-through-thickness rigidity of the sheathing, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3 for wood structural panels. For gypsum wallboard, Bv may be taken as 7000 N/mm)
en = sheathing-to-framing connection deformation, mm (see Clause A.11.7)
do = total vertical elongation of the wall overturning restraint system (including fastener slip, hold-down device elongation, anchor, or rod elongation) at the induced shear load

For shearwall segments without hold-downs, the total vertical elongation, do, may be calculated as follows:

do = 2.5 * df * Km * [(νHs - Pij) / (nu)]¹.⁷ * (sn / Ls)

Note: This equation is an approximation.

where
df = diameter of sheathing fastener, mm
Km = service-creep factor (see Table A.23)
ν = maximum shear due to specified load at the top of the wall, N/mm
Hs = height of shearwall segment, mm
Pij = specified uplift restraint force for storey i at the bottom of the end stud of a shearwall segment j, N
sn = length of sheathing spacing along panel edge, mm
Ls = length of shearwall segment, mm
nu = unit lateral strength resistance per shear plane of sheathing-to-framing connection, N (see Clause 12.9.3.1)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 368: 11.7.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.7.1.3 11.7.1.3 Unblocked shearwall segments
The deflection of an unblocked shearwall segment with wood structural panels, ub, may be calculated
as follows:
Δ_ub = Δ_sw/Jus

where
Δ_sw= deflection of a blocked shearwall segment with fasteners spaced at 150 mm on centre around
panel edges and 300 mm on centre along intermediate framing members, calculated in
accordance with Clause 11.7.1.2
Jus= adjustment factor for unblocked shearwalls (see Table 11.3)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 369: 11.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.7.2 Deflection of diaphragms
The lateral static deflection at mid-span, d, mm, of a simply supported blocked diaphragm with wood
structural panels constructed in accordance with Clause 11.3.2 may be calculated as follows:
Δd = (5vL³) / (96EALd) + (vL) / (4Bv) + 0.00061 * en + Σ(Δc * x) / (2Ld)

Where:
  v   = maximum shear due to specified loads in the direction under consideration, N/mm
  L   = dimension of diaphragm perpendicular to the direction of load, mm
  E   = modulus of elasticity of the chord, N/mm²
  A   = cross-sectional area of the chord, mm²
  Ld  = dimension of diaphragm parallel to the direction of load, mm
  Bv  = shear-through-thickness rigidity of the sheathing, N/mm (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3)
  en  = sheathing-to-framing connection deformation, mm (see Clause A.11.7)
  Σ(Δc * x) = sum of individual chord-splice slip values Δc (both sides of the diaphragm),
              each multiplied by its distance x to the nearest suppor
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 370: 11.8 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8 Seismic design considerations for light-frame shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 371: 11.8.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.1 General
Seismic design forces for shearwalls and diaphragms shall be determined using the appropriate
procedures specified in the National Building Code of Canada. The corresponding ductility-related
seismic-force-modification factor, Rd, and system overstrength related force modification factor, Ro, for
shearwalls are given in Table 11.5, provided failure is governed by sheathing-to-framing connection. The
sheathing-to-framing connections shall be designed to yield in mode c), d), e), or g) shown in
Clause 12.9.3.2 for nails to ensure ductility in the shearwall and diaphragm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 372: 11.8.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.2 Shearwall hold-downs and shear transfer connections
Anchor bolts and interstorey connections resisting seismic shear forces and hold-downs resisting seismic
uplift forces of a shearwall or a shearwall segment shall be designed for the forces that are at least 20%
greater than the effects of the seismic load.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 373: 11.8.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.3 Over-capacity of wood light-frame seismic force resisting system (SFRS)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 374: 11.8.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.3.1 Storey over-capacity coefficient, Ci
The over-capacity coefficient, Ci, for each storey, i, for each horizontal direction, shall be greater than or
equal to 1.0 and shall be calculated as follows:
Ci = Vri/Vfi

where
Vri = factored resistance of the wood light-frame SFRS in each storey, i
Vfi = factored seismic shear load for storey i obtained using Rd Ro coefficients for the wood light-frame
SFRS in accordance with the National Building Code of Canada
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 375: 11.8.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.3.2 Ratio of second storey to first storey over-capacity coefficients
For structures that have three or more storeys, the vertical SFRSs shall be designed so that the ratio of
the over-capacity coefficient of the second storey, C2, and the over-capacity coefficient of the first
storey, C1, is as follows:
0.9<C2/C1<1.2
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 376: 11.8.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.4 Light-frame diaphragms supported on light-frame shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 377: 11.8.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.4.1 General
Light-frame diaphragms shall be designed to resist seismic forces determined in accordance with
Clause 11.8.4.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 378: 11.8.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.4.2 Seismic design forces for diaphragms
The seismic design force for a diaphragm at each storey, i, for each horizontal direction, shall be
calculated as follows:
VDi = CDi Fi
where
VDi = seismic design force for a diaphragm at each storey, i
CDi = over-capacity coefficient at storey i for each horizontal direction
= lesser of Ci or 1.2
Fi = factored seismic force at each storey, i, calculated using Rd Ro for the light-frame shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 379: 11.8.5 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.5 Light-frame diaphragms in buildings with SFRSs other than light-frame
shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 380: 11.8.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.5.1 General
Clause 11.8.5 applies to buildings that
a) use reinforced concrete, masonry, steel, or wood-based structural systems other than light-frame
shearwalls for supporting vertical SFRSs; and
b) have light-frame diaphragms.
Vertical SFRSs shall be designed in accordance with appropriate CSA material standards.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 381: 11.8.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.5.2 Seismic design forces for diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 382: 11.8.5.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.5.2.1 Diaphragms designed to yield
Light-frame diaphragms intended to exhibit ductile behaviour and to yield before the supporting SFRS
shall be designed to resist seismic forces determined using the Rd Ro factors for the vertical SFRS. Such
seismic design loads, however, shall not be less than loads determined using Rd Ro = 2.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 383: 11.8.5.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.5.2.2 Diaphragms designed not to yield
Light-frame diaphragms intended not to yield before the supporting SFRS shall be designed to resist a
seismic force, VDi, calculated as follows:
VDi = 1.2 CiFi (for wood SFRS other than shearwalls sheathed with wood structural panels)
VDi = γiFi (for non-wood SFRS)
where
VDi = seismic design force on the diaphragm at storey i
Ci = over-capacity coefficient at storey i equal to the value of Ci determined in accordance with
Clause 11.8.3.1
Fi = factored seismic force at storey i calculated using the Rd Ro for the SFRS
γi = over-strength coefficient applied at level li for the vertical SFRSS, determined using principles of capacity-based design in accordance with the applicable CSA material standard
Note: VDi may be taken as not greater than Fi determined using Rd Ro = 1.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 384: 11.8.6 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.6 Design of force transfer elements
Diaphragm chords, splice joints in structural members and connections of the diaphragm around
openings, and other force-transfer elements shall be designed for seismic loads that are at least 20%
greater than the seismic design force on the diaphragm VDi.
Connections and drag struts that are transferring shear forces between the segments of the vertical
SFRS and the diaphragm shall be designed for seismic forces that are at least 20% greater than the
shear force that is being transferred.
Parts of the diaphragm around wall offsets shall be designed for seismic loads that are at least 20%
greater than the seismic design force of the offset SFRS.
Note: Forces used for the design of force transfer elements may be taken as not greater than the forces
determined using Rd Ro = 1.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 385: 11.8.7 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.7 Structures in low seismic zones
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 386: 11.8.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.7.1 General
Clauses 11.8.7.2 and 11.8.7.3 apply to structures where the Seismic Category of building is SC1 or SC2
determined in accordance with the National Building Code of Canada, Subclause 4.1.8.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 387: 11.8.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.7.2 Seismic design forces for diaphragms
Seismic design forces for diaphragms shall be determined in accordance with Clauses 11.8.4 and 11.8.5,
with the over-capacity coefficient, Ci, taken as 1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 388: 11.8.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.7.3 Design of force-transfer elements
Force-transfer elements shall be designed in accordance with Clause 11.8.6.
= over-strength coefficient applied at level i for the vertical SFRS, determined using principles of
capacity-based design in accordance with the applicable CSA material standar
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 389: 11.8.8 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.8 Requirements for shearwalls using gypsum wallboard
For seismic design, gypsum wallboard shall be used in combination with wood structural panels. The
shear force resisted by gypsum wallboard shall be equal to or less than the percentage of storey shear
forces specified in Table 11.6. If the maximum percentages are exceeded, Rd shall be equal to 1.0 and Ro
shall be equal to 1.0. Gypsum wallboard shall not be considered to provide lateral resistance when the
interstorey drift ratio exceeds 1%. For buildings that are higher than 4 storeys, the contribution of the
gypsum wallboard shall not be accounted for in seismic resistance.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 390: 11.8.9 
--------------------------------------------------
11.8.9 Load-bearing walls constructed with gypsum wallboard only
When the interstorey drift due to seismic loading exceeds 1% on any floor, all load-bearing stud walls
within the storey which rely on the gypsum wallboard sheathing to prevent weak axis buckling shall be
designed to resist the factored axial load combination with seismic load in accordance with the
applicable building code, and assuming the gypsum wallboard is providing no lateral support.
Alternatively a secondary blocking system shall be used to provide lateral support to the studs.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 391: 11.9 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9 Design of CLT shearwalls and diaphragms
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 392: 11.9.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.1.1 Standard systems
Clause 11.9 shall apply to platform-type CLT construction where
a) the lateral-load-resisting system consists of CLT shearwalls; and
b) CLT walls are placed on
i) a platform of CLT floor panels; or
ii) a concrete podium or concrete foundation at the lowest level.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 393: 11.9.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.1.2 Alternative systems
Alternative systems shall be designed in accordance with Clause 4.3.2 of this Standard and the National
Building Code of Canada, Article 4.1.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 394: 11.9.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.2.1 Lateral resistance of CLT shearwalls
The lateral resistance of CLT shearwalls shall be governed by the resistance of connections between the
shearwalls and the foundation or floor, and connections between the individual panels, calculated using
methods of mechanics.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 395: 11.9.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.2.2 Lateral resistance of CLT diaphragms
The lateral resistance of CLT diaphragms shall be governed by the resistance of connections between
the diaphragms and the supporting structure and connections between the individual panels, calculated
using methods of mechanics.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 396: 11.9.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.2.3 Shearwall resistance to overturning
Where the factored dead loads do not prevent shearwall overturning, hold-downs shall be used to
transfer the forces through a continuous load path.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 397: 11.9.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.2.4 Compressive resistance at ends of CLT shearwalls
The compressive resistance at the ends of shearwalls shall be calculated in accordance with
Clauses 8.4.5 and 8.4.6 and shall be greater than or equal to the overturning forces, calculated using
methods of mechanics.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 398: 11.9.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3 Seismic design considerations for CLT structures
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 399: 11.9.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.1 General
Except as specified in Clause 11.9.3.2.2, a SFRS consisting of moderately ductile CLT shearwalls,
platform-type construction, as defined in the National Building Code, shall be designed to resist forces
calculated using Rd = 2.0 and Ro = 1.5, where energy is dissipated in rocking motion of shearwall
segments through designated connections in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.3.1 following the capacity
design principles described in Clause 11.9.3.4. Shearwall segments shall have an aspect ratio as
specified in Clause 11.9.3.5.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 400: 11.9.3.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.2.1 Irregularity restrictions
CLT platform-type SFRS constructed with more than 4 storeys, and where the Seismic Category of
building is SC3 or SC4, shall be designed in accordance with the provisions of the National Building
Code, Article 4.1.8.7 and shall not contain irregularities prohibited in the National Building Code, Article
4.1.8.10.
Note: The Seismic Category of buildings is determined in accordance with the National Building Code of Canada,
Subclause 4.1.8.5 on the basis of IES(0.2) and IES(1.0) irrespective of the fundamental lateral period of the
building Ta.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 401: 11.9.3.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.2.2 Shear segments with aspect ratios less than 2:1
SFRS consisting of CLT shearwall segments with aspect ratios less than 2:1 as specified in
Clause 11.9.3.5.2 and that are considered part of the SFRS shall be considered limited ductility CLT
shearwalls, platform type construction, as defined in the National Building Code, and shall be designed
for forces calculated using Rd Ro 1.3, provided energy is dissipated through designated connections in
accordance with Clause 11.9.3.3.1 following the capacity design principles described in Clause 11.9.3.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 402: 11.9.3.2.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.2.3.1 Height limit for Seismic Categories SC1, SC2, and SC3
The height of the CLT SFRS shall not exceed 30 m where the Seismic Category determined in accordance
with the National Building Code is SC1, SC2, or SC3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 403: 11.9.3.2.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.2.3.2 Height limit for Seismic Category SC4
The height of the CLT SLRS shall not exceed 20 m where the Seismic Category determined in accordance
with the National Building Code is SC4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 404: 11.9.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.3.1 Energy-dissipative connections
Energy-dissipative connections shall satisfy all the following requirements:
a) Connections shall be designed so that a yielding mode governs the resistance.
b) Connections shall be at least moderately ductile in the directions associated with the rocking rigid
body motions of CLT panels.
c) Connections shall possess sufficient deformation capacity under the force and displacement
demands that are induced in them to allow for the CLT panels to develop rocking motion.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 405: 11.9.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.3.2 Non-dissipative connections
Non-dissipative connections shall be capacity-protected by designing them to remain elastic under the
force and displacement demands that are induced in them when the energy-dissipative connections
reach the 95th percentile of their ultimate resistance or target displacement in accordance with
engineering principles of equilibrium and displacement compatibility. Alternatively, the seismic design
force may be determined using Rd Ro = 1.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 406: 11.9.3.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.3.3.1 General
Where shearwall overturning restraint devices are required, discrete hold-downs or continuous steel
rods shall be designed to transfer the forces in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.3.3.2 or 11.9.3.3.3.3,
respectively.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 407: 11.9.3.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.3.3.2 Discrete hold-downs
The factored resistance of discrete hold-downs shall be at least 20% greater than the forces developed
in them when the connections between CLT segments reach their nominal resistance.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 408: 11.9.3.3.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.3.3.3 Continuous steel rods
Continuous steel rods used as hold-downs shall be anchored at each floor level and designed in
accordance with CSA S16 to remain elastic while allowing for the expected uplift due to overturning of
the shearwalls.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 409: 11.9.3.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.4.1 Energy-dissipative connections
Energy-dissipative connections shall be designed in accordance with the requirements in
Clause 11.9.3.3.1 to ensure that all principle inelastic deformations and principle energy dissipation
occurs in
a) connections between vertical joints of adjacent shearwall segments; and
b) shear connections of shearwalls to foundations, and shearwalls to floors beneath, in uplift only.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 410: 11.9.3.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.4.2 CLT panels
CLT panels that are part of the SFRS shall be capacity-protected by designing them for seismic forces
that are developed when energy-dissipative connections in shearwalls reach the 95th percentile of their
ultimate resistance. Alternatively, the seismic design force may be determined using Rd Ro 1.3.
Note: The in-plane shear resistance of the CLT panels is provided by the product manufacturer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 411: 11.9.3.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.5.1 Minimum shearwall thickness
CLT shearwalls shall have a minimum thickness of 87 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 412: 11.9.3.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.5.2 Permitted aspect ratio of shearwall segments
Except as permitted in Clause 11.9.3.2.2, all CLT shearwall segments considered part of the SFRS shall
have an aspect ratio of not less than 2:1 and not greater than 4:1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 413: 11.9.3.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.5.3 Panel aspect ratios less than 2:1
Except as permitted in Clause 11.9.3.2.2, CLT panels with aspect ratios less than 2:1 may be divided and
re-joined with energy-dissipative connections in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.3.1 to form shearwall
segments in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.5.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 414: 11.9.3.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.5.4 Openings in shearwalls
Parts of shearwalls interrupted by openings shall not be considered part of the SFRS.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 415: 11.9.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.6 Deflections of CLT shearwalls
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 416: 11.9.3.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.6.1 General
Deflections of shearwalls shall be determined using established methods of mechanics. Calculations
shall account for the main sources of shearwall deformations, such as panel rocking, connection
stiffness, and deformation of supports.
Note: Deflections determined in this Clause are used to confirm displacement compatibility of the energy-dissipative
and non-dissipative connections in Clause 11.9.3.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 417: 11.9.3.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.6.2 Limitation on flexural deformations
CLT shearwalls shall be designed so that the lateral deflection due to flexural deformations shall not
exceed 30% of the total lateral deflection at the top of the building.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 418: 11.9.3.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.7.1 CLT panels and connections
The CLT panels in the diaphragms shall be capacity protected in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.4.2. The
shear connections that connect the diaphragms to the walls beneath and the connections between
adjacent diaphragm panels shall be non-dissipative and designed in accordance with Clause 11.9.3.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 419: 11.9.3.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.7.2 Compressive resistance perpendicular to the face of the CLT panels
(bearing)
The compressive resistance perpendicular to the face of the diaphragm at locations where vertical
overturning forces are transferred from the walls shall be calculated in accordance with Clause 8.4.7
and shall be greater than or equal to the overturning forces calculated using methods of mechanics.
Note: See the CWC Commentary on CSA O86 for further information.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 420: 11.9.3.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.3.7.3 Force-transfer elements
Diaphragm chords, struts, and other force-transfer elements, including those around openings, shall be
capacity protected. They shall remain elastic under the force and displacement demands that are
