induced in them when the energy-dissipative connections that are connecting them to the seismic-force-resisting
system reach the 95th percentile of their ultimate resistance or the design target
displacement.
Note: The seismic design force is permitted to be taken as not greater than the force determined using Rd Ro = 1.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 421: 11.9.4 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.4 Members not considered part of the SFRS
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 422: 11.9.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.4.1 General
Clause 11.9.4 applies to all members of the structure not considered part of the SFRS unless the building
is located where the Seismic Category is SC1 or SC2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 423: 11.9.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.4.2 Non-structural elements
Elements not required to resist either gravity or lateral loading shall be considered non-structural and
are not required to be detailed for the effect of seismic loads provided that
a) the effects of non-structural elements are accounted for in the design of structural elements if the
non-structural elements increase the seismically induced deformation of, or the forces applied to, a
structural element; and
b) the non-structural elements are attached to the building in accordance with the National Building
Code of Canada, Article 4.1.8.18.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 424: 11.9.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
11.9.4.3 Gravity-load-resisting systems
All structural elements that are not considered part of the SFRS shall have the resistance and
displacement capability to support their gravity loads while undergoing seismically-induced
deformations calculated in accordance with the National Building Code, Article 4.1.8.13.
Note: Gravity-load-resisting members not part of the seismic-force-resisting system may be designed to behave
linearly or non-linearly.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 425: 12.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.1 Connections Scope
Clause 12 specifies criteria for the engineering design and appraisal of connections using split-ring and
shear-plate connectors, bolts, dowels, drift pins, lag screws, wood screws, timber rivets, truss plates,
nails, spikes, and joist hangers.
Note: The lateral resistance values for bolts, dowels, drift pins, lag screws, nails, spikes, and wood screws are
based on the relative density of the wood material. Relative density values are given in Table A.11.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 426: 12.2.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.1 General
The requirements in Clause 12 related to fasteners in the side grain of the members shall apply equally
to those in the panel face of CLT, unless specified otherwise. The angle of loading shall be measured
relative to the grain in wood members or in the outer laminations on the panel face of CLT. Special
provisions for fasteners installed in the end grain and in the panel edge (narrow face) of CLT shall be
applied.
Note: Connection details where shrinkage of the wood can lead to excessive tension perpendicular to grain stress
should be avoided.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 427: 12.2.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.2 Connection assembly
Connections shall be assembled so that the surfaces are brought into close contact.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 428: 12.2.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.3 Minimum end distance
The tables in Clause 12 are predicated on the requirement that the projecting end of a member shall
not be trimmed or otherwise altered in a manner that reduces the specified minimum end distance.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 429: 12.2.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.4 Conditions conducive to corrosion
Under severe conditions conducive to corrosion, connection design shall provide protection against
corrosion.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 430: 12.2.1.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.5 Connections made using hardwoods
Connections made using hard maple, soft maple, elm, beech, black oak, white oak, or birch may be
assigned the same resistances as the Douglas Fir-Larch species combination.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 431: 12.2.1.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.6 Shear depth at connections
Where a fastener or group of fasteners exerts a shear force on a member, the factored shear resistance
of the member, calculated in accordance with Clauses 6.5.4 for sawn lumber and Clause 7.5.7 for
glulam, shall be based on the shear depth de shown in Figure 12.1, instead of the full depth d. The shear
depth de is the distance, measured perpendicular to the axis of the member, from the extremity of the
fastener or group of fasteners to the loaded edge of the member.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 432: 12.2.1.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.7.1 Load-duration factor, KD
The load-duration factor, KD, for connections shall be as specified in Clause 5.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 433: 12.2.1.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.7.2 Service-condition factors, KSF
The service-condition factors for connections, KSF, shall be as specified in Table 12.1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 434: 12.2.1.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.1.7.3 Treatment factor, KT
For connections containing members treated with fire-retardant or other strength-reducing chemicals,
the strength resistance of connections shall be based on the documented results of tests that shall take
into account the effects of time, temperature, and moisture content in accordance with Clause 4.3.2.
Note: The effects of fire-retardant treatments can vary depending on manufacturing materials and processes.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 435: 12.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2 Split-ring and shear-plate connectors, bolts, dowels, and lag screws
Note: Clause 12.2.2 provides general requirements for connections with split-ring and shear-plate connectors,
bolts, dowels, and lag screws. Specific requirements are provided in Clause 12.3 for connections with split-ring and
shear-plate connectors, in Clause 12.4 for connections with bolts and dowels, and in Clause 12.6 for connections
with lag screws.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 436: 12.2.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.1 Inspection and tightening
Structures that have been assembled with unseasoned or partially seasoned wood members shall be
inspected regularly at intervals not exceeding six months until it becomes apparent that further wood
shrinkage will not be appreciable. At each inspection, the fasteners shall be tightened to bring the faces
of the connected members into close contact without deformation.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 437: 12.2.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.2 Grooves, daps, and holes
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 438: 12.2.2.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.2.1 Grooves, daps, and holes in wood members
Grooves, daps, and holes in wood members shall be fabricated and oriented accurately in the
contacting faces. Bolt holes in wood members shall be accurately aligned and drilled not less than
1.0 mm and not more than 2.0 mm larger than the bolt diameter. Pre-drilled holes in connections with
dowels shall have a diameter not greater than the dowel diameter. Lag-screw holes shall be drilled in
accordance with Clause 12.6.2.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 439: 12.2.2.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.2.2 Holes in steel plates
Holes in steel plates shall be accurately placed to line up with holes in the adjoining wood and shall not
be more than 2 mm larger than the diameter of the fastener.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 440: 12.2.2.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.3.1 General
A group of fasteners consists of one or more rows of fasteners of the same type and size arranged
symmetrically with respect to the axis of the load (see Clauses 12.3.3, 12.4.3, and 12.6.2).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 441: 12.2.2.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.3.2 Row of fasteners
A row of fasteners consists of one or more fasteners of the same type and size aligned with the
direction of the load.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 442: 12.2.2.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.3.3 Multiple rows of fasteners
When fasteners in adjacent rows are staggered and the spacing between adjacent rows is less than one-quarter
the spacing between the closest fasteners in adjacent rows measured parallel to the rows, the
adjacent rows shall be considered as one row to determine the resistance of the group. For a group of
fasteners having an even number of rows, this principle shall apply to each pair. For a group of fasteners
having an odd number of rows, the more conservative interpretation shall apply.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 443: 12.2.2.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.3.4 Group action factor, JG
The group action factor, JG, for split-ring, shear-plate, and lag-screw connections shall be as specified in
Tables 12.2 and 12.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 444: 12.2.2.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.4.1 General
A standard cut washer or its equivalent (see Table 12.4), or a metal strap of the same thickness as the
washer, shall be placed between the wood and the fastener head and between the wood and the nut.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 445: 12.2.2.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.4.2 Steel plates
When a bolt or lag-screw head or nut bears directly on a steel plate, washers may be omitted.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 446: 12.2.2.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.4.3 Washers for axially loaded fasteners
Bolts or lag screws in axial tension or with a calculated tension component shall be provided with steel
plate washers, standard ogee washers, or malleable iron washers under heads and nuts. The area of
these washers shall be such that the bearing stress on the wood under the washer does not exceed the
factored resistance in compression perpendicular to grain. If steel washers are used, the thickness shall
not be less than one-tenth the diameter or one-tenth the length of the longer side of the washer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 447: 12.2.2.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.5.1 General
The net section of wood members in connections made using bolts, dowels, lag screws, and split-ring
and shear-plate connectors shall be checked in accordance with Clause 5.3.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 448: 12.2.2.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.5.2 Staggered bolts, dowels, and lag screws
For a connection under parallel-to-grain loading, staggered adjacent bolts, dowels, or lag screws shall be
considered to be placed at the critical section unless their spacing centre-to-centre parallel to grain is
more than 8dF.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 449: 12.2.2.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.2.2.5.3 Split-ring and shear-plate connectors
For connections using timber split-ring and shear-plate connectors, the area deducted from the gross
section shall include the projected area of that portion of the connectors within the member and that
portion of the bolt hole not within the connector projected area, located at the critical plane. Where
connectors are staggered, adjacent connectors shall be considered as occurring in the same critical
transverse plane unless their spacing parallel to grain is more than two connector diameters.

--------------------------------------------------
Clause 450: 12.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.3 Split-ring and shear-plate connectors
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 451: 12.3.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.1.1 Connector unit
For specifying connection resistance in this Standard, aconnector unit shall consist of one ofthe
following, in any connection of any number of members:
a) one split ring with abolt or alag screw;
b) one shear plate with abolt or alag screw, used with asteel strap or plate in a wood-to-metal
connection; or
c) two shear plates used back-to-back in the contact faces of awood-to-wood connection with abolt
or alag screw.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 452: 12.3.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.1.2 Split-ring connectors
The tabulated resistances and design methods for split-ring connectors specified in Clause 12.3 are for
split rings that have dimensions in accordance with Table 12.5A and are manufactured from hot-rolled
carbon steel, SAE 1010, meeting the requirements ofthe SAE Handbook. Each ring shall form aclosed
true circle with the principal axis ofthe cross-section ofthe ring metal parallel to the geometric axis of
the ring. The ring shall be beveled from the central portion toward the edges to athickness less than
that at midsection so that it will fit snugly in aprecut groove; alternatively, another means that achieves
equivalent performance may be used. The ring shall be cut through in one place in its circumference to
form atongue and slot.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 453: 12.3.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.1.3 Shear-plate connectors
The tabulated resistances and design methods are for shear-plate connectors specified in Clause 12.3
are for shear plates that have dimensions in accordance with Table 12.5B and meet the requirements of
Item a) or b):
a) Pressed steel type: pressed steel shear plates manufactured from hot-rolled carbon steel,
SAE 1010, meeting the requirements ofthe SAE Handbook. Each plate shall be atrue circle with a
flange around the edge, extending atright angles to the face ofthe plate from one face only. The
plate portion shall have acentral hole and two small perforations on diametrically opposite sides of
the hole, each midway from the centre and circumference.
b) Malleable iron type: malleable iron shear plates manufactured in accordance with ASTM A47,
Grade 32510 (or ASTM A47M, Grade 22010). Each casting shall consist of aperforated round plate
with aflange extending atright angles to the face ofthe plate and projecting from one face only.
The plate portion shall have acentral bolt hole, reamed to size where required, with an integral
hub concentric to the bolt hole and extending from the same face asthe flange.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 454: 12.3.1.4
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.1.4 Connector Grooves
Connector grooves shall have the dimensions specified in the Tables 12.6A abd 12.6B for split rings and shear plates respectively.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 455: 12.3.2
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.2 Sevice-condition factors, KSf
The service-condition factors, Ksf, specified in Table 12.1 are based on the moisture content within a depth of 20 mm from the connected surface.

Clause 456: 12.3.3
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.3 Configuration factors, Jc
Connectors installed at any edge distance, end distance, or spacing less than the minimum for which a
tabulated value appears in the appropriate columns of Tables 12.7 to 12.9 shall not be considered to
provide resistance. Configuration factors, JC, for edge distance, end distance, and spacing shall be
separately determined and the lowest factor so determined for any one connector shall be applied to all
connectors resisting a common force in a connection (see Figures 12.2 and 12.3).
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 457: 12.3.4
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.4 Thickness factor, JT
For connectors installed in dimension lumber, thickness factor, Jₜ, specified in Table 12.10 shall be applied.
Connectors installed in lumber of a thickness less than the minimum specified in Table 12.10 for the connector type and use shall not be considered to provide resistance.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 458: 12.3.5
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.5 Connectors used with lag screws
When lag screws instead of bolts are used with connectors, the resistance shall vary uniformly with 
penetration into the point-side member, from the full resistance for one connector unit with bolt for 
standard penetration to 0.75 times the full resistance for one connector unit with bolt for minimum 
penetration. Penetration shall be as specified in Table 12.11 and shall not be less than the minimum 
value.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 459: 12.3.6
--------------------------------------------------
12.3.6 Lateral resistance

The factored lateral strength resistance of a split-ring or shear-plate connection, P_r, Q_r, or N_r,
determined using the equations specified in this Clause, shall be greater than or equal to the effect
of the factored loads. The factored strength resistance per shear-plate unit shall not exceed the values
specified in Table 12.14.

a) For parallel-to-grain loading:
   P_r = φ * P_u * n_F * J_F

b) For perpendicular-to-grain loading:
   Q_r = φ * Q_u * n_F * J_F

c) For loads at angle θ to grain:
   N_r = (P * Q_r) / (P * sin²θ + Q_r * cos²θ)

where:
  φ    = 0.6
  P_u  = p_u * (K_D * K_SF * K_T)
    where:
      p_u = lateral strength resistance parallel to grain, kN (see Table 12.12)

  n_F  = number of connector units in the connection

  J_F  = J_G * J_C * J_T * J_O * J_P
    where:
      J_G = group action factor (see Clause 12.2.2.3.4)
      J_C = minimum configuration factor (see Clause 12.3.3)
      J_T = thickness factor (see Table 12.10)
      J_O = factor for connector orientation in grain
         = 1.00 for side grain installation  
        = 0.67 for end grain and all other installations  
        J_P = penetration factor for lag screw (see Clause 12.3.5)  

Q_u = q_u (K_D · K_SF · K_T)  
  where:  
  q_u = lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain, kN (see Table 12.13)

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 460: 12.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.1 General Bolts and Dowels
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.4 apply to metallic bolts and dowels whose material
properties are referenced by aCanadian material design standard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 461: 12.4.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.2.1 Wood members
The resistance of wood members in aconnection shall be determined in accordance with Clause 12.4.4.
The bearing length offasteners in wood members, ti, shall be the lesser ofthe thinnest wood member
orthe smallest bearing length shown in Figure 12.4.
Note: To avoid eccentricity in loading, side members should be ofthe same thickness.2-5/8 in
shear plate 3/4 in bolt 7/8 in bolt


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 462: 12.4.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.2.2 Metal plates
When aconnection consists of a mixture of wood members and metal plates, only metal plates with
engineering design specifications in accordance with aCanadian structural design or material standard
shall be used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 463: 12.4.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.2.3 Concrete or masonry
When aconnection consists of a wood member attached to concrete or masonry, the connection shall
be designed as atwo-member connection in accordance with the equations in Clause 12.4.4. The wood
member shall be considered the side member. The concrete or masonry member shall be assumed to
have athickness equal to the penetration ofthe bolt in the concrete or masonry. The concrete or
masonry shall be designed to resist the applied loads.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 464: 12.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.3 Placement of bolts and dowels in connections
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 465: 12.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.3.1 Load component parallel to grain
In agroup offasteners where the load component is acting parallel to the grain, including those in the
panel face of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as specified in Table 12.15 (see
Figure 12.5).t1bt1b
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 466: 12.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.3.2 Load component perpendicular to grain
In agroup offasteners where the load component is acting perpendicular to the grain, including those
in the panel face of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as specified in Table 12.16 (see
Figure 12.6).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 467: 12.4.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.3.3 Placement ofbolts and dowels in the panel edge of CLT
In agroup offasteners installed in the panel edge of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as
specified in Table 12.17 (see Figure 12.7).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 468: 12.4.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.3.4 Maximum distance perpendicular to grain
Except for connections in CLT, asingle steel splice plate shall not be used for rows of bolts or dowels
when the distance between the two outer rows exceeds 125 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 469: 12.4.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.1 Potential failure modes
Connections shall be designed to resist all possible yielding and brittle failure modes associated with the
fasteners and material used as shown in Figure 12.8.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 470: 12.4.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.2 Requirements
Connections shall be designed in accordance with the following requirements:
a) Nf<Nr
where
Nf =factored load on the connection
Nr =factored lateral yielding resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.3.1)
b) Pf<Pr
where
Pf =factored load parallel to grain
Pr =factored resistance parallel to grain
   = the lesser of PRrT, PGrT, or TNrT
where
PRrT =factored row shear resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.4)
PGrT =factored group tear-out resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.5)
TNrT =factored net tension resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.6.1)
c) Qf<Qr
where
Qf =factored load perpendicular to grain
Qr = QSrT
where
QSrT =factored splitting resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.7)
d) for loading at an angle to grain, θ:
N_f ≤ (P_r * Q_r) / (P_r * sin²θ + Q_r * cos²θ)

where
θ = angle between the applied load and the grain
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 471: 12.4.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.3.1 General
The factored lateral yielding resistance, Nr, of agroup offasteners in aconnection is afunction ofthe
number ofshear planes and shall be calculated asfollows:
Nr = φy nu ns nF
where
φy=resistance factor for yielding failures
  = 0.8
nu=unit lateral yielding resistance per shear plane, N(see Clause 12.4.4.3.2)
ns=number ofshear planes inthe connection
nF = number offasteners in the connection
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 472: 12.4.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.3.2 Unit lateral yielding resistance
The unit lateral yielding resistance per shear plane, nu, shall be taken as the smallest value calculated in
accordance with Items a)to g). For two-member connections, only Items a), b), and d)to g)shall be
considered valid. For three-member connections, only Items a), c), d), and g) shall be considered valid.
For aconnection with four or more members, the resistance shall be determined by assuming that each
member is part of aseries ofthree-member connections.
a)  f₁ d_f t₁  
b)  f₂ d_f t₂  
c)  (1/2) f₂ d_f t₂  
d)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₁ / (5 d_f)))]  
e)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₂ / (5 d_f)))]  
f)  f₁ d_f² * (2/5) * [(t₁ / d_f) + (f₂ t₂) / (f₁ d_f)]  
g)  f₁ d_f² * √[(2/3) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁)]

where
dF = nominal diameter offastener, mm
t1, t2 = bearing length offastener in members 1and 2in accordance with Clause 12.4.2.1, mm
f1, f2 = embedment strengthof member 1 and 2 calculated in accordance with Clause 12.4.4.3.3
        where member 1 is the side member, MPa
fy =yield strength offastener in bending in accordance with Clause 12.4.4.3.3.3, MPa
where member 1is the side member, MPa
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 473: 12.4.4.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.3.3.1 Wood members
For fasteners installed in the side grain, the embedment strength fi, in MPa, shall be calculated as
follows:
f_ih = (f_ip * f_iq) / (f_ip * sin²θ + f_iq * cos²θ) * (K_D * K_SF * K_T)

Where:
f_ih = embedment strength of member i for a fastener bearing at angle θ relative to the grain
f_ip = embedment strength for a fastener bearing parallel to grain (θ = 0°)
     = 50 * G * (1 − 0.01 * d_f) * J_X

Where:
  G  = mean relative density (see Table A.11)
  J_X = adjustment factor for connections in CLT
      = 0.9 for CLT
      = 1.0 for other wood members

f_iq = embedment strength for a fastener bearing perpendicular to grain (θ = 90°)
     = 22 * (1 − 0.01 * d_f)

θ    = angle of bearing relative to the grain
K_D  = load-duration factor in accordance with Clause 5.3.2
K_SF = service-condition factor in accordance with Clause 12.2.1.7.2
K_T  = treatment factor in accordance with Clause 12.2.1.7.3

For fasteners installed in the panel edge of CLT, the embedment strength in any loading direction, f_ih,
shall not be greater than 0.6 * f_iq * (K_D * K_SF * K_T) of the fasteners installed perpendicular to the panel face.

Note: The values of f_ih are applicable to the entire dowel-bearing length of the fastener.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 474: 12.4.4.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.3.3.2 Non-wood materials
The embedment strength, fi, of non-wood materials shall be calculated as follows:
a) for steel:
fi=Ksp (φsteel /φy) fu
where
Ksp= 3.0 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
    =2.25 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136
fu =specified minimum tensile strength ofsteel, MPa
Note: The specified minimum tensile strength of steel, fu, is given in the relevant material standards, e.g.,
a)fu =400 MPa for ASTM A36/A36M steel;
b)fu =450 MPa for CSA G40.21 steel, Grades 300W and 350W; and
c)fu =310 MPa for cold-formed light-gauge steel, Grade SS 230.


φsteel = resistance factor for steel plates in connections with bolts and dowels
    = 0.8 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
    =0.5 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136

φy =resistance factor for yielding failures in wood members in connections with bolts and
dowels
    = 0.8
b) for concrete or masonry:
fi=125 MPa
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 475: 12.4.4.3.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.3.3.3 Dowel or bolt yield strength
The yield strength, fy, ofadowel orbolt shall betaken asfollows:
a) for ASTM A307 and SAE J429 Grade 2fasteners:
fy =310 MPa; or
b) for other CSA-or ASTM-compliant fasteners:

fyy = (fym+fum)/2
where
fym=specified yield strength obtained from applicable material standards, MPa
fum=specified tensile strength obtained from applicable material standards, MPa
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 476: 12.4.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.4 Row shear resistance
The total factored shear resistance, PRrT, of aconnection shall be calculated as the sum ofthe factored
row shear resistances ofthe wood members resisting the load, asfollows:
PR_T = Σ (PR_Ri)

The total factored row shear resistance of fasteners in a wood member i shall be calculated as follows:

PR_Ri = φ_w * PR_ij_min * n_R

where:
  φ_w        = resistance factor for brittle failures
             = 0.7
  PR_ij_min  = minimum row shear resistance of any row in the connection from PR_i1 to PR_inR
  n_R        = number of fastener rows
  PR_ij      = shear resistance of fastener row j in member i, N

PR_ij = 1.2 * f_v * (K_D * K_SV * K_T) * K_is * t * n_c * α_cri

Where:
  f_v     = specified longitudinal shear strength of member i, MPa
          = value specified in Tables 6.4, 6.6, 6.7, or 7.2
          = 0.6 × value specified in Table 6.5
  K_is    = factor for member loaded surfaces (see Figure 12.9)
          = 0.65 for side member
          = 1.0 for internal member
  t       = thickness of member i, mm
  n_c     = number of fasteners in row j of member i
  α_cri   = minimum of α_L and S_p for row j of member i, mm (see Figure 12.5)
  K_SV    = service-condition factor for longitudinal shear (see Tables 6.10 and 7.3)


The row shear resistance of each member shall be checked separately. For CLT, the row shear failure is
not required to be considered.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 477: 12.4.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.5 Group tear-out resistance
The total factored group tear-out resistance, PGrT, of aconnection shall be calculated as the sum ofthe
factored group tear-out resistance ofthe wood members resisting the load, asfollows:
PG_T = Σ (PG_Ri)

The factored group tear-out resistance of wood member i, in N, shall be calculated as follows:

PG_Ri = φ_w * [((PR_i1 + PR_inR) / 2) + f_ti * (K_D * K_ST * K_T) * A_PGi]

Where:
  φ_w     = resistance factor for brittle failures
          = 0.7

  PR_i1   = shear resistance of wood member i along row 1 bounding the fastener group, N
          = 1.2 * f_vi * (K_D * K_SV * K_T) * K_is * t * n_c1 * α_cr1

  PR_inR  = shear resistance along row n_R of member i bounding the fastener group, N
          = 1.2 * f_vi * (K_D * K_SV * K_T) * K_is * t * n_cR * α_crnR

  f_ti    = specified strength in tension parallel to grain of member i, MPa
          = value specified in Table 6.4, 6.6, or 6.7
          = value for net section specified in Table 7.2
          = 0.65 × values specified in Table 6.5
    Kst=service-condition factor for tension parallel to grain (see Tables 6.10 and 7.3)
    KSv=service-condition factor for tension parallel tograin (see Tables 6.10 and 7.3)
    APGi = critical perpendicular net area between rows 1and nR of member i, mm2

The group tear-out resistance of each member in tension shall be checked separately. For CLT, group
tear-out failure is not required to be considered. Group tear-out failure is not required to be considered
if the load is applied in such away that the member isin compression (see Figure 12.8).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 478: 12.4.4.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.6.1 General
The total factored net tension resistance, TNrT, of wood members loaded parallel to grain at agroup of
fasteners shall be calculated asfollows:
TNrT =Σ TNr i
TNr iof member iat agroup offasteners shall be determined using Clause 6.5.8 for sawn lumber and
Clause 7.5.11 for glulam.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 479: 12.4.4.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.6.2 Net section of wood member atthe connection
The cross-sectional area deducted from the gross cross-section shall not be greater than 25% ofthe
member gross area in accordance with Clause 5.3.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 480: 12.4.4.7 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.4.7 Splitting resistance
The total factored splitting resistance, QSrT, of aconnection shall be calculated as the sum ofthe
splitting resistances ofthe wood members resisting the load as follows:
QSrT =Σ QSri
The factored splitting resistance of wood member i,in N,shall be calculated as follows:
QS_Ri = φ_w * QS_i * (K_D * K_SF * K_T)

Where:
  φ_w = resistance factor for brittle failures
      = 0.7

  QS_i = 14t * sqrt(d_e / (1 - d_e / d))

Where:
  t   = member thickness, mm
  d_e = effective depth of member, mm
      = d - e_p

Where:
  d   = depth of member, mm
  e_p = unloaded edge distance, mm

The splitting resistance is not required to be considered for fasteners installed in the panel face of CLT
and loaded perpendicular to the panel face, but it shall be checked for fasteners installed in the panel
edge of CLT.
Note: See Clause 12.2.1.6 for member shear resistance based on effective depth.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 481: 12.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.5 Axial resistance
Bolts shall be designed to resist the load component parallel to their axis. Washers or plates shall be
designed to resist the factored load component parallel to the axis ofthe bolt. Dowels shall not be
designed to resist axial loads.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 482: 12.4.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.4.6 Combined lateral and axial resistance
The resistance of bolts subjected to lateral and axial loading shall be verified in accordance with the
applicable Canadian material design standard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 483: 12.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.1 General Drift Pins
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.5 apply to cribwork connections with drift pins with a
diameter of 16 to 25 mm and meeting the requirements of CSA G40.21 or ASTM A307.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 484: 12.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.2 Pre-drilled holes
Holes in timber shall be pre-drilled not less than 0.8 mm and not more than 1 mm smaller than the
drift-pin diameter.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 485: 12.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.3 Drift-pin points
The leading end of drift pins shall be chisel-pointed, conically tapered, and hemispherical or otherwise
shaped to permit driving into pre-drilled holes with minimum damage to the wood.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 486: 12.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.4 Axial tension
Drift-pin connections shall be used only where gravity or mechanical restraint prevents axial tensile
stress in the drift pins.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 487: 12.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.5 Size and placement of drift pins in connections
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 488: 12.5.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.5.1 Drift-pin length
Drift-pin length shall be equal to the sum ofthe depths oftwo superimposed members to be
connected, less 15 mm. Each drift pin shall be considered to give one shear plane. Figure 12.10 shows a
typical drift-pin connection in timber cribwork.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 489: 12.5.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.5.2 Drift-pin diameter
The drift-pin diameter shall not be greater than one-tenth ofthe width ofthe timbers to be connected.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 490: 12.5.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.5.3 End and edge distances
End and edge distances shall be atleast 2.5 times the pin diameter.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 491: 12.5.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.5.4 Spacing
Spacing between pins parallel and perpendicular to the grain shall be atleast four times the pin
diameter.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 492: 12.5.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.5.6 Lateral resistance
The factored lateral strength resistance, P_r, Q_r, or N_r, of a drift-pin connection shall be greater than or
equal to the effect of the factored loads and shall be calculated as follows:

a) For parallel-to-grain loading, P_r shall be the lesser of:
   - 0.6 * PR_T
   - 0.6 * PG_T
   - 0.6 * TN_T

b) For perpendicular-to-grain loading:
   - Q_r shall be 0.6 * QS_T

c) For loads at angle θ to grain:
   - N_r shall be as follows:
     N_r = (P_r * Q_r) / (P_r * sin²θ + Q_r * cos²θ)

Where:
  PR_T  = factored row shear resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.4)
  PG_T  = factored group tear-out resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.5)
  TN_T  = factored net tension resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.6)
  QS_T  = factored splitting resistance (see Clause 12.4.4.7)

Note:
At any shear plane between two overlapping timbers, as shown in Figure 12.10, only two pins shall be
counted as resisting the shear force.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 493: 12.6.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.1.1 Lag Screws Materials
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.6 apply to two-member connections with lag screws
that meet the requirements of ASME B18.2.1 and are made of steel that meets or exceeds the
properties of ASTM A307 Grade Aor SAE J429 Grade 1.
Note: For the use of alternate dowel-type self-drilling fasteners, see the CWC Commentary on CSA O86.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 494: 12.6.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.1.2 Connection assembly
The threaded portion ofthe lag screw shall be inserted by turning with awrench or other similar tool,
not by driving. Care shall be exercised to avoid over-tightening the lag screws during installation.
Note: If over-tightened, the lag screw will not have withdrawal resistance specified in this Standard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 495: 12.6.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.1.3 Facilitating connection assembly
Soap or other non-petroleum-based lubricant may be used on the lag screws orin the lead hole to
facilitate insertion and prevent damage to the lag screw.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 496: 12.6.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.1.4 Net section of wood member atthe connection
The cross-sectional area deducted from the gross cross-section shall not be greater than 25% ofthe
member gross area in accordance with Clause 5.3.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 497: 12.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2 Placement oflag screws in connections
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 498: 12.6.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2.1 Load component parallel to grain
In agroup offasteners where the load component is acting parallel to the grain, including those in the
panel face of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as specified in Table 12.18 [see
Figure 12.11 a)].
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 499: 12.6.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2.2 Load component perpendicular to grain
In agroup offasteners where the load component is acting perpendicular to the grain, including those
in the panel face of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as specified in Table 12.19 [see
Figure 12.11 b)].

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 500: 12.6.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2.3 Placement oflag screws in the panel edge of CLT
For lag screws in the panel edge of CLT, the minimum fastener spacing, as specified in Clause 12.4.3.3,
shall be used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 501: 12.6.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2.4 Maximum distance perpendicular to grain
Except for connections in CLT, asingle steel splice plate shall not be used for rows oflag screws when
the distance between the two outer rows exceeds 125 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 502: 12.6.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.2.5 Lag screw holes
Lag screw holes in wood members shall consist ofthe clearance hole and lead hole meeting the
following requirements:
a) The clearance hole for the unthreaded portion ofthe shank shall have the same diameter, dF, and
the same depth asthe penetration length ofthe unthreaded shank.
b) The lead hole for the threaded portion ofthe shank shall have adiameter equal to 0.65dF to 0.85dF
for dense hardwoods, 0.60dF to 0.75dF for Douglas Fir-Larch, and 0.40dF to 0.70dF for less dense
wood. The larger lead-hole diameter in each range shall apply to lag screws ofthe greater
diameters. The length ofthe lead hole shall fit the threaded portion ofthe lag screw.
Note: Lead holes for the threaded portion are not required for 10 mm and smaller diameter lag screws loaded
primarily in withdrawal in wood with relative density, G 0.5, if the fasteners are placed so asto prevent unusual
splitting.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 503: 12.6.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.3 Penetration length oflag screws
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 504: 12.6.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.3.1 Penetration length
For determining the penetration length ofalag screw into a member, the length ofthe tapered tip of
the threaded shank shall not be included.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 505: 12.6.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.3.2 Maximum penetration length
Unless the tensile resistance ofthe lag screw atthe net (root) section is verified (see Clause 12.6.6.2),
the maximum length ofthreaded shank penetration into the point-side member (Lt in Clause 12.6.6.1)
used to determine withdrawal resistance shall not exceed the following values:
a) for Douglas Fir-Larch: 9dF;
b) for Hem-Fir: 10dF;
c) for Spruce-Pine-Fir and Northern Species: 11dF; and
d) for denser species: determined based on the tensile resistance offasteners (see Clause 12.6.6.2).
Note: For lag screws loaded laterally, the same limits on the maximum length ofpenetration into main member (t2
in Clause 12.6.5.1.2) may be used, because further increasing the length of alag screw does not increase either the
strength orstiffness ofthe connection.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 506: 12.6.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.3.3 Minimum penetration length
For lag screws loaded laterally, the minimum length of penetration into the point-side member (t2 in
Clause 12.6.5.1.2) shall be not less than 5dF.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 507: 12.6.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.4.1 Wood side members
The thickness of wood side members shall be atleast 2dF.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 508: 12.6.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.4.2 Steel side plates
The stresses induced in the steel side plate and atthe bearing ofthe fastener on the plate shall not
exceed the resistance ofthe steel used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 509: 12.6.5.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.5.1.1 Lateral Side Grain General
The factored lateral strength resistance, Pr, Qr, or Nr, of atwo-member lag-screw connection shall be
greater than or equal to the effect ofthe factored loads and shall be calculated asfollows:
a) for parallel-to-grain loading:
Pr= PunFJG JPL
b) for perpendicular-to-grain loading:
Qr = Qu nFJG JPL
c) For loads at angle θ to grain:

N_r = (P_r * Q_r) / (P_r * sin²θ + Q_r * cos²θ)

Where:
  φ    = 0.6
  P_u  = p_u * (K_D * K_SF * K_T)
    where:
      p_u = unit lateral strength resistance for parallel-to-grain loading, N (see Clause 12.6.5.1.2)
  n_F  = number of fasteners in the connection
  J_G  = group-action factor (see Tables 12.2 and 12.3)
  J_PL = factor for reduced penetration
      =0.625 for penetration of5dF and 1.0for 8dF (for intermediate values, interpolate linearly)
Qu=qu(KD KSF KT)
qu =unit lateral strength resistance for perpendicular-to-grain loading, N(see
Clause 12.6.5.1.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 510: 12.6.5.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.5.1.2 12.6.5.1.2 Unit lateral strength resistance
The unit lateral strength resistances, pu or qu, shall be taken as the smallest value determined as
follows:
a)  f₁ d_f t₁  
b)  f₂ d_f t₂  
c)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₁ / (5 d_f)))]  
d)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₂ / (5 d_f)))]  
e)  f₁ d_f² * (1/5) * [(t₁ / d_f) + (f₂ t₂) / (f₁ d_f)]  
f)  f₁ d_f² * √[(2/3) * (f₂ / (f₁ + f₂)) * (f_y / f₁)]

Where:
  d_f = nominal diameter of lag screw, mm
  t₁  = thickness of side member, mm (see Clause 12.6.4)
  t₂  = length of penetration into main member, mm (see Clause 12.6.3)
  f₁  = embedment strength of side member, MPa
  f₂  = embedment strength of wood main member, MPa

For wood side members:
  f₁ = f₂ = 50G (1 − 0.01 d_f) * Jₓ for parallel-to-grain loading
  f₂ = 22G (1 − 0.01 d_f) for perpendicular-to-grain loading

Where:
  G  = mean relative density (see Table A.11)
  Jₓ = 0.90 for CLT
    = 1.0 for other wood members

For steel side plates:
  f₁ = K_sp * (φ_steel / φ_wood) * f_u

Where:
  K_sp     = 3.0 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
           = 2.25 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136

  f_u      = specified minimum tensile strength of steel

Note: The specified minimum tensile strength of steel, f_u, is given in the relevant material standards, e.g.:
  a) f_u = 400 MPa for ASTM A36/A36M steel
  b) f_u = 450 MPa for CSA G40.21 steel, Grades 300W and 350W
  c) f_u = 310 MPa for cold-formed light-gauge steel, Grade SS 230

  φ_steel  = resistance factor for steel plates in connections with lag screws
           = 0.8 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
           = 0.5 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136

  φ_wood   = resistance factor for wood members in connections with lag screws
           = 0.6

  f_y      = yield strength of fastener in bending, MPa
           = 310 MPa for lag screws meeting SAE J429 Grade 1
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 511: 12.6.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.5.2 End grain
The lateral resistance oflag screws inserted parallel to grain in the end grain ofthe main member shall
not be greater than two-thirds ofthe lateral side grain resistance for perpendicular to grain if wood side
plates are used. Ifsteel side plates are used, the lateral resistance shall not be greater than one-half of
the lateral side grain resistance for perpendicular-to-grain loading in the main member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 512: 12.6.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.5.3 Panel edge of CLT
The lateral resistance oflag screws inserted in panel edge of CLT shall not be greater than two-thirds of
the lateral resistance for perpendicular to grain oflaminations in the panel face if wood side plates are
used, or one-half ifsteel side plates are used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 513: 12.6.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.5.4 12.6.5.4 Connection deformation
Where required for design, the lateral deformation oflag screw connections may be estimated in
accordance with Clause A.12.6.5.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 514: 12.6.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.6.1 Withdrawl resistance General
The factored withdrawal resistance, Prw, of alag screw connection shall be greater than or equal to the
effect of the factored loads and shall be calculated as follows:
Prw = φ Yw LtnFJE
where
φ=0.6
Yw= yw(KD KSF KT)
where
yw =specified withdrawal resistance per millimetre ofthreaded shank penetration into main
member, N/mm
= 59dF0.82G1.77 JX
where
dF =nominal diameter oflag screw, mm
G = mean relative density of main member (see Table A.11)
JX = 0.9 for CLT
= 1.0 in all other cases
Lt =length ofthreaded shank penetration into main member, mm (see Clause 12.6.3)
nF = number offasteners in the connection
JE = end grain factor for lag screws
=0.75 in end grain
=0.67 in panel edge ofCLT
= 1.00 in all other cases
Note: The use oflag screws in end grain should be avoided.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 515: 12.6.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.6.6.2 Tensile resistance ofthe lag screw
The tensile resistance ofthe lag screw atthe net (root) section shall not be exceeded. The specified
tensile strength ofthe lag screw, fu, shall be a minimum of410 MPa.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 516: 12.7 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7 Timber rivets
Note: Timber rivets are also referred to as “glulam rivets” or “rivets” in the following clauses.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 517: 12.7.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.1.1 Timber rivets with steel side plates
The design methods and tabulated resistances specified in Clause 12.7 are for timber rivets with steel
side plates that meet the following requirements:
a) rivets are manufactured to have the following properties:
i) hardness: Rockwell C32-39;
ii) ultimate tensile strength: 1000 MPa, minimum; and
iii) finish: hot-dip galvanized;
b) steel side plates meet the requirements of CSA G40.21 or ASTM A36/A36M; and
c) rivets and steel plates have dimensions as shown in Figure 12.12.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 518: 12.7.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.1.2 Steel side plates for wet-service conditions
For wet-service conditions, steel side plates shall be hot-dip galvanized.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 519: 12.7.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.1.3 Wood members
The design criteria in Clause 12.7 for timber rivet connections shall only apply to timber rivets that meet
the requirements of Clause 12.7.1.1 loaded in single shear orin withdrawal, with steel side plates, on
Douglas Fir-Larch or Spruce-Lodgepole Pine-Jack Pine glued-laminated timber manufactured in
accordance with CAN/CSA-O122, or on sawn lumber of 64 mm minimum thickness.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 520: 12.7.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.1.4 Cross-section of steel side plates
Steel side plates shall have across-section designed to resist tension and compression forces, as well as
buckling at critical sections, but shall not beless than 3.2 mm thick.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 521: 12.7.1.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.1.5 Installation oftimber rivets
Each rivet shall be placed with its major cross-sectional dimension aligned parallel to grain. The design
criteria in Clause 12.7 are based on rivets driven through circular holes in the side plates until the
conical heads are firmly seated, but rivets shall not be driven flush.
Note: Rivets atthe perimeter ofthe group should be driven first. Successive rivets should be driven in aspiral
pattern from the outside to the centre ofthe group.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 522: 12.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2 Placement oftimber rivets in connections
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 523: 12.7.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2.1 Minimum spacing
The minimum spacing oftimber rivets shall be 15 mm perpendicular to the grain and 25 mm parallel to
the grain.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 524: 12.7.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2.2 Minimum end and edge distances
Minimum end and edge distances (see Figure 12.13) shall be as specified in Table 12.20.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 525: 12.7.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2.3 Penetration oftimber rivets
The maximum penetration of any rivet shall be 70% ofthe thickness ofthe wood member, whether
driven on two faces or one face only. Except as permitted by Clause 12.7.2.4 for connections with rivets
driven from opposite faces of awood member, the rivet length shall be such that the points do not
overlap.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 526: 12.7.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2.4 Overlapping oftimber rivets
For connections where rivets are driven from opposite faces of a wood member such that their points
overlap, the minimum spacing requirements of Clause 12.7.2.1 shall apply to the distance between the
rivets at their points. The total lateral resistance ofthe connection shall be calculated in accordance
with Clause 12.7.3, considering the connection to be aone-sided timber rivet connection, with
a) the number ofrivets associated with the one plate equaling the total number ofrivets atthe
connection; and
b) Sp and SQ determined asthe distances between the rivets attheir points.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 527: 12.7.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.2.5 Maximum distance perpendicular to grain
For wet fabrication conditions in sawn lumber, the maximum distance perpendicular to grain over which
atimber rivet group spans shall not exceed 200 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 528: 12.7.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.1 General Lateral Resistance
Atimber rivet joint (one steel side plate and the rivets associated with it) in side grain shall be designed
so that the factored lateral strength resistance ofthe joint is greater than or equal to the effect ofthe
factored loads on the joint.
Note: The resistance of timber rivet joints loaded laterally is governed by either the ductile failure ofthe rivets or
the brittle failure ofthe wood.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 529: 12.7.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.2 Factored lateral strength resistance parallel to grain
For loading parallel to grain, the factored lateral strength resistance, Pr, of atimber rivet joint shall be
calculated asfollows:
Pr = φ Pu H
where
φ= 0.6
Pu=unit lateral strength resistance parallel to grain, kN (see Clause 12.7.3.3)
H = material factor
= 1.00 for Douglas Fir-Larch glulam
=0.80 for Spruce-Lodgepole Pine-Jack Pine glulam
=0.50 for Douglas Fir-Larch sawn timber
= 0.45 for Hem-Fir sawn timber
=0.40 for Spruce-Pine-Fir sawn timber
=0.35 for Northern Species sawn timber
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 530: 12.7.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.3 12.7.3.3 Unit lateral strength resistance parallel to grain
The unit lateral strength resistance parallel to grain, Pu, per joint, shall be the lesser of Py or Pw,
calculated asfollows:
Py =(1.09Lp0.32nRnC) JY(KSF KT) for rivet resistance
Pw =pw (KD KSF KT) for wood resistance
where
Lp =length ofpenetration, mm (see Figure 12.12)
=(overall rivet length) –(plate thickness) –3.2
nR =number ofrows ofrivets parallel tothe direction ofload
nC = number ofrivets per row
JY =side plate factor
=1.00 for aside plate thickness of6.4 mm and more
=0.90 for aside plate thickness of4.7 mm or more but less than 6.4 mm
=0.80 for aside plate thickness of3.2 mm or more but less than 4.7 mm

pw =specified unit lateral strength resistance per joint parallel tograin, kN(see Table 12.21), using
wood member thickness for the member dimension in Table 12.21 for connections with steel
plates on opposite sides and using twice the wood member thickness for the member
dimension in Table 12.21 for connections having only one plate
Note: As an alternative, pw may be calculated in accordance with Clause A.12.7.3.3.1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 531: 12.7.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.4 Factored lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain
For loading perpendicular to grain, the factored lateral strength resistance, Qr, of atimber rivet joint
shall be calculated asfollows:
Qr = φ Qu H
where
φ= 0.6
Qu=unit lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain, kN(see Clause 12.7.3.5)
H = material factor (see Clause 12.7.3.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 532: 12.7.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.5 12.7.3.5 Unit lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain
The unit lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain, Qu, per joint, shall be the lesser of Qy or Qw,
calculated as follows:
Qy =(0.62Lp^0.32 nR nC) JY(KSF KT) for rivet capacity
Qw =(qw Lp^0.8Ct)(KD KSF KT) for wood capacity
where Lp,nR, nC, JY are as specified in Clause 12.7.3.3
qw=specified unit strength lateral resistance per joint perpendicular tograin, kN (see Table 12.22)
Ct=timber rivet joint configuration factor (see Table 12.23)
Note: As an alternative, qw and Ct may be calculated in accordance with Clause A.12.7.3.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 533: 12.7.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.6 12.7.3.6 Factored lateral strength resistance at an angle to grain
For loading at an angle to the grain, ,the factored lateral strength resistance, Nr, of atimber rivet joint
shall be calculated asfollows:
N_r = (P_r * Q_r) / (P_r * sin²θ + Q_r * cos²θ)

Where:
  P_r = factored lateral strength resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 12.7.3.2)
  Q_r = factored lateral strength resistance perpendicular to grain (see Clause 12.7.3.4)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 534: 12.7.3.7 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.3.7 End grain
When timber rivets are installed in the end grain, the factored lateral strength resistance ofthe joint
shall be 50% ofthat for rivets installed in the side grain and loaded perpendicular to grain. When timber
rivets are installed in the end grain at an intermediate angle, the factored lateral strength resistance
may beincreased linearly from the value calculated for the end grain, up to 100% ofthe applicable
value for rivets installed in the side grain loaded parallel or perpendicular to grain.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 535: 12.7.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.7.4.1 Load duration
Timber rivets loaded in withdrawal shall only be permitted for dry-service conditions for short-term and
standard-term load durations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 536: 12.7.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
2.7.4.2 Withdrawal resistance from the side grain
The factored withdrawal resistance from the side grain, Prw, of atimber rivet joint shall be greater than
or equal to the effect of the factored loads and shall be calculated as follows:
Prw = φ Yw Lp nR nC
where
φ= 0.6
Yw=yw(KSF KT)
where
yw =specified withdrawal resistance per rivet per millimetre ofpenetration, N/mm
    =13for glulam
    = 7for sawn timber
Lp, nR, and nC are as specified in Clause 12.7.3.3.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 537: 12.8.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.1 Truss Plates Materials
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.8 apply to truss plate connections using light-gauge
metal plates that
a) depend on extended teeth or nails embedded into the wood to transfer load;
b) meet the requirements of Clause 16.4; and
c) have been tested in accordance with Clause 16.4.2 for the species group with which the plates are
to be used.
Notes:
1) Test results for such plates are listed in the Registry of Product Evaluations published by the Canadian
Construction Materials Centre at NRC, Ottawa, Ontario.
2) The provisions of Clause 12.8 are predicated on truss fabrication and erection in accordance with recognized
practices such asthose referenced by TPIC.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 538: 12.8.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.2 Limitations
Clause 12.8 does not apply to
a) truss plates under corrosive conditions; and
b) the use of galvanized truss plates in lumber that has been treated with afire retardant and is used
in wet service conditions or in locations prone to consideration. 
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 539: 12.8.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.3 Placement of plates in the joints
Connection design shall be based on tight-fitted joints with truss plates placed on opposing faces in such
away that, at each joint, the plates on opposing faces are identical and are placed directly opposite
each other.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 540: 12.8.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.4 Nail-on plates
In cases where nail-on plates are used, the word “nail” should be read in place of “tooth” in Clause 12.8.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 541: 12.8.1.5 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.5 Design assumptions
The design criteria for truss plates in Clause 12.8 are based on the following conditions:
a) the plate is prevented from deforming during installation;
b) the teeth are normal to the surface ofthe lumber;
c) the tooth penetration in connections is not less than that used in the testing specified in
Clause 16.4.2; and
d) the lumber beneath the plate complies with Appendix Gof TPIC.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 542: 12.8.1.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.6 Minimum member thickness
The thickness of members used in connections shall not beless than twice the tooth penetration.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 543: 12.8.1.7 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.1.7 Primary axis ofatruss plate
The primary axis of atruss plate, in the case ofslotted truss plate tooth configurations, shall be parallel
to the direction ofslots in the plate. For rosette-style configurations, the primary axis shall be that axis
ofsymmetry in which the tensile strength ofthe truss plate is the greatest.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 544: 12.8.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.2.1 Design requirements
Truss plate connections shall be designed to meet the following requirements:
a) For the strength limit state, the effect offactored loads shall be less than or equal to the factored
i) ultimate lateral resistance ofthe teeth;
ii) tensile resistance ofthe plates; and
iii) shear resistance ofthe plates.
b) For the serviceability limit state, the effect ofspecified loads shall be less than or equal to the
lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 545: 12.8.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.2.2 Compression loads
Truss plates shall not be considered effective in transferring compression loads at ajoint.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 546: 12.8.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.2.3 Design considerations
The design oftruss plate connections shall take the following into consideration:
a) species oflumber;
b) orientation of plates relative to the applied load (Figure 12.14, angle );
c) direction ofthe applied load relative tothe grain (Figure 12.14, angle ); and
d) orientation of plates relative to the applied shear force.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 547: 12.8.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.2.4 Ultimate lateral resistance and lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth
The factored ultimate lateral resistance and the lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth shall be expressed in
terms ofthe surface area ofthe plates.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 548: 12.8.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
 12.8.2.5 Surface area
Surface area shall be based on the net area method using the test values, or on the gross area method
using 80% ofthe test values, where the
a) gross area is defined as the total area of a member covered by atruss plate; and
b) net area is defined as the total area of a member covered by atruss plate less the area within a
given distance from the edge or end ofthe member, as shown in Figure 12.15. For net area
calculation, the minimum end distance, a, measured parallel to grain, shall be the greater of
12 mm or one-half the length ofthe tooth; the minimum edge distance, e, measured perpendicular
to grain, shall be the greater of 6 mm or one-quarter the length ofthe tooth.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 549: 12.8.2.6 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.2.6 Tensile and shear resistance ofthe plates
The factored tensile resistance ofthe plates shall be expressed in terms ofthe dimension ofthe plate
measured perpendicular to the line of action of the applied forces. The factored shear resistance shall
be expressed in terms ofthe dimension ofthe plate measured along the line of action ofthe shearing
forces.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 550: 12.8.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.3 Factored resistance oftruss plates
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 551: 12.8.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.3.1 General
For the strength limit state, the factored resistances oftruss plates shall be calculated asfollows:
a) for the factored ultimate lateral resistance ofthe teeth:
Nr = NuJH
where
φ= 0.9

Nu =nu(KD KSF KT)
where
nu =ultimate lateral resistance ofthe teeth, determined in accordance with the
manufacturer’s product evaluation report (see Clause 12.8.3.2)
JH = moment factor for heel connection (see Table 12.24)
b) for the factored tensile resistance ofthe plate:
Tr = φ tp
where
φ= 0.6
tp=tensile resistance ofthe plate, determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s product
evaluation report
c)for the factored shear resistance ofthe plate:
Vr= φ vp
where
φ= 0.6
vp=shear resistance ofthe plate, determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s product
evaluation report
The shear resistance values for the tensile mode of failure shall be used where the applied shear forces
create tension in the plate. Where the applied forces create compression in the plate, the compressive
shear values shall be used. Alternatively, the lower ofthe two shear resistances for an angle may be
used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 552: 12.8.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.3.2 Ultimate lateral resistance ofthe teeth
The ultimate lateral resistance ofthe teeth shall be calculated asfollows:
a) For loads parallel to the primary axis of the plate:
   η_u = (p_u * q_u) / (p_u * sin²θ + q_u * cos²θ)

b) For loads perpendicular to the primary axis of the plate:
   η_u' = (p_u' * q_u') / (p_u * sin²θ + q_u * cos²θ)

Where:
  θ = angle of the applied load relative to the primary axis

p_u, q_u, p'_u, q'_u = ultimate lateral resistances determined in accordance with the manufacturer's
product evaluation report and used with the following values of θ and ρ:

         |  θ     |  ρ
  p_u    |  0°    | 0°
  q_u    | 90°    | 0°
  p'_u   |  0°    | 90°
  q'_u   | 90°    | 90°

Note: θ and ρ are as shown in Figure 12.14.

When the primary axis of the plate is oriented at an angle other than parallel or perpendicular to the
direction of the load, the resistance value shall be determined by linear interpolation between the
values η_u and η'_u.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 553: 12.8.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.4.1 Adjusted lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth
For the serviceability limit state, the adjusted lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth, Nrs, shall be calculated
asfollows:
Nrs =Ns KSF
where
Ns =lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth (see Clause 12.8.4.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 554: 12.8.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.8.4.2 Lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth
The lateral slip resistance ofthe teeth shall be calculated asfollows:
a) For loads parallel to the primary axis of the plate:
   N_s = (p_s * q_s) / (p_s * sin²θ + q_s * cos²θ)

b) For loads perpendicular to the primary axis of the plate:
   N'_s = (p'_s * q'_s) / (p'_s * sin²θ + q'_s * cos²θ)

Where:
  p_s, q_s, p'_s, q'_s = lateral slip resistances determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s
                         product evaluation report and used with the following values of θ and ρ:

         |  θ     |  ρ
  p_s    |  0°    | 0°
  q_s    | 90°    | 0°
  p'_s   |  0°    | 90°
  q'_s   | 90°    | 90°

Note: θ and ρ are as shown in Figure 12.14.

When the primary axis ofthe plate is oriented at an angle other than parallel or perpendicular to the
direction ofthe load, the resistance value shall be determined bylinear interpolation between the
values Nsand N's.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 555: 12.9.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.1 Nail and Spikes General
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.9 apply only to common round steel wire nails and
spikes and common spiral nails spiraled to head as defined in CSA B111 or ASTM F1667, including
power-tool driven common nails.
Note: See Tables A.21 and A.22 for commonly available nail and spike sizes.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 556: 12.9.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.2.1 12.9.2.1 Connection configuration Placement ofnails and spikes in side grain
For connections nailed at 10% wood moisture content or greater, the minimum spacing offasteners in
sawn lumber side plates and main members, including those in the panel face of CLT, shall be as
specified in Table 12.25. Additional fasteners may be staggered on the intersection of diagonal lines
drawn between rows of nails (see Figure 12.16).
Note: When the moisture content ofthe wood is expected to be less than 10% at time offabrication, the spacing
should be increased and holes should be predrilled to avoid splitting.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 557: 12.9.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.2.2 Penetration length and member thickness
Penetration length and member thicknesses for wood-to-wood and steel-to-wood connections shall be
as shown in Figure 12.17.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 558: 12.9.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.2.3 Placement of nails and spikes in the panel edge of CLT
In agroup offasteners installed in the panel edge of CLT, the minimum spacing offasteners shall be as
specified in Table 12.26 (see Figure 12.7):

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 559: 12.9.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.3.1 Lateral Resistance General
The factored lateral strength resistance ofaconnection with nails or spikes, Nr, shall be greater than or
equal to the effect ofthe factored loads, and shall be calculated asfollows:


Nr = φ Nu nF nSJF
where
φ= 0.8
Nu=nu(KD KSF KT)
where
nu =unit lateral strength resistance per shear plane, N(see Clause 12.9.3.2)
nF = number offasteners in the connection
nS = number of shear planes per fastener
JF =JEJA JBJD
where
JE =end grain factor
=0.67 for nailing into end grain
= 1.0 in all other cases
JA =toe-nailing factor
=0.83 for toe-nailing, where toe-nails are started atapproximately one-third ofthe nail length
from the end ofthe piece and driven at an angle of about 30° to the grain ofthe member
=1.00 for cases other than toe-nailing
JB =nail clinching factor
=1.6 for nail clinching onthe far side in atwo-member connection
= 1.0 if not clinched orin three-or-more member connections
JD =factor for diaphragm and shearwall construction
=1.3 for fasteners used in diaphragm and shearwall construction
= 1.0 in all other cases
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 560: 12.9.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.3.2 12.9.3.2 Unit lateral strength resistance
The unit lateral strength resistance per shear plane, nu, shall be taken asthe smallest value calculated in
accordance with Items a)to g). For two-member connections, only Items a), b), and d)to g)shall be
considered valid. For three-member connections, only Items a), c), d), and g) shall be considered valid.
a) f1 df t1
b) f2 df t2
c) 1/2 f2 df t2
d)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₃ / (f₁ + f₃)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₁ / (5 d_f)))]  
e)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₃ / (f₁ + f₃)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₂ / (5 d_f)))]  
f)  f₁ d_f² * (1/5) * [(t₁ / d_f) + (f₂ * t₂) / (f₁ * d_f)]  
g)  f₁ d_f² * √[(2/3) * (f₃ / (f₁ + f₃)) * (f_y / f₁)]

where
    dF =nominal diameter offastener, mm
    t1 = head-side member thickness in two-member connections, mm
     =head-side member thickness orlength ofpenetration into point-side member, whichever isless,
        in three-member connections, mm (see Clause 12.9.2.2)
    t2 =length ofpenetration into point-side (main) member intwo-member connections, mm
        =central member thickness inthree-member connections, mm (see Clause 12.9.2.2)
    =embedment strength ofside member, MPa f1
    f2 = embedment strength of point-side (main) member for two-member connections for yield modes
    b) and f), MPa
        = embedment strength ofcentral member in three-member connections for yield mode c), MPa
    f3 =embedment strength ofpoint-side wood member for two-member connections for yield modes
        d), e), and g), MPa 
        =embedment strength ofcentral member inthree-member connections for yield modes d)and g), MPa

For wood members:
f1=f2=50 G(1–0.01dF) Jx
f3= 110 G1.8 (1–0.01dF) Jx
where
G = mean relative density
Note: Mean relative density values for wood members (lumber, glulam, and CLT) are provided in
Table A.11.
Jx = 0.9 for CLT
= 1.0 for other wood members

For structural panels:
f1 =f2=104 G(1–0.1dF)
where
G = 0.49 for DFP
= 0.42 for CSP and OSB
For steel:
f1 =f2 =Ksp (steel/wood) fu
where
Ksp= 3.0 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
    =2.7 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136
φsteel=resistance factor for steel members in connections with nails and spikes
= 0.80 for mild steel referenced in CSA S16
=0.4 for cold-formed light-gauge steel referenced in CSA S136
φwood=resistance factor for wood members in connections with nails and spikes
= 0.8

fu=specified minimum tensile strength ofsteel
Note: The specified minimum tensile strength ofsteel, fu, is given in the relevant material standards, e.g.,
a)fu =400 MPa for ASTM A36/A36M steel;
b)fu =450 MPa for CSA G40.21 steel, Grades 300W and 350W; and
c)fu =310 MPa for cold-formed light-gauge steel, Grade SS 230.

fy =yield strength offastener in bending, MPa
= 50 (16 –dF)
