Clause 561: 12.9.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.3.3 Connection deformation
Where required for design, the lateral deformation of wood-to-wood connections with nails and spikes,
including structural panel-to-lumber connections, may be estimated in accordance with
Clause A.12.9.3.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 562: 12.9.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.4.1 Load duration
Nails and spikes loaded in withdrawal shall only be used for short-term loading.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 563: 12.9.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.4.2 Withdrawal from the side grain
The factored withdrawal resistance of aconnection with nails or spikes, Prw, driven into the side grain
shall be greater than or equal to the effect ofthe factored loads and shall be calculated asfollows:
Prw = φ Yw Lp nFJA JB
where
φv= 0.6
Yw=yw(KSF KT)
where
yw = specified withdrawal resistance per millimetre of penetration into point-side member,
N/mm
= 16.4dF^0.82G^2.2Jx

where
dF = nominal diameter offastener, mm
G = mean relative density (see Table A.11)
Jx = 0.9 for CLT
= 1.0 in all other cases
Lp =length of penetration into point-side member, mm
nF = number offasteners in the connection
JA =toe-nailing factor
= 0.67 for toe-nailing
=1.00 for cases other than toe-nailing
JB = nail-clinching factor
=1.6 for nail-clinching inthe point-side member ofatwo-member connection
= 1.0 if not clinched orin three-or-more member connections
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 564: 12.9.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.9.4.3 Withdrawal from the end grain
Nails and spikes driven into the end grain shall not be considered to carry load in withdrawal. Where
designs rely on withdrawal resistance offasteners in the panel edge of CLT, precaution shall be taken to
ensure that side grain penetration occurs.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 565: 12.10.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.10.1.1 Joist Hangers Materials
The design requirements specified in Clause 12.10 apply to proprietary mass-produced metal devices,
usually cold-formed from light-gauge steel or welded from steel plate, that are used to transfer loads
from joists to headers or beams and have been tested in accordance with Clause 16.5. The joists and
headers or beams may be sawn lumber, wood trusses, glued-laminated timber, prefabricated wood
I-joists, orSCL.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 566: 12.10.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.10.1.2 Limitations
The provisions of Clause 12.10 do not apply under the following conditions:
a) corrosive conditions;
b) the use of galvanized joist hangers inlumber that has been treated with afire retardant and is
used in wet-service conditions or conditions prone to condensation;
c) joist hangers connected to headers or beams of other than wood-based materials; and
d) special hangers having askew in the horizontal or vertical plane (except skewed hangers with level
bearing seats).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 567: 12.10.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.10.1.3 Construction requirements
Joist hangers shall be constructed to meet the following requirements:
a) The height ofthe hanger shall be atleast half the depth ofthe joist and be capable of providing
lateral support for the joist unless the joist is prevented from twisting by other means.
b) The hanger shall be fastened to both the joist and the header or beam. Where nails or wood
screws are used, the size and spacing shall prevent splitting ofthe wood. Where bolts are used, the
spacing shall meet the requirements of Clause 12.4 for bolts and Clause 12.6 for lag screws.

c) Hangers used to support prefabricated wood I-joists that do not require bearing stiffeners shall be
high enough to provide lateral stability to the top flange ofthe joist.
d) Where aprefabricated wood I-joist isthe header, backer blocks shall be provided between the web
and face mount hangers.
e) Where aprefabricated wood I-joist is supporting atop mount hanger, filler blocks shall be used
between the top and bottom flange ofthe I-joist. The blocks shall be tight to the bottom ofthe top
flange.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 568: 12.10.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.10.2.1 Factored resistance
The factored resistance, Nr, ofjoist hangers shall be greater than or equal to the effect ofthe factored
loads, and shall be calculated asfollows:
Nr = φ Nu
where
φ= 0.6
Nu=nu(KD KSF KT)
where
nu =ultimate resistance ofthe hanger
KD =load-duration factor determined in accordance with Clause 5.3.2, except that there shall not
be an increase for short-term load duration where the ultimate resistance is determined by
the strength ofthe steel
Note: In general, proprietary design values are published by the product manufacturer (i.e., proprietary design
literature and CCMC Evaluation Reports in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations, published by the Canadian
Construction Materials Centre) with appropriate factors for specific applications.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 569: 12.10.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.10.2.2 Shear resistance ofthe header or beam
For joist hangers attached to the face of aheader or beam, the shear resistance ofthe header or beam
shall be checked in accordance with Clause 12.2.1.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 575: 12.11.3.1

Nr = φ Nu nF nsJAJE
where
φ= 0.8
Nu=nu(KD KSF KT)

ns =number ofshear planes per fastener
JA =toe-screwing factor
=0.83 where screws are started atapproximately one-third the screw length from the end ofa
piece and driven at an angle of about 30° to the grain ofthe member
= 1.0 in all other cases
JE =factor for fastening into end grain
=0.67 in end grain
= 1.0 in all other cases
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 576: 12.11.3.2

accordance with Items a)to g). For two-member connections, only Items a), b), d)to f), and g) are valid.
For three-member connections, only Items a), c), d), and g) are valid.

b)  f₂ d_f t₂  
c)  (1/2) f₂ d_f t₂  
d)  f₁ d_f² * [√((1/6) * (f₃ / (f₁ + f₃)) * (f_y / f₁) + (t₁ / (5 d_f)))]
e)
f)
g)
where

    = head-side member thickness orlength of penetration into point-side member, whichever isless,
    in three-member connections, mm (see Clause 12.11.2.4)
t2 =length ofpenetration into point-side (main) member intwo-member connections, mm
    =central member thickness inthree-member connections, mm (see Clause 12.11.2.4)
f1  =embedment strength ofside member, MPa 
f2 =embedment strength ofpoint-side (main) member intwo-member connections for yield modes
    b)and f), MPa
    =embedment strength ofcentral member inthree-member connections for yield mode c), MPa
f3 =embedment strength ofpoint-side wood member for two-member connections for yield modes
    d), e), and g), MPa
    =embedment strength ofcentral member inthree-member connections for yield modes d)and
    g), MPa

Clause 578: 12.11.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
12.11.4.1 General Withdrawl Resistance
The factored withdrawal resistance of aconnection with wood screws shall be greater than or equal to
the effect ofthe factored loads and shall be taken asthe lesser ofthe factored screw withdrawal
resistance ofthe point-side member (see Clause 12.11.4.2) and the factored head pull-through
resistance ofthe head-side member (see Clause 12.11.4.3).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 579: 12.11.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
12.11.4.2 Withdrawal resistance of point-side member
For atwo-member connection with wood screws, the factored withdrawal resistance, Prw, in N, ofthe
point-side member shall be calculated asfollows:
Prw = φ Yw Lpt nF
where
φ= 0.6
Yw=yw(KD KTKSF)
where
yw =specified withdrawal resistance per millimetre ofthreaded shank penetration in point-side
member, N/mm
= 59dF^0.82G^1.77Jx
where

G = mean relative density ofpoint-side member (see Table A.11)
Jx = 0.9 for CLT
    = 1.0 in all other cases
Lpt =threaded length penetration inthe point-side member, mm
nF = number offasteners in the connection
For aconnection with three members, the threaded length penetration shall be the greater threaded
length within any member other than the head-side member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 580: 12.11.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
12.11.4.3 12.11.4.3 Head pull-through resistance ofhead-side member
The factored head pull-through resistance, Ppt, in N, of aconnection with wood screws shall be
calculated as follows:
a) for connections with steel side plates:
Ppt =1.5 φ t1 dw fu nF
b) for connections with lumber, glulam, CLT, orstructural panel head-side members:
Ppt =65 φ t1 nF KD
where
φ = 0.4
t1 =thickness of head-side member, mm
dw=diameter ofscrew head, mm
fu=specified minimum tensile strength ofsteel, MPa

Note: The specified minimum tensile strength ofsteel, fu, is given in the relevant material standards, e.g., for
a)fu =400 MPa for ASTM A36/A36M steel;
b)fu =450 MPa for CSA G40.21 steel, Grades 300W and 350W; and
c)fu =310 MPa for cold-formed light-gauge steel, Grade SS 230.
nF = number offasteners in the connection
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 581: 12.11.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
12.11.4.4 Withdrawal from the end grain
Wood screws installed through the end grain shall not be considered to carry load in withdrawal. Where
designs rely on withdrawal resistance ofscrews in the panel edge of CLT, precaution shall be taken to
ensure that side grain penetration occurs.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 582: 13.1 
--------------------------------------------------
13.1 13.1 Scope Timber piling
The design data and methods specified in Clause 13 apply only to the engineering design of piling that
meets the requirements of CAN/CSA-O56 as structural members. Calculation ofthe bearing (supporting)
capacity ofthe soil orrock is not covered by Clause 13.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 583: 13.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
13.2.1 Preservative treatment
Except as specified in Clause 13.2.2, the design data and methods specified in Clause 13 are based on
the use ofpiling pressure treated with preservatives in accordance with the requirements ofthe
CAN/CSA-O80 Series of Standards.
Note: Species covered by CAN/CSA-O56 are not necessarily suitable for pressure treatment with preservatives. See
the CAN/CSA-O80 Series of Standards for lists of species of piles that can be treated with preservatives.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 584: 13.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
13.2.2 Untreated piling
The design data and methods specified in Clause 13 may also be applied to untreated piling used for
temporary construction.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 585: 13.3 
--------------------------------------------------
13.3 Specified strengths and moduli of elasticity
The specified strengths and moduli of elasticity for round timber piles are given in Table 13.1.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 586: 13.4 
--------------------------------------------------
13.4 Modification factors
The modification factors specified in Clause 5.3.2 for duration ofload and Clause 6.4.2 for service
conditions shall apply to timber piling. Other modification factors shall not apply.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 587: 13.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.1 General
Timber piles may act as end-bearing piles or friction piles and shall be designed to transmit all of the
applied loads to supporting soil orrock.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 588: 13.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.2 Piles as compression members
Piles shall be considered to act as compression members. Where necessary, piles shall be designed to
withstand factored bending moments and factored tensile forces due to uplift or other causes, in
accordance with the applicable requirements of Clause 6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 589: 13.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.3 Effective length
When the finished pile projects above ground level and is not secured against buckling by bracing, the
effective length shall be governed by the fixity conditions imposed on it bythe structure itsupports and
by the nature of the ground into which itis driven. In firm soil, the lower point of contraflexure may be
taken to be atadepth below ground level ofabout one-tenth ofthe exposed length. Where the top
stratum is soft clay or silt, this point may be taken at about one-half the depth of penetration into this
stratum, but not less than one-tenth ofthe exposed length ofthe pile. Where apile is wholly
embedded, its carrying capacity is not limited by its strength as along column. However, where there is
astratum ofvery soft soils or peat, piles shall be designed in accordance with Clause 13.5.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 590: 13.5.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.4.1 General
That portion of apile permanently in contact with soil orrock providing lateral support shall be
designed in accordance with Clause 6.5.5 using aslenderness factor KC =1.00.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 591: 13.5.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.4.2 End-bearing piles
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, of end-bearing piles shall be calculated for an area, A, equal to
the minimum cross-sectional area ofthe pile.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 592: 13.5.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.4.3 Friction piles
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, offriction piles shall be calculated over an area, A,equal to the
cross-sectional area ofthe pile at apoint one-third ofthe length ofthe embedded portion ofthe pile
from the tip.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 593: 13.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
13.5.5 Unembedded portion
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, ofthat portion ofthe pile in contact with air, water, or soils that
do not provide adequate lateral support shall be calculated in accordance with Clause 6.5.5. The
slenderness factor, KC, shall be calculated using aslenderness ratio, CC, determined in accordance with
Clauses 14.5.2.5 and 14.5.2.6. Piles subject to eccentric orlateral loads shall be designed in accordance
with Clause 6.5.9.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 594: 14.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
14.1.1 Round poles Pole Type Construction
The design data and methods specified in Clause 14 apply only to the engineering design ofround poles
complying with the physical requirements, other than strength properties, of CAN/CSA-O15 as structural
members in pole-type structures. Calculation ofthe bearing (supporting) capacity ofthe soil is not
covered by Clause 14.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 595: 14.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
14.1.2 Sawn timbers
Sawn timbers used as poles shall meet the requirements of Clause 6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 596: 14.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
14.2.1 Preservative treatment
The design data and methods specified in Clause 14 for poles and other wood components that are
exposed to soil, moisture, inadequate ventilation, contact with masonry or concrete, or other conditions
favourable to decay are based on the assumption that the poles and other wood components are
pressure treated with preservatives in accordance with the requirements ofthe CAN/CSA-O80 Series of
Standards.
Note: Species covered by CAN/CSA-O15 are not necessarily suitable for pressure treatment with preservatives.
Species of poles to be treated with preservatives are restricted to the species listed in the CAN/CSA-O80 Series of
Standards.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 597: 14.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
14.2.2 Short poles
When round pole lengths are shorter than specified in CAN/CSA-O15 but meet all other requirements of
CAN/CSA-O15, the same taper and the same minimum circumference atthe top, specified in
CAN/CSA-O15, shall be used in calculations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 598: 14.3 
--------------------------------------------------
14.3 Specified strengths
The specified strengths for round poles, except eastern white cedar poles, shall be 80% ofthe values
specified in Table 6.6 for select structural grade beams and stringers ofthe applicable species
combination. The specified strengths for round eastern white cedar poles shall be 50% ofthe values
specified in Table 6.6 for select structural grade beams and stringers ofthe species combination
Northern Species.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 599: 14.4 
--------------------------------------------------
14.4 Modification factors
The modification factors used for beams and stringers in Clause 6shall apply to round poles.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 600: 14.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.1 General
Poles shall be designed to transmit all applied factored loads to the soil and shall be suitable for the soil
conditions atthe site.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 601: 14.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2 Poles as compression members
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 602: 14.5.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.1 General
Where necessary, poles shall be designed to withstand factored bending moments and factored tensile
forces due to uplift or other causes in accordance with the applicable requirements of Clause 6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 603: 14.5.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.2 Effective length
Effective length shall be established in accordance with Clause 13.5.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 604: 14.5.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.3 Embedded portion
That portion of apole permanently in contact with soil orrock providing lateral support shall be
designed in accordance with Clause 6.5.5, using aslenderness factor KC =1.00.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 605: 14.5.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.4 Unembedded portion
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, of the portion of apole in contact with air, water, or soil that
does not provide adequate lateral support shall be calculated in accordance with Clause 6.5.5. The
slenderness factor, KC, shall be calculated using aslenderness ratio, CC, determined in accordance with
Clauses 14.5.2.5 and 14.5.2.6. Poles subject to eccentric orlateral loads shall be designed in accordance
with Clause 6.5.9.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 606: 14.5.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.5 Constant non-rectangular cross-section
For non-rectangular compression members ofconstant section, the slenderness ratio, CC, shall be
calculated in accordance with Clause 6.5.5.2.2 substituting the member width or depth with
ris the applicable radius of gyration ofthe cross-section ofthe member.where
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 607: 14.5.2.6 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.2.6 Variable circular cross-section
The radius ofgyration ofround tapered compression members shall be calculated for an effective
diameter equal to the minimum diameter plus 0.45 times the difference between the maximum and
minimum diameters. The factored compressive resistance determined in this manner shall not exceed
the factored resistance based on the minimum diameter in conjunction with aslenderness factor
KC =1.00.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 608: 14.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
14.5.3 Poles as bending members
The factored bending moment resistance, Mr, ofround members shall be taken asthat of asquare
member having the same cross-sectional area. Atapered round member shall be considered an
equivalent square member ofvariable cross-section.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 609: 15.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.1 Scope Proprietary structural wood products —Design 
The design requirements for proprietary structural wood products used in specific applications specified
in Clause 15 are provided for the project engineer or building designer. The product design values are
usually generated by the manufacturer’s engineer in accordance with Clause 16. Unless otherwise

specified bythe product manufacturer, proprietary products shall be used only under dry-service
conditions.
Note: In general, proprietary design values are published by the product manufacturer (i.e., proprietary design
literature and Product Evaluation Reports in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations) with appropriate factors for
specific applications. For applications where adjustments to design values are possibly warranted, the designer
should seek guidance from the product manufacturer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 610: 15.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.1 General Prefabricated Wood I-Joists
Prefabricated wood I-joists for use in accordance with Clause 15.2 shall meet the applicable
requirements of Clause 16.2.
Note: The I-joist should bear the mark ofthe accredited certification organization that is providing the I-joist
product certification in accordance with ISO/IEC 17065.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 611: 15.2.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.2.1 Load-duration factor, KD
The specified strengths ofprefabricated wood I-joists shall be multiplied by aload-duration factor, KD, as
specified in Clause 5.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 612: 15.2.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.2.2 Service-condition factor, KS
The prefabricated wood I-joists described in Clause 16.2 shall only be used in dry-service conditions for
which all service-condition factors KS =1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 613: 15.2.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.2.3 Treatment factor, KT
The strengths and stiffnesses described in Clause 16 are applicable to untreated prefabricated wood
I-joists, with KT =1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 614: 15.2.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.2.4 System factor, KH
The system factor, KH, shall be taken as 1.0 for all strength properties of prefabricated wood I-joists.
Note: For additional information, see Appendix X1.4.1 of ASTM D5055.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 615: 15.2.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.1 Bending moment resistance
The factored bending moment resistance, Mr, of prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated as
follows:
Mr= φ M’r(KD KS KH KT) KL
where
φ= 0.90
M’r=adjusted bending moment resistance
KD =load-duration factor (see Clause 15.2.2.1)
KS =service-condition factor (see Clause 15.2.2.2)
KH =system factor (see Clause 15.2.2.4)
KT =treatment factor (see Clause 15.2.2.3)

KL =lateral-stability factor (see Clause 15.2.3.2)
Note: Factored ultimate resistance values, M’r, are listed in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 616: 15.2.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.2 Lateral-stability factor, KL
The lateral-stability factor, KL, shall be equal to 1.00 when lateral support is provided at points of
bearing, to prevent lateral displacement and rotation, and along all compression edges. Lateral support
requirements and lateral-stability factors for other applications such as continuous spans shall be based
on analytical and engineering principles, documented test data, or both, that demonstrate the safe use
ofthe product in the intended application.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 617: 15.2.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.3 Notches
There shall be no notching nor cutting ofthe flanges of prefabricated wood I-joists unless such details
have been evaluated and shown to be acceptable based on documented test data.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 618: 15.2.3.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.4.1 General
In the calculation ofshear resistance, the effect of all loads acting on the member shall be considered,
including the loads acting within adistance from asupport equal to the depth ofthe member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 619: 15.2.3.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.4.2 Factored shear resistance
The factored shear resistance, Vr, of prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated asfollows:
Vr= φ V’r(KD KS KT)
where
φ= 0.90
V'r=shear resistance determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report
Note: Factored ultimate resistance values, V’r, are listed in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 620: 15.2.3.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.5.1 General Shear Resistance
In the calculation ofreaction resistance, the effect of allloads acting on the member shall be
considered, including the loads acting near supports.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 621: 15.2.3.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.5.2 Factored end reaction resistance
The factored end reaction resistance, ERr, atthe specified end bearing length of prefabricated wood
I-joists shall be calculated asfollows:
ERr = φ ER’r(KD KS KT)
where
φ = 0.90
ER’r=end reaction resistance determined in accordance with Clause 16 and published inthe
manufacturer’s product evaluation report
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 622: 15.2.3.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.5.3 Factored intermediate reaction resistance
The factored intermediate reaction resistance, IRr, atthe specified intermediate bearing length of
prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated asfollows:
IRr = φ IR’r(KD KS KT)
where
φ = 0.90
IR’r=intermediate reaction resistance determined in accordance with Clause 16 and published in the
manufacturer’s product evaluation report
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 623: 15.2.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.3.6 Web openings, bearing length, and web stiffener requirements
Designers shall obtain information regarding web openings, bearing length, and web stiffener
requirements from the manufacturers of wood I-joists.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 624: 15.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.4 Serviceability limit states
The design of prefabricated wood I-joists for serviceability limit states shall bein accordance with
Clauses 5.1.3 and 5.4. Deflection calculations shall be in accordance with the manufacturer’s product
evaluation report. Calculations shall include bending and shear deflection. Bending and shear stiffness
properties shall be applicable to untreated joists used in dry-service conditions only.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 625: 15.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.5 Connections for prefabricated wood I-joists
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 626: 15.2.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.5.1 Nails
Nailed connections shall be designed in accordance with Clause 12.9.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 627: 15.2.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.2.5.2 Joist hangers and other framing connectors
The use ofjoist hangers and other framing connectors with prefabricated wood I-joists shall be based
on documented test data.
Note: Required details of use and attachment are available from the manufacturers.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 628: 15.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.1 General Structural composite lumber
SCL for use in accordance with Clause 15.3, including products subjected to secondary processing
operations, shall meet the applicable requirements of Clauses 16.3.1 to 16.3.6.
Note: The SCL should bear the mark ofthe accredited certification organization that is providing the SCL
certification in accordance with ISO/IEC 17065.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 629: 15.3.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.1 Load-duration factor, KD
The load-duration factor, KD, specified in Clause 5.3.2 is applicable to the specified strengths of SCL,
provided that appropriate testing demonstrating the validity ofthe factor for use with the applicable
product has been conducted.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 630: 15.3.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.2 Service-condition factor, KS
The strengths and stiffness of SCL described in Clause 15.3 are applicable for use in dry-service
conditions, with KS =1.0. Ifthe products are to be used in other than dry-service conditions,
consideration shall be given to the choice of adhesive, and the specified strength and stiffness shall be
evaluated. This shall include development ofappropriate strength reduction factors, based on
documented test results, determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 631: 15.3.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.3 Treatment factor, KT
The strengths and stiffness described in Clause 15.3 are applicable to untreated SCL, with KT =1.0.
Treatment adjustments for specified strength and stiffness shall be based on the documented results of
tests considering the effects oftime, temperature, and moisture content, determined in accordance
with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 632: 15.3.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.4 System factor, KH
The system factor, KH, for SCL used in aload-sharing system shall be 1.04. To qualify for this increase,
SCL shall be part of awood-framing system consisting of atleast three parallel members joined by
transverse load-distributing elements capable of supporting the design load and shall not be spaced
more than 610 mm on centre.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 633: 15.3.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.5 Size factor in bending, KZb
The size factor in bending, KZb, for SCL shall be determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s
product evaluation report.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 634: 15.3.2.6 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.2.6 Size factor in tension, KZt
The size factor in tension, KZt, for SCL shall be determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s
product evaluation report.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 635: 15.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.1 Bending moment resistance
The factored bending moment resistance, Mr, of SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
Mr = φ Fb SKZb KL
where
φ = 0.90
Fb =fb(KD KH KSb KT)
where
fb =specified bending strength, MPa, determined inaccordance with the manufacturer’s
product evaluation report
KZb =size factor in bending (see Clause 15.3.2.5)
KL =lateral-stability factor (see Clause 15.3.3.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 636: 15.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.2 Lateral-stability factor, KL
The lateral-stability factor, KL, for SCL shall be determined in accordance with Clause 6.5.3.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 637: 15.3.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.3 Notches
SCL products with notches orcuts shall not be used unless such details have been evaluated and shown
to be acceptable based on documented test data.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 638: 15.3.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.4 Shear resistance
The factored shear resistance, Vr, of SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
where
Vr=φ Fv 2/3 A Kzv
φ= 0.90
Fv=fv(KD KSv KT)
where
fv =specified shear strength ofSCL, MPa, determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s
product evaluation report
A = cross-sectional area of member, mm2
KZv = 1.0
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 639: 15.3.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.5 Compressive resistance parallel to grain
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 640: 15.3.3.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.5.1 Effective length, Le
Unless noted otherwise, the effective length, Le =KeL, shall be used in determining the slenderness ratio
of SCL in compression.
Note: Recommended effective-length factors for SCL in compression are provided in Table A.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 641: 15.3.3.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.5.2 Slenderness ratio, CC
The slenderness ratio, CC, ofsimple compression members ofconstant rectangular section shall not
exceed 50 and shall be taken as the greater ofthe following:
Cc = effective length associated with width/member width
or
Cc = effective length associated with depth/member depth
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 642: 15.3.3.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.5.3 Factored compressive resistance parallel to grain
The factored compressive resistance parallel to grain, Pr, of SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
Pr = φ Fc A KC KZc
where
φ= 0.80
Fc=fc(KD KSc KT)
where
fc =specified strength incompression parallel to grain, MPa, determined in accordance with the
manufacturer’s product evaluation report
A = cross-sectional area of member, mm2
KC =slenderness factor (see Clause 15.3.3.6)
KZc = 1.0
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 643: 15.3.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.6 Slenderness factor, KC
The slenderness factor, KC, shall be calculated as follows:

K_c = [1.0 + (F_c K_Z C_c³) / (35 E_05 K_SE K_T)]^(-1)

Where:
  E_05 = 0.87 * E

Where:
  E = specified modulus of elasticity, MPa, determined in accordance with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 644: 15.3.3.7 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.7 Compressive resistance perpendicular to grain (bearing)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 645: 15.3.3.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.7.1 Maximum loads
Factored bearing forces shall not exceed the factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
determined in accordance with Clauses 15.3.3.7.2 to 15.3.3.7.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 646: 15.3.3.7.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.7.2 Effect of all applied loads
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Qr, of SCL under the effect ofall applied
loads shall be calculated asfollows:
Qr = φ Fcp Ab KB KZcp
where
φ= 0.80
Fcp=fcp (KD KS KT)
where
fcp =specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain, MPa, determined inaccordance
with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report
Ab = bearing area, mm2
KB =length-of-bearing factor (see Clause 6.5.6.5)
KZcp =size factor for bearing (see Clause 6.5.6.4), except that KZcp shall be equal to 1.0 in the flatwise
(L-X plane, as defined in ASTM D5456) orientation
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 647: 15.3.3.7.3 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.7.3 Effect ofloads applied near asupport
The factored compressive resistance perpendicular to grain, Q’
Q’r=(2/3) φ Fcp A’b KB Kzcp
where
φ= 0.8
Fcp=fcp (KD KS KT)
where
fcp=specified strength in compression perpendicular to grain, MPa, determined inaccordance
with the manufacturer’s product evaluation report
A’b=average bearing area, mm2 (see Clause 6.5.6.3.2)
Note: See Figure 6.2.
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 648: 15.3.3.8 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.8 Compressive resistance at an angle to grain
The factored compressive resistance of SCL at an angle to grain shall be calculated in accordance with
Clause 6.5.7 using the appropriate factored resistances for the proprietary grade ofthe product.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 649: 15.3.3.9 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.9 Tensile resistance parallel to grain
The factored tensile resistance parallel to grain, Tr, of SCL shall be calculated as follows:
Tr= φ Ft An KZt
where
φ= 0.90
Ft=ft(KD KSt KT)
where
ft=specified strength intension parallel to grain, MPa, determined in accordance with the
manufacturer’s product evaluation report
An= net cross-sectional area, mm2

KZt =size factor intension (see Clause 15.3.2.6)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 650: 15.3.3.10 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.3.10 Resistance to combined bending and axial load
Members subject to combined bending and compressive or tensile axial loads shall be designed to
satisfy the applicable interaction equation, as follows:

(P_f / P_r)^2 + (M_f / M_r) * [1 / (1 - (P_f / P_E))] ≤ 1

or

(T_f / T_r) + (M_f / M_r) ≤ 1

Where:
  P_f = factored compressive axial load
  P_r = factored compressive resistance parallel to grain (see Clause 15.3.3.5.3)
  M_f = factored bending moment
  M_r = factored bending moment resistance (see Clause 15.3.3.1)
  P_E = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied moment
      = (π² * E_05 * K_SE * K_T * I) / L_e²

Where:
  E_05 = modulus of elasticity for design of compression members, MPa
  I    = moment of inertia in the plane of the applied moment, mm⁴
  L_e  = effective length in the plane of the applied moment
       = K_e * L
    Where:
      K_e = effective-length factor (see Clause A.6.5.5.1)

  T_f = factored tensile axial load

Tr =factored tensile resistance parallel tograin calculated in accordance with the requirements of
Clause 15.3.3.9
Note: See Clause A.6.5.9 for a more detailed interaction formula for combined bending and compressive loads.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 651: 15.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.4 Serviceability limit states
The design ofSCL for serviceability limit states shall be in accordance with Clauses 5.1.3 and 5.4.
Deflection shall be calculated in accordance with the manufacturer’s material evaluation report. The
published bending and shear stiffness properties shall be applicable to untreated SCL used in dry-service
conditions only.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 652: 15.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.5 Connections for structural composite lumber
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 653: 15.3.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.5.1 Joist hangers
The use ofjoist hangers with proprietary SCL shall meet the requirements of Clause 12.10.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 654: 15.3.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
15.3.5.2 Other connections
The design procedures for nails, wood screws, bolts, dowels, lag screws, timber rivets, shear plates,
truss plates, and split rings in Clause 12 may be used for the design of connections for proprietary SCL
when testing has demonstrated the validity ofthose procedures for use with that product.
Notes:
1) Design information for some fasteners, primarily nails and joist hangers, applicable for use with specific
proprietary products are listed in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations.
2) In the absence of design information for specific fasteners in specific proprietary products, connections for
these products should belimited to bearing-type arrangements.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 655: 16.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.1 Scope Proprietary structural products —Materials and evaluation
Clause 16 applies to the derivation of design values for proprietary structural products that comply with
the requirements of and applicable standards referenced in Clause 16. The design value derivation
methods are directed at manufacturers and manufacturers’ engineers to provide assurance that the
proprietary design values are consistent with the intent of Part 4ofthe National Building Code of
Canada and with this Standard with respect to strength, serviceability, and reliability.
Note: In general, proprietary design values are published by the product manufacturer (i.e., proprietary design
literature and CCMC Evaluation Reports in the CCMC Registry of Product Evaluations), with appropriate factors for
specific applications.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 656: 16.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.1 General Prefabricated Wood I Joists
Except as otherwise specified in Clause 16.2, prefabricated wood I-joists for use in accordance with this
Standard shall meet the requirements of, and be evaluated for strength and stiffness in accordance
with, ASTM D5055. Characteristic values for design with prefabricated wood I-joists shall be determined
in accordance with Clause 16.2.3.5. Prefabricated wood I-joists for use in accordance with this Standard
shall meet the applicable requirements of Clause 16.2.
Note: The I-joist should bear the mark ofthe accredited certification organization that is providing the I-joist
product certification in accordance with ISO/IEC 17065.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 657: 16.2.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.2.1 Flange materials
Clause 16.2 applies to flanges as specified in Clause 6for sawn lumber or Clause 7for glued-laminated
timber. Lumber not meeting the requirements of Clause 6and SCL may be used asflange material when
such material is qualified bytesting as specified in ASTM D5055.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 658: 16.2.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.2.2 Structural panel webs
Webs for prefabricated wood I-joists shall be manufactured from structural panels meeting the
requirements of CSA O121, CSA O151, CSA O153 (for exterior bond only), or CSA O325.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 659: 16.2.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.2.3 Adhesives
Prefabricated wood I-joists shall be manufactured using
a) aclass of adhesives meeting the requirements of CSA O112.6 or CSA O112.7; or
b) alternative adhesives meeting the requirements of CSA O112.9 or CSA O112.10.
Note: For additional information on these Standards, see the commentary in the referenced Standards.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 660: 16.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3 Specified strengths, capacities, and modulus ofelasticity
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 661: 16.2.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.1 Specified strength parallel to grain for flanges
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 662: 16.2.3.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.1.1 Specified axial strength, fa, for flanges —General
The specified axial strength, fa, for flanges shall be the lesser of
fa =ft KLN KZt
or
fa =fc
where
ft =specified strength intension parallel to grain, MPa (see Clause 16.2.3.1.2)
KLN =length-adjustment factor as specified in ASTM D5055 (see Clause A.16.2.3.1)
KZt =size factor for tension parallel to grain from Table 6.13 (applicable only to visually stress-graded
lumber)
fc =specified strength incompression parallel to grain, MPa (see Clause 16.2.3.1.3)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 663: 16.2.3.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.1.2 Specified strength in tension parallel to grain, ft,for flanges
The specified strength in tension parallel to grain, ft, for flanges shall be determined asfollows:
a) When the flange material is sawn lumber meeting the requirements of Clause 6.2 or glued-laminated
timber meeting the requirements of Clause 7.2, the specified strength in tension parallel
to grain shall be determined from ftin Clause 6.3 orftg in Table 7.2, respectively.
b) When the flange material is not as described in Item a), ftshall be calculated asfollows:
ft =tKr
where
t=characteristic value for tension parallel to grain, MPa, asspecified in Clause 16.2.3.5
Kr=reliability normalization factor for bending and tension as specified in Table 16.1

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 664: 16.2.3.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.1.3 Specified strength in compression parallel to grain, fc, for flanges
The specified strength in compression parallel to grain, fc, for flanges shall be determined asfollows:
a) When the flange material is sawn lumber meeting the requirements of Clause 6.2 or glued-laminated
timber meeting the requirements of Clause 7.2, the specified strength in compression
parallel to grain shall be determined from fcin Clause 6.3 or fcin Table 7.2, respectively.
b) When the flange material is not as described in Item a), fcshall be calculated as follows:
fc =cKr

where
c=characteristic value for compression parallel to grain, MPa, asspecified in Clause 16.2.3.5
Kr=reliability normalization factor for bending and tension as specified in Table 16.1
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 665: 16.2.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.2 Specified shear capacity, Vc
The specified shear capacity, Vc, shall be calculated as follows:
Vc =vKr
where
v=characteristic value for shear, N,asspecified in Clause 16.2.3.5
Kr=reliability normalization factor for shear for prefabricated wood I-joists as specified in Table 16.1

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 666: 16.2.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.3.1 General Reaction Capacities
The specified end reaction capacity and the specified intermediate reaction capacity shall be calculated
in accordance with Clauses 16.2.3.3.2 and 16.2.3.3.3, respectively.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 667: 16.2.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.3.2 Specified end reaction capacity, ERc
The specified end reaction capacity, ERc, at aspecified bearing length shall be calculated as
ERc =re Kr
where
re=characteristic value for end reaction asdefined in Clause 16.2.3.5, N
Kr=reliability normalization factor for reaction for prefabricated wood I-joists asspecified in
Table 16.1
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 668: 16.2.3.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.3.3 Specified intermediate reaction capacity, IRc
The specified intermediate reaction capacity, IRc, at aspecified bearing length shall be calculated as
IRc =riKr
where
ri=characteristic value for intermediate reaction asdefined in Clause 16.2.3.5, N
Kr=reliability normalization factor for reaction for prefabricated wood I-joists asspecified in
Table 16.1
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 669: 16.2.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.4 Modulus of elasticity, E,offlange material
The modulus of elasticity, E, offlange material shall be determined as follows:
a) When the flange material is sawn lumber meeting the requirements of Clause 6.2 or glued-laminated
timber meeting the requirements of Clause 7.2, the modulus of elasticity shall be
determined from Clause 6.3 or Table 7.2, respectively.
b) When the flange material is not as described in Item a), the modulus of elasticity shall be the mean
value ofthe modulus of elasticity determined from the test results required by Section 6.6.2.1 of
ASTM D5055.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 670: 16.2.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.3.5 Characteristic values
Characteristic values shall be determined as follows:
a) The maximum characteristic shear value, v,for prefabricated wood I-joists shall be the shear
capacity specified in ASTM D5055 and multiplied by 2.37.

b) The maximum characteristic reaction values for prefabricated wood I-joists shall be the end
reaction capacity, re, and intermediate reaction capacity, rI,for aspecified bearing length, as
defined in ASTM D5055 and multiplied by 2.37.
c) The maximum characteristic value in tension parallel to grain, t,for flanges of prefabricated wood
I-joists shall be taken asfollows:
i) sawn lumber: the flange tensile capacity determined in accordance with ASTM D5055 and
multiplied by 2.1; and
ii) SCL: the characteristic value in tension, tSCL, as specified in Clause 16.3.3.6.
d) The maximum characteristic value in compression parallel to grain, c,for flanges of prefabricated
wood I-joists shall be calculated asfollows:
i) sawn lumber:
c=t(fc1/ft1)
where
fc1 = specified strength in compression parallel to grain as assigned in Clause 6.3 for the
same grade, species combination, and size as ft1
ft1 =closest specified strength toftintension parallel to grain asassigned in Clause 6.3 for
the species combination and size tested in accordance with ASTM D5055
ii) SCL: the characteristic value in compression, c, asspecified in Clause 16.3.3.4.
e) The maximum characteristic value for moment capacity for prefabricated wood I-joists with sawn
lumber or structural composite flanges may be determined in accordance with the empirical
method specified in Section 6of ASTM D5055. Where this method is used, the maximum
characteristic value for moment capacity shall be based on the lower 5% tolerance limit with 75%
confidence.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 671: 16.2.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.1 Adjusted bending moment resistance, M‘
The adjusted bending moment resistance, M‘r of the prefabricated wood I Joists shall be calculated as
M‘r=fa Anet Y
or
M‘r= Mcv Kr
where
fa =specified axial strength for flanges, MPa (see Clause 16.2.3.1)
Anet = net cross-sectional area of one flange, excluding all areas of web material and rout, mm2
Y = distance between the flange centroids with the rout removed, mm
Mcv = characteristic value for moment capacity,N.m as specified in Clause 16.2.3.5 e)
Kr =reliability normalization factor for bending and tension (see Table 16.1)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 672: 16.2.4.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.2.1 General Shear resistance
In the calculation of adjusted shear resistance, the effect of allloads acting on the member shall be
considered, including the loads acting within adistance from asupport equal to the depth ofthe
member. Adjustments to the shear design value near the support shall be substantiated byindependent
testing to the shear capacity criteria specified in ASTM D5055.


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 673: 16.2.4.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.2.2 16.2.4.2.2 Adjusted shear resistance, V’r
The adjusted shear resistance, V’r, of prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated as
V’r= Vc
where
Vc =specified shear capacity for agiven brand and depth ofprefabricated wood I-joist, N,in
accordance with Clause 16.2.3.2
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 674: 16.2.4.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.3.1 General Adjusted reaction resistances
The adjusted end reaction resistance and the adjusted intermediate reaction resistance shall be
calculated in accordance with Clauses 16.2.4.3.2 and 16.2.4.3.3, respectively.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 675: 16.2.4.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.3.2 Adjusted end reaction resistance, ER’r
The adjusted end reaction resistance, ER’r, of prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated as follows:
ER’r =ERc
where
ERc =specified end reaction capacity for agiven brand and depth ofprefabricated wood I-joist, ata
specified bearing length in accordance with Clause 16.2.3.3.2, N
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 676: 16.2.4.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.3.3 Adjusted intermediate reaction resistance, IR’r
The adjusted intermediate reaction resistance, IR’r, of prefabricated wood I-joists shall be calculated as
follows:
IR’r=IRc
where
IRc =specified intermediate reaction capacity for agiven brand and depth of prefabricated wood
I-joist at aspecified bearing length in accordance with Clause 16.2.3.3.3, N
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 677: 16.2.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.4.4 Web openings, minimum bearing length, and web stiffener details
The requirements for web openings, minimum bearing length, and web stiffener details shall be
determined in accordance with ASTM D5055.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 678: 16.2.5 
--------------------------------------------------
16.2.5 Serviceability limit states
Deflection calculations shall include shear deformation.
The flange modulus of elasticity, Es, for stiffness calculations shall be calculated as follows:
Es =E(KSE KTE)
The effective stiffness, EIw, of prefabricated wood I-joist web members employing structural panels as
specified in Clause 9.3 and meeting the requirements of CSA O121, CSA O151, or CSA O325 shall be
calculated as follows:
EI_w = (ΣB_α) * (W_D^3 / 12) * K_SE * K_TE

The shear-through-thickness rigidity,WS, ofstructural panels as specified in Clause 9.3 that are used as
web members of prefabricated wood I-joists and meeting the requirements of CSA O121, CSA O151, or
CSA O325 shall be calculated as follows:
WS =Bv KSG KTG
where
E =specified modulus ofelasticity offlange material (see Clause 16.2.3.4)
KSE =service-condition factor for modulus of elasticity
    = 1.0 for dry-service conditions
KTE =treatment factor for modulus of elasticity
    =1.0 for untreated prefabricated wood I-joists (see Clause 15.2.2.3)
Ba =axial stiffness (tension orcompression) from Table 9.1, 9.2, or9.3, N/mm
Wd =shear-through-thickness rigidity from Table 9.1, 9.2, or 9.3, N/mm
KSG =service-condition factor for shear-through-thickness rigidity
    =1.0 for dry-service conditions
KTG =treatment factor for shear-through-thickness rigidity
    =1.0 for untreated prefabricated wood I-joists
Note: For axial web stiffness and web shear-through-thickness rigidity for products not covered by Table 9.1, 9.2,
or 9.3, refer to appropriate standards or documented test data which can be obtained from the manufacturer of
the prefabricated wood I-joists.

--------------------------------------------------

16.3.3.1 General
Specified strengths and modulus of elasticity for SCL for use in accordance with this Standard shall be

Clause 685: 16.3.3.2

16.3.3.2 Specified bending strength, fb
The specified bending strength, fb, for SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
fb =FB Kr
where
FB =characteristic value for bending, MPa, determined in accordance with ASTM D5456
Kr =reliability normalization factor for bending and tension (see Table 16.1)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 686: 16.3.3.3

The specified shear strength, fv, for SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
fv =vSCL Kr
where
vSCL = characteristic value for shear, MPa, determined in accordance with ASTM D5456
Kr =reliability normalization factor for shear for SCL (see Table 16.1)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 687: 16.3.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
16.3.3.4 Specified compression strength parallel to grain, fc
The specified compression strength parallel to grain, fc, for SCL shall be calculated as follows:
fc =cKr
where
c=characteristic value in compression parallel to grain, MPa, as determined in accordance with
ASTM D5456
Kr=reliability normalization factor for compression parallel to grain (see Table 16.1)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 688: 16.3.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
16.3.3.5 Specified compression strength perpendicular to grain, fcp
The specified compression strength perpendicular to grain, fcp, MPa, for SCL shall not exceed the
following:
a) the characteristic value determined in accordance with ASTM D5456 and multiplied by 1.09 in the
edgewise (L-Y plane, as defined in ASTM D5456) orientation; and
b) the characteristic value determined in accordance with ASTM D5456 and multiplied by 1.81 in the
flatwise (L-X plane, as defined in ASTM D5456) orientation.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 689: 16.3.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------

The specified strength in tension parallel to grain, ft, for SCL shall be calculated as follows:
ft =tSCL Kr
where
tSCL = characteristic value in tension parallel to grain, MPa, as determined in accordance with
ASTM D5456
Kr =reliability normalization factor for bending and tension (see Table 16.1)

The specified modulus of elasticity, E,for SCL shall be the mean value determined in accordance with
ASTM D5456.

Clause 691: 16.3.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
16.3.4.1 Size factor in bending, KZb
The size factor in bending, KZb, for SCL shall be calculated asfollows:SS
K_ZB = (d₁ / d)^(1/n)
where
d1 =specified depth on which the published specified strength in bending, fb,is based
d = depth of application member
n =parameter specified inSection 7.4.1.3 of ASTM D5456

Clause 692: 16.3.4.2

The size factor in tension, KZt, for SCL shall be calculated asfollows:
K_Zt = (L₁ / L)^(1/m)
where
L1 = base length between test grips, determined in accordance with Section 5.5.2 of ASTM D5456
L =end use length
m = parameter determined in accordance with Annex A1 of ASTM D5456

Clause 693: 16.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
16.3.5 16.3.5 Serviceability limit states
Deflection calculations shall include shear deformation.
The member modulus of elasticity, Es, for stiffness calculations shall be calculated asfollows:
Es =E(KSE KTE)
where
E =specified modulus ofelasticity, MPa, in accordance with Clause 16.3.3.7
KSE =service-condition factor for modulus of elasticity
    =1.0 for dry-service conditions
KTE =treatment factor for modulus of elasticity
    =1.0 for untreated SCL
The shear modulus or modulus ofrigidity, GS, for stiffness calculations shall be calculated asfollows:
GS =G(KSG KTG)
where
G =specified shear modulus or modulus ofrigidity, MPa, established by testing or as published in a
recognized reference for the SCL wood species
KSG =service-condition factor for shear modulus
    =1.0 for dry-service conditions
KTG =treatment factor for shear modulus
    = 1.0 for untreated SCL

Clause 698: 16.4.2.1

16.4.2.1 Ultimate lateral resistance ofteeth
Ultimate lateral resistance values pu, qu, p,q,u shall be obtained from tests carried out in 
accordancewith CSA S347 and calculated as follows

nu =0.8 Rc BKmu Kpu
where
nu=ultimate lateral resistance values pu, qu, pu, or q'u
Rc=the lesser ofthe following:
a) Ru(1 –2.104 CV)
b) 0.753 Ru
where
Ru=average ultimate lateral resistance from the test data 
CV = coefficient of variation ofthe test data
where
B = 1.44 –2.18 CV, but not greater than 1.1
Kmu = moisture response factor for ultimate strength
= 0.83 for sawn lumber to sawn lumber connections
= determined in accordance with CSA S347 for SCL to SCL connections, and sawn lumber to SCL
connections
Kpu =roller press modification factor for ultimate strength determined in accordance with CSA S347
Note: Where the moisture response factor for SCL to sawn lumber isless than 0.83, two values of nu will be
calculated for sawn lumber connections, one value for sawn lumber to sawn lumber connections and another value

tp =tuL CF

where

The shear resistance ofthe plate, vp, shall be determined for specified angles of plate axis to load

vp=vuL CF
where

CF = correction factor for strength of plate material from CSA S347
For all other angles, shear resistance shall be determined bylinear interpolation.

ns=(Rs/1.2) Kps Kms
where
ns=lateral slip values ps, qs, p‘s,orq‘s

CSA S347
Kps=roller press modification factor for slip, determined in accordance with CSA S347
Kmss= moisture response factor for slip
    = 0.83 for sawn lumber to sawn lumber connections
    =determined in accordance with CSA S347 for SCL to SCL connections, and sawn lumber to SCL
    connections

Note: Where the moisture response factor for sawn lumber to SCL isless than 0.83, two values ofns will be
calculated for sawn lumber connections, one value for sawn lumber to sawn lumber and another value for sawn
lumber to SCL.

Note: Galvanizing may be carried out before manufacturing and should conform to minimum G90 galvanizing
class.sshall be obtained from tests carried out in accordance with
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 703: 16.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.5.2 Testing
The design requirements specified in Clause 16.5 are for joist hangers tested for vertical load capacity in
accordance with ASTM D7147. Aset of atleast three tests (six hangers) shall be conducted for each
possible variation ofthe hanger, wood material, and fasteners, including
a) joist species, size, and type;
b) header species, size, and type;
c) joist hanger size and type; and
d) fastener size, type, and spacing.
For sawn wood and glued-laminated timber joists and headers, the relative density ofthe material used
in testing shall not be greater than 2% above the mean relative density values for the material tested.
For manufactured wood products, the relative density shall not be greater than 2% above the average
ofthe population. The moisture content of sawn wood atthe time oftesting shall be no less than 11%.
For wood products that are manufactured, installed, and maintained at or below 15% moisture content,
the tests shall be made at amoisture content of no less than 7%. To allow for relaxation effects, atleast
one week shall elapse between assembly and testing ofthe specimens.
Note: Mean relative density values for sawn wood and glued-laminated timber are provided in Table A.11.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 704: 16.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
16.5.3 Ultimate resistance ofjoist hangers
The ultimate resistance ofjoist hangers shall be obtained from vertical load tests on atleast three pairs
of hangers conducted in accordance with Clause 16.5.2. The ultimate resistance shall be calculated as
follows:
a) for fewer than 10 pairs of hangers, the lesser of
i)the corrected ultimate load per hanger calculated in accordance with Clause 16.5.4, multiplied
by 0.91; or
ii) the average load per hanger at which the vertical movement between the joist and the header
is 3mm, multiplied by 2.42.
b) for 10 or more pairs of hangers, the lesser of
i)the corrected ultimate load per hanger calculated in accordance with Clause 16.5.4, multiplied
by 1.2; or
ii) the average load per hanger at which the vertical movement between the joist and the header
is 3 mm, multiplied by 2.42.
--------------------------------------------------

The corrected ultimate load per hanger obtained from testing on atleast three pairs of hangers shall be
the lower of
a) Nult CFw; and
b) Nult steel CFs.

Clause 707: 16.5.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
16.5.4.2 Multiple species testing
The corrected ultimate load per hanger obtained from testing on atleast six pairs of hangers where the
only difference in test setup isthe species of wood (at least three pairs of hangers per species) shall be
the lower of
a) Nult CFw per species; and
b) Nult steel CFs.

For testing where failure ofthe hanger steel does not occur, the highest ultimate load per assembly in
place ofthe Nult steel in Clauses 16.5.4.1 b)and 16.5.4.2 b)shall be used
where
CFw= Nrspec /Nr test 1.0
CFs=fuspec /fu test 1.0
fuspec=specified minimum tensile strength ofthe hanger steel
futest=tensile strength ofthe hanger steel, measured in accordance with ASTM E8/E8M

per Clause 12 using fuspec in place of fu
Nrtest=factored lateral resistance ofthe joint used to attach the hanger tothe header calculated
per Clause 12 using futest in place of fu
