Clause 15: A.6.5.5.2.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.2.4 Factored compressive resistance parallel to grain
Except for members designed in accordance with Clause 6.5.12, the following procedure may be used to
determine the factored compressive resistance parallel to grain of members subject to acompressive
stress that is not uniform along its length, either due to concentrated loads or distributed loads:
a) Divide the member into two sections with lengths L1and L2asfollows:
L1=length of member with amaximum factored compressive force Pf1, mm
L2=length of member with amaximum factored compressive force Pf2, mm
such that Pf1 <Pf2
b) Determine the factored compressive resistance parallel to grain, Pr1, ofsection L1in accordance
with Clause 6.5.5.2.4 using L=L1+L2inthe calculation ofKZc.
c) Determine the factored compressive resistance parallel to grain, Pr2, ofsection L2in accordance
with Clause 6.5.5.2.4 using the following formula:
KZc =6.3 (d L’)-0.13<1.3
where
d=dimension in direction ofbuckling (depth or width), mm
L’=L1(Pf1/Pf2)7.9 +L2, mm
d) Verify that Pr1 Pf1, and Pr2 Pf2. For combined bending and compression, separately check Pf1 and
Pf2 using Pr1 and Pr2in Clause 6.5.9.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 16: A.6.5.5.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.1 General
Spaced compression members shall consist oftwo or more individual members joined with connectors
and having spacer and end blocks as specified in Clauses A.6.5.5.3.2 to A.6.5.5.3.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 17: A.6.5.5.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.2 Spacer and end blocks
Spacer and end blocks shall meet the following requirements:
a) End blocks shall be placed so that end and edge distances and spacing, as required by Clause 12 for
the size and number of connectors, are maintained in end blocks and in individual members.
Connectors shall be placed so that the limits specified in Clause A.6.5.5.3.3, depending on the fixity
factor assumed, are met. In compression members oftrusses, apanel point that is braced laterally
may be considered asthe end ofthe spaced member.
b) Asingle spacer block shall belocated within the middle 10% ofthe length ofthe compression
members; when so located, connectors shall not be necessary for this block. When more than one
spacer block is used, the distance between any two blocks shall not exceed one-half the distance
between centres ofconnectors in the end blocks. When two or more spacer blocks are used,
connectors shall meet the requirements ofItem a).
c) The thickness of spacer and end blocks shall not be less than that ofthe individual members ofthe
spaced compression member, except that spacer and end blocks of athickness between that ofthe
individual members and one-half that thickness may be used, provided that the length ofthe
blocks is made inversely proportional to the thickness in relation to the required length offull-thickness
block. Spacer and end block sizes shall be adequate to develop the strength required by
Clause 12.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 18: A.6.5.5.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.3 Fixity classes
The end-fixity of spaced compression members shall be classified as one ofthe following in accordance
with Figure A.2:
a) Condition A:the centroid of connectors or ofthe connector group in the end block shall be within
1/20 ofthe length, L,from the end ofthe member.
b) Condition B:the centroid ofconnectors or ofthe connector group in the end block shall be
between 1/20 and 1/10 ofthe length, L,from the end ofthe member.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 19: A.6.5.5.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.4 Connectors in end blocks
The connectors in each pair of contacting surfaces of end blocks and individual members at each end of
aspaced compression member shall be atleast of asize and number to provide afactored strength
resistance, in newtons, equal to the required cross-sectional area in square millimetres of one ofthe
individual members multiplied by the appropriate end block constant specified in Table A.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 20: A.6.5.5.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5 Factored compressive resistance parallel to grain
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 21: A.6.5.5.3.5.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5.1 General
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, parallel to grain ofaspaced member shall bethe smaller value
calculated in Clauses A.6.5.5.3.5.2 and A.6.5.5.3.5.5.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 22: A.6.5.5.3.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5.2 Resistance ofspaced compression member
The factored compressive resistance, Pr, parallel to grain ofaspaced compression member shall be
calculated as follows:

Pr= φFc AKcKZc
where
φ=resistance factor
    = 0.80 for sawn lumber
    =0.90 for glued-laminated timber
Fc=fc(KD KSc KT)
where
fc =specified strength incompression parallel tograin, MPa (see Tables 6.4to6.9forsawn
lumber and Table 7.2 for glulam)
A =total cross-sectional area of members, mm2
KC =slenderness factor (see Clause A.6.5.5.3.5.4)
KZc =size factor
    =6.3(dL)–0.13 <1.3 for sawn lumber
    =1.0 for glued-laminated timber
where
d = member dimension in direction ofbuckling (depth or width), mm
L =length of member, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 23: A.6.5.5.3.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5.3 Slenderness ratio, CC
The slenderness ratio, CC, ofspaced compression members of uniform rectangular section shall not
exceed 80 and shall be calculated as follows:

Cc = (actual length between points of a lateral support)/(least dimension of the individual member)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 24: A.6.5.5.3.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5.4 Slenderness factor, KC
The slenderness factor, KC, depending on CC(Clause A.6.5.5.3.5.3), shall becalculated asfollows:
a) When C_C does not exceed 10:
   K_C = 1.00

b) When C_C is greater than 10 but does not exceed C_K:
   K_C = 1 - (1/3) * (C_C / C_K)^4

   Where:
     C_K = (0.76 * E_05 * K_SE * K_E * K_T) / F_C

     Where:
       E_05 = applicable value from Tables 6.4 to 6.7 for visually graded sawn lumber
           = 0.82E for machine stress-rated lumber
           = 0.87E for glued-laminated timber

       K_E = end-fixity factor (see Clause A.6.5.5.3.3)
           = 2.50 for Condition A
           = 3.00 for Condition B

c) When C_C is greater than C_K but does not exceed 80:
   [Further conditions not shown in image snippet]
K_c = (E_05 * K_SE * K_E * K_T) / (K_C * C_C² * F_C)
where
k = 1.8 for sawn lumber
    =2.0 for glued-laminated timber
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 25: A.6.5.5.3.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.5.5 Total resistance ofindividual members
The factored resistance ofspaced compression members shall be checked against the sum offactored
resistances ofindividual members taken assimple compression members where CCshall betaken as
follows:
Cc = (actual length between points of lateral support)/(larger dimension of an individual member)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 26: A.6.5.5.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.5.3.6 Combined bending and axial load
When axial compression in spaced compression members is combined with bending stresses,
Clause 6.5.9 shall be used only ifthe bending isin adirection parallel to the larger dimension ofthe
individual member.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 27: A.6.5.6 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.6 Compression perpendicular to grain
A relationship between mean compressive strength perpendicular to grain and mean oven-dry wood
density was introduced to establish aconsistent basis for bearing strengths for various products in the
1994 edition ofthis Standard. Itis asfollows:
fcp =0.9L(2243.8G –473.8)/M
where
fcp =specified strength incompression perpendicular to grain, MPa
0.9 =factor applied to obtain alower tolerance limit
L =conversion factor to limit states desing and standard term load duration
    =1.8125
G = mean oven-dry relative density
M = conversion factor for metric units
    = 145.038
Tables 6.8 and 6.9 assign increased compression perpendicular to grain design values to specific grades
of Spruce-Pine-Fir or Hem-Fir machine-graded lumber, which have higher mean density than visually
stress-graded lumber of the same species (see Table A.11).

The NLGA Standard Grading Rules for Canadian Lumber also includes provisions for mills producing any
grade of machine-graded lumber to qualify for other density values based on tests, daily quality control,
and marking the qualified density value on the lumber. In these cases the rules provide for compression
perpendicular values to be based on the marked density value and the formula specified in this Clause,
without the 0.9 tolerance limit.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 28: A.6.5.9 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.9 A.6.5.9 Combined bending and compressive loads
Members subject to combined bending and compressive loads may be designed using the alternative
interaction equation:
(Pf / Pr)² + (Mf + Pf * ΔL) / Mr * [1 / (1 - Pf / PE)] ≤ 1
Where:
Pf = factored compressive axial load, N

Pr = factored compressive load resistance parallel to grain, N (per Clause 6.5.5)

Mf = factored bending moment, N·mm

ΔL = lateral deflection calculated using serviceability load combinations

PE = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied moment
  = (π² * E₀₅ * K_SE * K_f * I) / Le²

  Where:
  - E₀₅ = modulus of elasticity for design of compression members, MPa
  - I = moment of inertia in the plane of the applied moment, mm⁴
  - Le = effective length in the plane of the applied moment
    = K_e * L
      Where:
      - K_e = effective-length factor (Table A.4)
Mr = factored bending moment resistance (Clause 6.5.3), N·mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 29: A.6.5.11.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1 General Permanent wood foundations
Studs for permanent wood foundations may be designed in accordance with recognized engineering
methods. When assumed to be laterally supported and when no surcharge exists, the formulas specified
in Clauses A.6.5.11.1.5 to A.6.5.11.1.10 give conservative approximations for practical construction. The
dimensions used in the formulas are identified in Figure A.3.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 30: A.6.5.11.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.1 Studs
Studs for exterior foundation walls may be designed as members subjected to combined bending and
axial compressive loading. Deflection due to lateral and axial loads should not exceed 1/300 ofthe
unsupported height ofthe stud.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 31: A.6.5.11.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.2 Sheathing
Sheathing for exterior foundation walls may be designed assimple bending members. The calculated
maximum deflection at apoint 300 mm above the bottom ofthe sheathing should not exceed 1/180 of
the span ofsheathing between studs. The nominal thickness of sheathing should not be less than
12.5 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 32: A.6.5.11.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.3 Floors and connections
Floors and connections between floors and walls shall be designed to withstand loads imposed on them
by lateral soil pressure as well as floor loads appropriate for the occupancy.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 33: A.6.5.11.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.4 Unequal pressure distribution
Unequal pressure distribution can result from differing backfill heights on opposite sides ofabuilding,
openings in foundation walls, openings in floors at the top offoundation walls, or other causes. Framing
members and sheathing shall be designed as diaphragms or other systems to resist loads resulting from
unequal pressure distribution.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 34: A.6.5.11.1.5 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.5 Combined bending and compressive load effects
Combined bending and compressive load effects may be evaluated using the following formula:

(Pf / Pr)^2 + (Mf / Mr) * [1 / (1 - Pf / PE)] ≤ 1

Where:
  Pf = factored compressive load on stud, N
  Pr = factored compressive resistance (Clause 6.5.5.2.4), N
  Mf = maximum factored bending moment on stud (Clause A.6.5.11.1.6), N·mm
  Mr = factored bending moment resistance (Clause 6.5.3.1), N·mm
     = (π² * E05 * K_SE * K_I * I) / Le²

  PE = Euler buckling load in the plane of the applied moment

Where (for PE and Mr):
  E05 = modulus of elasticity for compression design, MPa
  I   = moment of inertia in the plane of the applied moment, mm⁴
  Le  = effective length in the plane of the applied moment
      = K_e * L
        where K_e = effective-length factor (Table A.4)

Note:
A KD factor of 0.65 applies to the calculation of Mr,
and a KD factor of 1.0 applies to the calculation of Pr.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 35: A.6.5.11.1.6 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.6 Factored bending moment on astud
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 36: A.6.5.11.1.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.6.1 General
The following formula, which is derived from recognized engineering formulas, may be used to calculate
the maximum bending moment on astud, Mf, due tofactored lateral load (see Clause A.6.5.11.1.6.2).
Atany point, x,above the floor, the factored bending moment due tofactored lateral load, Mfx, in
N•mm, is calculated as follows:
M_fk = (w_f * H² / 6L) * [ (H - 3a) * (L - x)/H - L * ((H - Ax)/H)^3 ]

Where:
  w_f = maximum factored lateral load per stud, N/mm
      = maximum factored lateral soil pressure, N/mm², times stud spacing, mm
  H, L, a, and x = variables shown in Figure A.3, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 37: A.6.5.11.1.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.6.2 Maximum factored bending moment on astud, Mf
The following formulas may be used to determine the maximum factored bending moment, M_f, and its location, x:

a) For wood sleeper and slab floors:
  M_f = (w_f * H² / 6L) * [L - H + (2/3) * (H³ / 3L)^(1/2)]
  x = H - (H³ / 3L)^(1/2)

b) For suspended floors:
  M_f = (w_f * H² / 6L) * K_m

Where:
  K_m = (H - 3a) * [K_1 + (L + a - H)/H - L * K_1³]

Where K₁ is determined as follows:

  i) Between supports:
     K₁ = (H - 3a / 3L)^(1/2)
     x = H - a - H * (H - 3a / 3L)^(1/2)

  ii) At the support:
     K₁ = (H - a) / H and x = 0

Note: Values of K_m for a range of backfill heights and typical wall dimensions are specified in Table A.6.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 38: A.6.5.11.1.7 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.7 Deflection ofstuds,
The deflection ofstuds, ,can be calculated atany point, x,above the basement floor (see Figure A.3),
using the following formula:
Δ = (w_f * (L - x) * K_Δ) / (360 * E * I * L * H)

Where:
  w_f = variable shown in Figure A.3, N/mm

  K_Δ = [10 * H² * (H - 3a) * (2L - x) * x - 3 * (H - a)^5 + K₂]

    Where:
      K₂ = (3L / (L - x)) * (H - a - x)^5   when x ≤ H - a
         = 0                                when x > H - a

  E = modulus of elasticity of stud, MPa


I = moment ofinertia ofstud in the plane ofthe applied moment, mm4
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 39: A.6.5.11.1.8 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.8 Maximum deflection ofstuds
Maximum deflection may be calculated from Clause A.6.5.11.1.7 with x=0.45L and using specified
rather than factored loads to give agood approximation ofthe theoretical maximum deflection.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 40: A.6.5.11.1.9 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.9 Maximum factored shear force, Vf, per stud
The maximum factored shear force, Vf,in N,per stud may betaken asthe greatest value calculated
from the following formulas, which are derived from recognized engineering formulas:
a) For wood sleeper and slab floors at the bottom of the foundation wall:
   Vf = (w_f * H / 2) * [H / (3L) - ((H - d) / H)^2]

b) For suspended floors:
   i) Just above the suspended floor:
      Vf = (w_f * H / 2) * [(H - 3a) / (3L) - ((H - a - c) / H)^2]

   ii) Just below the suspended floor:
      Vf = (w_f * H / 2) * [1 - ((H - a + c) / H)^2]

Where:
  w_f = variable shown in Figure A.3, N/mm
  d   = depth of stud, mm
  c   = depth of stud + 1/2 of the joist depth, mm
  H, L, a = variables shown in Figure A.3, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 41: A.6.5.11.1.10.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.10.1 A.6.5.11.1.10.1 Lateral restraint attop
The lateral restraint required atthe top ofthe foundation wall may be calculated from the following
formulas:
a) for wood sleeper and slab floors:
RT = (wfH^2)/6L
b) for suspended floors:
Rt = (wf H /(2L))*(H/3-a)

where
RT=inward reaction atthe top ofthe stud, N
wf= variable shown in Figure A.3, N/mm
H,L,a=variables shown in Figure A.3, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 42: A.6.5.11.1.10.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.11.1.10.2 Lateral restraint at bottom
The lateral restraint required atthe bottom ofthe foundation wall may be calculated from the following
formulas:
a) for wood sleeper and slab floors:
RB = wfH/2L * (L-H/3)
b) for suspended floors:
RB=wfH/2L * (L+a-H/3)

where
RB=inward reaction atthe bottom ofthe stud, N
wf= variable shown in Figure A.3, N/mm
H,L,a=variables shown in Figure A.3, mm
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 43: A.6.5.12.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.12.1 Scope Specific truss applications
Fully triangulated —The modified design procedures of Clause 6.5.12* apply only to sawn lumber used
in trusses where all the members form aside of atriangle. In such asystem, abending failure at apanel
point of acompression member would not normally result in collapse ofthe triangle. An attic truss is
not afully triangulated system. Also, the ends oftop chords in top-chord-bearing trusses, and top-chord
overhangs (i.e., outward extensions oftruss chords beyond the panel points) do not fall within the
scope of Clause A.6.5.12 and therefore are not considered part ofthe overall truss length.
*The modified design procedures ofClause 6.5.12 are based onresearch reported in C.Lum, E.Jones, and B. Hintz
(1996).
Clear span limitation —The 12.2 mclear span limitation is consistent with that for snow loading for
National Building Code of Canada Part 9structures (see Subsection 9.4.2). When the 12.2 mspan limit
is exceeded or when other conditions are in effect, an 80% snow load factor shall be used (i.e., the truss
is designed as aPart 4truss). When the 610 mm spacing limit is exceeded, the 80% snow load factor
shall be used and the KHfactor isreduced from 1.1 to 1.0.
Truss configuration —Clause A.6.5.12 limits the applicability of Clause 6.5.12 to roof trusses with
slopes that are similar to those trusses tested. Compared to the standard pitched chord trusses
evaluated in the testing program, very low pitch (less than 2in 12) roof and flat trusses have ahigher
axial force to bending moment ratio and are excluded from coverage in this Standard.
The overall length is alimit that the truss industry has traditionally used to place additional limits on
design. The two limits, 12.2 mclear span and the 18.0 moverall length, provide aboundary between
traditional residential spans and long span roof trusses. Below the 18.0 moverall truss length limit, the
truss may consist ofcantilevers or multiple clear spans, or both, provided that no single span exceeds
12.2 m.
Girder, bowstring, semi-circular, attic, flat, and floor trusses are outside the scope of Clause A.6.5.12.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 44: A.6.5.12.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.12.3 Compressive resistance parallel to grain
Effective length —Recommended effective-length factors are specified in Table A.4. TPIC also provides
recommendations on the effective length oftruss compression members. Factor selection depends on
the load distribution and the type ofstructure.
Compression-chord splices —For strength and deflection calculations, acompression-chord splice may
be considered continuous ifitislocated at aninflection point for the load case being considered. To
allow for changes in lumber length, the splice need only be within ±10% ofthe panel length from the
inflection point. This allowance also recognizes that the location ofthe inflection point will depend on
the loading condition.
Size effects incompression —In most cases, the member length for computing KZcisthe panel length;
between panel points, the axial force changes little compared with changes at the panel points. In cases
where the axial stresses are high relative to the bending stresses, resulting in relatively short panel
lengths, and where the axial forces are relatively constant between adjacent panels, the member length
for computing KZc should include several panels. One-half the chord length between pitch breaks has
been judged to cover these cases.
Note: Apitch break is apoint along the chord analogue line where the slope ofthe chord changes.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 45: A.6.5.12.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.12.4 Compressive resistance perpendicular to grain
Bearing reinforcement —Bearing reinforcement consists ofapplying truss plates to both sides of a
member that can be subjected to compression perpendicular to grain stresses through the depth ofthe
member. Designs also need to meet the basic bearing requirement of Clause 6.5.6.1.
Note: Testing to support this method ofimproving the bearing resistance is described in Bulmanis, N.S., Latos,
H. A., and Keenan F.J.(1983).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 46: A.6.5.12.5 
--------------------------------------------------
A.6.5.12.5 Resistance to combined bending and axial load
Amplified moments —The proposed design procedures have been written to cover the general case
where amplified moments are used. Although moment amplification should not be ignored, some
structures can be accurately analyzed without having to use analysis methods that include moment
amplification. An analysis of moment amplification in trusses indicated that mid-panel moments were
more susceptible to P-delta effects, while panel point moments were less susceptible. Furthermore, the
amount of moment amplification calculated is sensitive to the type ofstructure and the analogue
assumptions.
Results from the testing program suggest that the design procedure used by TPIC results in trusses that
exhibit satisfactory levels of performance. The TPIC design approach does not include moment
amplification; however, the procedure does require that the mid-panel deflection be limited. This, in
effect, limits the length oftruss panels, even though the chord member can possess the required
strength. Ifthe deflection limitations in TPIC are not used tolimit panel length, itis possible that the
bending capacity modification factor, KM, from Table 6.19 will not be appropriate.
Bending capacity modification factor, KM —In addition to being afunction ofthe member’s span-to-depth
ratio, the KM factor, calculated from Table 6.19,* also depends on the shape ofthe moment
diagram.
AKMfactor greater than 1generally indicates abending moment distribution with one or more
inflection points in the member between panel points, and apanel point moment that is higher than
the mid-panel moment.

For cases where the mid-panel moment is higher than the panel point moments or where the loading is
such that there are noinflection points inthe panel, the KMfactor isgenerally less than 1.
For other cases where the structural analysis indicates zero moment atthe panel points (i.e., M2 =0),
the bending capacity increase will simply be afunction ofthe span-to-depth ratio. This generally occurs
at pitch breaks or panel point splices, where, although the bending moments are not necessarily zero,
designers traditionally assume apin connection. However, afictitious analogue member, such as that
used to model aheel joint in apitched chord truss, is considered to introduce apanel point moment in
the heel. Therefore, the top chord of aking post truss can be assumed to be continuous over apanel
point atthe heel, but not atthe peak.
The test trusses and trusses analyzed in the impact study, which are considered typical designs, result in
values of KM up to 1.3. The upper limit on KM at 1.3 has been introduced to prevent extrapolation to
higher values.
*The KM factors calculated from Table 6.19 are based on Lau, W., Barrett, J. D., and Lam, F.(1995).
Interaction equation —The modification to the axial ratio term was introduced to recognize the
increase in bending capacity when abrittle material is subjected to axial compression in addition to
bending. The KM factor is used to adjust the bending capacity for various moment configurations in the
top chords.
These two changes to the design of compression chords help to explain the satisfactory levels of safety
observed in the test trusses.
No increase is permitted for combined tension and bending members, asthe testing program was not
designed to evaluate the performance of tension chord members.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 47: A.7.5.5 
--------------------------------------------------
A.7.5.5 Standard sizes for glued-laminated timber-GLM
The standard dimensions for glued-laminated timber are asfollows:
a) widths of 80, 130, 175, 215, 265, 315, and 365 mm; and
b) depths, as calculated for
i)straight or cambered members, in multiples of38 mm; and
ii) members curved to aradius of curvature less than 10 800 mm, in multiples ofthe required
lamination thickness (see Table A.7).
Notes:
1) Commercially available widths can vary.
2)For widths greater than 365 mm, designers should check availability before specifying.


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 48: A.8.5.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.8.5.2 Deflection of CLT panels -Cross laminated Timber (CLT)
The maximum deflection ofaCLT panel, max, may be calculated as the sum of deflections under short-and
long-term loads asfollows:
Δ_max = Δ_ST + Δ_LT * K_creep

Where:
  Δ_ST    = elastic deflection due to short-term and/or standard-term loads, without dead loads in combination
  Δ_LT    = instantaneous elastic deflection due to long-term loads
  K_creep = creep adjustment factor
          = 2.0 for dry-service condition

Deflection under a specified uniformly distributed load, ω, acting perpendicular to the face of a single-span panel
may be calculated as the sum of the deflections due to moment and shear effects using:

- Effective flatwise bending stiffness, (EI)_eff,f
- Effective shear stiffness in flatwise bending, (GA)_eff,f

Formula:
Δ = (5 / 384) * (ω * L⁴ / (EI)_eff,f) + (1 / 8) * (ω * L² / (GA)_eff,f)

For aconcentrated line load, P,located inthe middle ofasingle span CLT panel acting perpendicular to
the panel, the deflection may be calculated as follows:
Δ = (1/48) * (P * L³) / (EI)_eff,f + (1/4) * (P * L) / (GA)_eff,f

Note: Where the shear deformation component ofthe total deformation of CLT panel under out-of-plane standard-term
loading such assnow and live loads issignificant (i.e., in short spans, short span cantilever, etc.) as
determined by the designer, the shear deformation under these loads should be increased by 30% to account for
time-dependent effect associated with rolling shear.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 49: A.8.5.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.8.5.3 A.8.5.3 Vibration performance ofCLT floors
The allowable span for the control offloor motions caused by walking on aCLT floor may be calculated
using the following equation:

ℓ_v ≤ 0.11 * [(EI)_eff,f / 10⁶]^0.29 / m^0.12

Where:
  ℓ_v        = vibration-controlled span limit, m
  (EI)_eff,f = effective flatwise bending stiffness for a 1 m wide panel, N·mm² (see Clause 8.4.3.2)
  m          = linear mass of CLT for a 1 m wide panel, kg/m

Note: The above equation assumes the floor:
  a) has a single span with both ends simply supported; and
  b) is bare with no topping material.

For multiple-span floors with anon-structural element that is considered to provide enhanced vibration
effect, the calculated vibration-controlled span may beincreased by up to 20%, provided itis not
greater than 8 m.
Notes:
1) The calculation procedure given in this Clause for single-span systems may be applied to individual spans in a
multiple-span system, with adjustment if appropriate.
2) For floors with concrete topping, where the concrete is applied directly tothe CLT panel, this equation may be
used assuming bare floor construction for calculation purposes, i.e., weight ofconcrete isignored in
calculating the mass, m,provided the area density ofthe topping is not greater than twice the bare CLT floor
area density.
3) The current vibration criteria might not address all occupant performance expectations. CLT manufacturer
literature may provide additional span adjustments.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 50: A.9.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.9.2.2 Construction sheathing OSB-Structural Panels
As noted inits preface, CSA O325 does not recommend engineering design values, nor does itsuggest
methods ofcalculating such values.
The design values in Table 9.3 for construction sheathing OSB that complies with CSA O325 are
consistent with values developed through in-grade testing and supported by various organizations.
Certification organizations shall ensure that reference values for bending strength and bending stiffness
of construction sheathing OSB that complies with CSA O325 are also consistent with the design values
ofthis Standard.

Panel marks consist of an end-use mark followed by aspan mark (see Table A.8), e.g., 2F24 or W16.
Multiple panel marks may be shown on panels qualified for more than one end use, e.g., 1R24/2F16
and 2R48/2F24/1F24.
Note: See Table A.9.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 51: A.10.6.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.10.6.3.4 Buckling of plywood compression flange - Composite building components
For stressed skin panels with aplywood compression flange, the factored buckling resistance, expressed
asthe maximum factored load applied perpendicular to the compression flange, shall be calculated as
follows:

B_r = φ * X_B * [(2h_w + h_t + h_c)(10^9)] / [2 * (s * ℓ_p)^2]

Where:
  B_r = factored buckling resistance, kN/m²
  φ   = 0.95
  X_B = buckling coefficient (see Table A.10)
  s   = clear spacing between longitudinals, mm
  ℓ_p = span of stressed skin panel, mm

Note:
This Clause is not applicable to OSB compression flanges. Buckling coefficients have not been developed for OSB.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 52: A.11.7 
--------------------------------------------------
A.11.7 A.11.7 Sheathing-to-framing connection deformation, en, for shearwall and
diaphragm deflection calculations
For nails used in wood-based sheathing with dry lumber, en may be calculated asfollows:
e_n = [0.013 * v * s / d_f²]²

Where:
  v  = maximum specified shear force per unit length along the diaphragm boundary or top of shearwall, N/mm
  s  = nail spacing along panel edges, mm

- For nails used in wood-based sheathing with green lumber, multiply the dry lumber e_n values by 2.
- For fasteners used in gypsum wallboard with dry lumber, e_n may be taken as 0.76 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 53: A.11.7.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.11.7.1 Deflection of shearwalls in multi-storey buidlings
a) Deflection of blocked shearwall segments:
  The interstorey drift, Δ_i^storey, at the i-th level, mm, may be calculated as follows:
Δ_i^storey = Δ_b,i^storey + Δ_s,i^storey + Δ_n,i^storey + Δ_a,i^storey

Where:
  Δ_b,i^storey = drift at i-th level due to bending
  Δ_s,i^storey = drift at i-th level due to panel shear
  Δ_n,i^storey = drift at i-th level due to nail slip
  Δ_a,i^storey = drift at i-th level due to wall anchorage system elongation

The total deflection Δ_i^total at the i-th level is:

Δ_i^total = Σ_{j=1}^{i} Δ_j^storey

i) Deflection due to bending:
   Δ_b,i^storey = Δ_θ,i + (H_i² / 2) * (θ_i - θ_i-1)

Where:
  θ_i (or θ_j) = change in slope over the i-th storey height:
               = M_i * H_i / (EI)_i

Δ_θ,i = H_i² * q_i / (3 * E_i * I)

Δ_a,i = horizontal distance from top of i-th storey to tangent at the bottom:
       = M_i * H_i² / (2 * E_i * I) + V_i * H_i³ / (3 * E_i * I)

Where:
  H_i = interstorey height of the i-th storey, mm
  V_i = shear force in the i-th storey:
      = Σ_j=1^i F_j = F_1 + F_2 + ... + F_n

  M_i = overturning moment at level i:
      = Σ_j=i+1^n V_j * H_j

  n = total number of stories
  F_j = lateral force at j-th level
  H_j = interstorey height at j-th level

(EI)_i = bending stiffness at the i-th storey:
       = (E * A)_i * (L_s / 2)² * θ² = (EA)_i * t² / 2

Where:
  E = modulus of elasticity at shearwall segment boundary, N/mm²
  A = cross-sectional area of the vertical member, mm²

Ls =length ofshearwall segment, mm
Note: For acontinuous rod system anchored ateach floor level, the effective bending stiffness ofthe
shearwall should be used.

ii) Deflection due to panel shear:
Δ_s,i^storey = Δ_s,i

Where:
  Δ_s,i = v_f,i * H_i / B_v,i

  Where:
    v_f,i = V_i / L_i = maximum shear flow due to specified loads at the top of the wall at the i-th storey, N/mm
    B_v,i = shear-through-thickness rigidity of the sheathing at the i-th storey, N/mm
            (see Tables 9.1 to 9.3 for wood structural panel sheathing)
            For gypsum wallboard, B_v may be taken as 7000 N/mm

iii) Deflection due to sheathing-to-framing connection deformation:
Δ_n,i^storey = Δ_n,i

Where:
  Δ_n,i = 0.0025 * H_i * e_n,i

  Where:
    e_n,i = sheathing-to-framing connection deformation at the i-th storey, mm
            (see Clause A.11.7.1)

iv) Deflection due to elongation in wall anchorage system:
Δ_a,i^storey = H_i * (Σ_{j=i+1}^{n} α_j) = H_i * α_i + H_i * (Σ_{j=1}^{i-1} α_j)

Where:
  α_i = (d_a,i) / L_a

  Where:
    d_a,i = total vertical elongation of the wall anchorage system at the i-th storey
b) Deflection of unblocked shearwall segments:

The interstorey drift of an unblocked shearwall segment with wood structural panels at the i-th storey may be calculated as:

Δ_ub,i^storey = Δ_b,i^storey / J_us,i

Where:
  Δ_ub,i^storey = interstorey drift of a blocked shearwall segment at the i-th level
  J_us,i        = adjustment factor for unblocked shearwall segment at the i-th level

Note: This Clause is appropriate for a typical light-frame wood shearwall cantilevered from its base assuming
the shearwall is stacked for the full height of the building. This is purely a mechanics-based approach to
determine the deflection for a cantilevered single wall acting as a component of the building. There could be
other factors that affect the behaviour of a wall, which should be accounted for by the designer.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 54: A.12.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.1 Scope- Connections 
Refer to table A.11

Notes:
1) Relative density values specified in this Table are based on a mean oven-dry mass and oven-dry volume. In
the connection equations, these values are modified to relate connection resistances to fifth percentile density
values on a15% moisture content volume basis.
2) Where resistance of aconnection with bolts, dowels, drift pins, lag screws, nails, or wood screws in wood of a
given relative density isnot available, use the resistance in alower relative density wood orcalculate
resistance using the equations specified in this Standard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 55: A.12.6.5.4 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.6.5.4 Lateral deformation oflag screw connections
For aspecified load, P,the lateral deformation ofalag screw connection may becalculated as follows:
Δ = P / (k * d_f * t_2 * n_f)

Where:
  Δ   = lateral deformation, mm
  P   = specified load on the connection, N
  k   = lateral slip resistance of a lag screw, MPa

      For θ = 0° (parallel-to-grain):
        k_p = (5.04 * G - 0.29) * J_y * J_G * K_SF

      For θ = 90° (perpendicular-to-grain):
        k_Q = (5.04 * G - 0.29) * J_Q * J_G * K_SF

      For 0° < θ < 90° (angle-to-grain loading):
        k = (k_p * k_Q) / (k_p * sin²θ + k_Q * cos²θ)

Where:
  G    = mean relative density (Table A.11)
  J_y  = side plate factor (1.5 for steel side plates)
  J_G  = group-action factor (Tables 12.2 and 12.3)
  J_Q  = perpendicular-to-grain load factor (Table A.12)
  K_SF = service-condition factor (Table 12.1)
  d_f  = nominal diameter of lag screw, mm
  t_2  = length of penetration into main member, mm (Clause 12.6.3)
  n_f  = number of fasteners in the connection

Note:
Lag screws loaded laterally tend to reach permanent deformation at around 0.8–1.0 mm. This should be avoided.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 56: A.12.7.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.7.3.3 Analysis oftimber rivet joints —General method for Douglas Fir-Larch
glulam
Note: The design formulas in this Clause are derived from tests ontimber rivet (also referred to as “glulam rivet”)
connections in Douglas Fir-Larch glulam. For connections in other species of glulam orin sawn timber, reduce the
resulting strength resistance by the factor Hspecified in Clause 12.7.3.2.=perpendicular-to-grain load factor (see Table A.12)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 57: A.12.7.3.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.7.3.3.1 Parallel-to-grain loading
The specified unit lateral strength resistance for wood capacity, pw, kN, per joint-loaded parallel to grain
is equal to the least value ofthe tensile strength ofthe timber, Pt, and the shear strength ofthe timber,
Pv,calculated asfollows:
a) Pt = (X_t * f_tn * S_Q * (n_R - 1)) / (K_T * β_t * E_t)

Where:
  X_t = adjustment factor for tension parallel to grain (1.41)
  f_tn = specified strength in tension parallel to grain at net section, MPa (see Table 7.2)
  S_Q = rivet spacing perpendicular to grain, mm (Figure 12.13)
  n_R = number of rows of rivets
  K_T = constant depending on n_R and n_C (Table A.13)
    where:
      n_C = number of rivets per row
      β_t = constant based on S_P, S_Q, and n_R (Table A.14)
  S_P = rivet spacing parallel to grain, mm (Figure 12.13)
  E_t = constant based on b and L_p (Table A.15)
    where:
      b = member dimension (single plate: 2× width, double plates: width)
      L_p = length of penetration (Figure 12.12)

b) Pv = (X_v * F_v * [S_p(n_c - 1) + 50]) / (K_v * β_f)

Where:
  X_v = adjustment factor for shear (1.48)
  F_v = f_v (0.15 + 4.35 * C_v), MPa
    where:
      f_v = specified longitudinal shear strength, MPa (Table 7.2)
      C_v = (β_1 * β_2 * β_3)^-0.2

Where:
  β_1 = (1 / 1300) * L_p * (n_C - 1) * [1 + 500 * exp^(-0.52 * (S_p - 12.5))]
  β_2 = 0.5 * 10^-16 * L_p * [(n_C - 1) * S_p]^3 * [(n_R - 1) * S_Q]^4.5 * exp^((a - 50) / 100)
  β_3 = [(3μ / 2 + 1 - μ / 50) * (1 - exp^((1.9 - 0.95 * b) / L_p))]^5

Where:
  a = end distance (Figure 12.13), mm
  μ = 43.9 * [(n_C - 1) * S_p]^-0.4 * [(n_R - 1) * S_Q]^-0.2
  L_p = length of penetration (Figure 12.12)
    K_v  = constant depending on n_R and n_C (Table A.16)
    β_v  = constant depending on S_P and S_Q (Table A.17)
    γ    = 90.5 + 5.4 * L_p

Note: For cases where b ≥ 175 mm, S_P = 40 mm, S_Q = 25 mm, and L_p ≥ 55 mm, P_v will be greater than P_t.


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 58: A.12.7.3.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.7.3.3.2 Perpendicular-to-grain loading
In Clause 12.7.3.3.4, the lateral strength resistance for wood capacity, q_w kN per joint loaded perpendicular to grain and the value of C_t may be calculated as follows:

a) q_w = (23.3 * X_tp * f_tp * (n_C - 1) * S_Q * L_p^0.5) / (K_tp * β_tp * 10^6 * [(n_C - 1) * S_Q]^0.2)

Where:
  X_tp = adjustment factor for tension perpendicular to grain (1.45)
  f_tp = specified strength in tension perpendicular to grain, MPa (Table 7.2)
  K_tp = constant depending on n_R and n_C (Table A.18)
  β_tp = constant depending on S_P and S_Q (Table A.19)

b) C_t = [1 / (β_D * (n_C - 1) * S_Q)]^0.2

Where:
  β_D = constant depending on e_p / [(n_C - 1) * S_Q] (Table A.20)
  e_p = unloaded edge distance, mm (Figure 12.13)


--------------------------------------------------

Clause 59: A.12.9.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
A.12.9.3.3 Lateral deformation of wood-to-wood connections with nails, spikes, or
wood screws
For specified loads, P,not greater than nu/3, the lateral deformation of wood-to-wood connections with
nails, spikes, or wood screws, including structural panel-to-lumber connections, may be estimated as
follows:
Δ = 0.5dfKm(P/nu)^1.7
where
Δ=lateral deformation, mm
dF= nominal diameter offastener, mm
Km=service-creep factor (see Table A.23)
P=specified load per fastener per shear plane, N
nu=unit lateral strength resistance per shear plane, N(see Clause 12.9.3.2)
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 60: A.16 
--------------------------------------------------
A.16 Proprietary structural products —Materials and evaluation
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 61: A.16.2.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
A.16.2.3.1 Length-adjustment factor, KLN
The length-adjustment factor, KLN, isused by manufacturers to develop proprietary I-joist moment
resistance values and is not intended asanadjustment factor for specific applications. The value ofKLN
is taken from Section 6.4.1.5 of ASTM D5055 and is the lesser of 1.0 or the value calculated as follows:
KLN = KSD (L1/L)^z < 1.0
where
KSD =stress distribution adjustment factor
    =the adjustment ofspecified axial strength, fa,from full-length constant stress (such asatension
    test) to the reference stress condition (simple span and uniform load)
    = 1.15
L1 =gauge length (distance between grips) used in tension tests, parallel to grain, for I-joist flange
    material
L=I-joist span
    =18times the joist depth
Z=coefficient that accounts for the variation intensile strength ofthe flange material (see
Table A.24)
--------------------------------------------------
Clause 1: B.1.1 
--------------------------------------------------
Annex B(informative)
Fire resistance oflarge-cross-section wood elements
Notes:
1) This informative (non-mandatory) Annex has been written in normative (mandatory) language to facilitate
adoption where users ofthe Standard orregulatory authorities wish to adopt itformally as additional
requirements tothis Standard.
2) When this informational (non-mandatory) Annex is not otherwise adopted formally by building regulatory
authorities as additional requirements to this Standard, the methodology presented provides information that
may be useful to users ofthe Standard in the development of aproposal for an alternative solution to meet
the objectives ofthe National Building Code of Canada (NBC).
B.1.1
The design tables, data, and methods specified in Annex Bprovide adesign methodology to develop
fire-resistance ratings oflarge-cross-section wood elements based on structural criteria.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 2: B.1.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.1.2
The design methodology is intended to be used as an alternative approach for determining
fire-resistance ratings for establishing compliance to the National Building Code of Canada, as
determined by testing in conformance with CAN/ULC-S101.
Note: The fire performance criteria for evaluating the separating function of building elements related to the
passage offlames or hot gases and transmission of heat through the assembly, as defined in CAN/ULC-S101, are
outside the scope of Annex B, except as otherwise noted.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 3: B.1.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.1.3
The structural resistance of a wood element reduces as afunction of time when exposed to fire. A
structural element is deemed to possess afire-resistance rating for aduration offire exposure provided
the reduced structural resistance ofthe element, after the specified exposure time, is greater than the
specified load effects.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 4: B.1.4 
--------------------------------------------------
B.1.4
The methodology in Annex Bis an engineering approach, intended to predict the structural fire
resistance oflarge-cross-section wood elements exposed to the standard fire-resistance test,
CAN/ULC-S101. The standard test method requires load-bearing elements to be tested with a
superimposed load that represents afull specified load condition or arestricted load use condition.
When calculating the fire-resistance rating using the methodology in Annex B,the specified gravity
loads are used (i.e., D+L).
Note: When aperformance-based fire safety design approach is used in which the specific fire scenario(s) has a
design fire(s) having time-temperature relationships other than that specified inthe CAN/ULC-S101 fire-resistance
test, additional analysis may berequired. For example, aheat transfer analysis may be needed to determine an
appropriate charring rate and zero-strength layer depth. In this case, it may also be appropriate to use the load
factors suggested in Paragraph 25 ofthe most recent edition ofStructural Commentary Aofthe National Building
Code of Canada. Such fire scenarios can be evaluated as an alternative solution to meet the objectives ofthe
National Building Code of Canada.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 5: B.1.5 
--------------------------------------------------
B.1.5
Itis possible that built-up beams as described in Clause 6.4.4.3 and built-up compression members as
described in Clause 6.5.5.4 will not exhibit similar fire performance as similar-sized solid members and
therefore are beyond the scope of Annex B.
Note: Connections between built-up elements are critical for ensuring performance as asingle solid member and,
in some cases, have been shown to be unable to keep the individual elements from separating during fire exposure
thus significantly increasing the charring rate.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 6: B.2.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.2.1 General Materials
Annex Bapplies to the materials specified in Clause 6for timbers and decking, Clause 7for glued-laminated
timber, Clause 8for cross-laminated timber, and Clause 15.3 for structural composite lumber.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 7: B.2.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.2.2 Glued-laminated timber
To calculate the fire resistance of glulam beams using the specified strength values given in Table 7.2,
the following manufacturing requirements shall be fulfilled:
a) Beams targeting a1-hour fire-resistance rating when protected from fire exposure on the top shall
be manufactured to the specified layups, except that one core lamination shall be removed and
one 38-mm-thick outer tension lamination added on the bottom [see Figure B.1 b)].
b) Beams targeting a1-hour fire-resistance rating when not protected from fire exposure on the top
and subjected to positive and negative bending moments shall be manufactured to the specified
layups, except that two core laminations shall be removed and one 38-mm-thick outer tension
lamination added on the top and on the bottom [see Figure B.2 b)].
c) Beams targeting a1.5-or 2-hour fire-resistance rating when protected from fire exposure on the
top shall be manufactured to the specified layups, except that two core laminations shall be
removed and two 38-mm-thick outer tension laminations added on the bottom [see Figure B.1 c)].
d) Beams targeting a1.5-or 2-hour fire-resistance rating when not protected from fire exposure on
the top and subjected to positive and negative bending moments shall be manufactured to the
specified layups, except that four core laminations shall be removed and two 38-mm-thick outer
tension laminations added on the top and on the bottom [see Figure B.2 c)].
Ifthe additional tension laminations are not substituted for core laminations, the specified strength
values ofthe individual laminations shall be used to calculate the fire resistance of glulam beams.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 8: B.2.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.2.3 CLT
When determining the axial orflatwise-bending moment resistance of CLT panels exposed to fire, only
the layers parallel to the direction of the applied stress shall be considered in determination of the fire
resistance ofthe panels.
Note: When high shear stress governs design, such as apoint load from acolumn on afloor element, shear
resistance should be determined. In the case ofshear resistance, alllayers contributing tothe resistance should be
considered.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 9: B.3.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.1 General Factors affecting resistance
The specified strengths of materials and connections used in calculating the resistance shall be
multiplied bythe modification factors specified in Clause B.3 and in the applicable clauses ofthis
Standard.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 10: B.3.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.2 Resistance factor,
The resistance factor, ,shall be taken as 1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 11: B.3.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.3 Load-duration factor, KD
The load-duration factor, KD, shall betaken in accordance with Clause 5.3.2 for short-term load
duration.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 12: B.3.4 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.4 System factor, KH
The system factor, KH, shall betaken as 1.0.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 13: B.3.5 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.5 Size factor, KZ
The size factor, KZ, shall be determined in accordance with applicable Clauses inthis Standard using the
original cross-sectional dimensions.Fire-resistance rating
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 14: B.3.6 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.6 Lateral-stability factor, KL
The lateral-stability factor, KL, shall be determined in accordance with Clause 6.5.3.2 for sawn lumber or
Clause 7.5.6.4 for glued-laminated timber using the effective cross-section ofthe beam (see
Clause B.6.2). To be considered in the calculations, the members providing the intermediate lateral
support shall have atleast the same fire-resistance rating as that sought for the beam.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 15: B.3.7 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.7 Slenderness ratio, CC
The slenderness ratio, CC, shall be determined using the effective cross-section (see Clause B.6.2). To be
considered in the calculations, the members providing the intermediate lateral support shall have at
least the same fire-resistance rating asthat sought for the column.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 16: B.3.8 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.8 Slenderness factor, KC
The slenderness factor, KC, shall be determined using the effective cross-section (see Clause B.6.2) and
the specified mean modulus of elasticity (see Clause B.6.4).
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 17: B.3.9 
--------------------------------------------------
B.3.9 Adjustment factor for fire resistance, Kfi
The adjustment factor for fire resistance, Kfi, shall be determined asgiven in Table B.1.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 18: B.4.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.1 General Char layer depth 
The charring rates in Table B.2 apply when members are exposed to the standard fire exposure in
accordance with CAN/ULC-S101. Clause B.4.3 shall be used to determine the char layer depth for one-dimensional
heat transfer, such asin solid wood walls and floors or when corner rounding is explicitly
considered for rectangular cross-sections following Clause B.4.5. For CLT, the char layer depth shall be
determined in accordance with Clause B.4.6. For all other cases, the char layer depth shall be
determined in accordance with Clause B.4.4.
Note: Use ofthe notional charring rate in Clause B.4.4 isrecommended when considering rectangular cross-section
members because the method implicitly accounts for the effect ofcracking, formation offissures, and corner
rounding.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 19: B.4.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.2 Charring rates
The one-dimensional and notational charring rates, o and n, are given in Table B.2.

Note: When the smallest dimension ofthe effective cross-section ofa member subjected to heating on parallel
sides isreduced toless than 70 mm, the charring rate will increase asthe temperature rise beyond the char front
meets in the middle ofthe cross-section. In this case, aheat transfer analysis may be required to determine the
proper effective cross-section to use.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 20: B.4.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.3 One-dimensional char layer depth
The char layer depth for one-dimensional charring, xc,o (mm), shall be calculated asfollows:
xc,o =βot
where
βo= one-dimensional charring rate, mm/min
t=fire exposure duration, min
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 21: B.4.4 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.4 Notional char layer depth
The char layer depth for notional charring, xc,n (mm), shall becalculated asfollows:
xc,n =βnt
where
βn= notional charring rate, mm/min
t=fire exposure duration, min
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 22: B.4.5 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.5 Corner rounding
The corners ofrectangular cross-sections exposed to fire are subjected to two-dimensional heat transfer
resulting in acorner-rounding effect. When explicitly considering the effect of corner rounding, the
radius ofthe corner shall be taken asthe depth ofthe charred layer using the one-dimensional charring
rate, in accordance with Clause B.4.3, and the section properties shall be determined accordingly.
Note: The effect of corner rounding is not required to be considered explicitly when the char layer depth is
determined in accordance with Clause B.4.4.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 23: B.4.6 
--------------------------------------------------
B.4.6 Char layer depth for CLT
The one-dimensional charring rate, o, specified in Table B.2 and Clause B.4.3 shall be used when the
char layer depth will not reach the first bond line between the exposed layer and the subsequent layer
for the duration ofthe fire resistance required. Ifthe char layer depth surpasses the first bond line
during the fire-resistance period sought, the notional charring rate, n, specified in Table B.2 and
Clause B.4.4 shall be used.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 24: B.5 
--------------------------------------------------
B.5 Zero-strength layer depth
To account for areduction in strength ofthe heated wood beyond the char front, azero-strength layer
shall be subtracted to further reduce the cross-section beyond the char layer depth determined in
Clause B.4.3 orB.4.4. The zero-strength layer depth, xt(mm), shall be calculated asfollows:
xt=(t/20) x 7 (for t<20)
xt=7(for t>=20)
where
t =fire exposure duration, min
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 25: B.6 
--------------------------------------------------
B.6 Resistance of effective cross-section
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 26: B.6.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.6.1 General
Charring ofall surfaces ofawood element directly exposed to fire shall be taken into account including,
where relevant, any surfaces initially protected from fire exposure where wood charring could occur at
some point during the standard fire exposure for fire-resistance rating required. The effective cross-section
shall be assumed to have properties as specified in Clauses B.6.3 and B.6.4, while the char layer
and zero-strength layer shall be assumed to provide no strength or stiffness.
Note: Only surfaces protected from fire exposure for the duration ofthe exposure, such asthe top surface of a
beam protected by afire-resistance-rated floor orroof assembly, may be considered to be protected from the fire
for the duration ofthe exposure.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 27: B.6.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.6.2 Effective cross-section
The effective cross-section shall be the initial cross-section reduced by the char layer depth (see
Clause B.4) and the zero-strength layer depth (see Clause B.5) on each exposed surface (see Figure B.2).
Section properties shall be calculated using standard equations for area, section modulus, and moment
ofinertia using the dimensions ofthe effective cross-section.
Note: In some instances, such asthe effective cross-section of CLT, the location ofthe neutral axis must be
determined prior to calculating the moment ofinertia and section modulus. In addition, for calculating the section
modulus ofCLT, the height divided by 2(h/2) must bereplaced with c,the distance from the extreme (bottom)
tension fibre to the neutral axis, thus replacing 2/h with 1/c in the section modulus equation.

--------------------------------------------------

Clause 28: B.6.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.6.3 Resistance ofthe effective cross-section
The resistances ofthe members exposed to fire shall be calculated in accordance with the applicable
equations in Clauses 6, 7, 8and 15.3 using the strength properties modified in accordance with
Clause B.3 and the effective cross-section in accordance to Clause B.6.2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 29: B.6.4 
--------------------------------------------------
B.6.4 Modulus of elasticity
The modulus of elasticity used in calculating the resistance of the member shall be taken as the
specified mean value.
Note: The modulus ofelasticity is used in calculations ofthe lateral-stability factor for bending members, KL, and
the slenderness factor for compression members, Kc.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 30: B.7 
--------------------------------------------------
B.7 Fire-resistance rating
Astructural element shall be assigned afire-resistance rating of aduration offire exposure ifthe
effective structural resistance ofthe element for that fire exposure is greater than the specified gravity
load effects.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 31: B.8 
--------------------------------------------------
B.8 Surfaces protected by gypsum board
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 32: B.8.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.8.1 Gypsum board
Provided that surfaces are protected from fire exposure by fire-rated Type Xgypsum board, the
assigned fire-resistance duration calculated in accordance with Clause B.7 can be increased by the
following times:
a) 15 min when one layer of 12.7 mm Type Xgypsum board is used;

b) 30 min when one layer of 15.9 mm Type Xgypsum board is used;
c) 60 min when two layers of 15.9 mm Type Xgypsum boards are used; or
d) 60 min when two layers of 12.7 mm Type Xgypsum boards are applied to CLT.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 33: B.8.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.8.2 Gypsum board fasteners
The values in Clause B.8.1 shall only apply where the fasteners used to attach the gypsum board
penetrate the wood element a minimum of 25 mm and are spaced a maximum of 300 mm on centre
and each length of gypsum board is attached by a minimum oftwo rows offasteners that are offset by
half the fastener spacing ifrow spacing isless than 300 mm.
Note: Steel or wood furring providing agap between the gypsum board and wood member will not reduce the
additional fire resistance attributed to the gypsum board, provided the gypsum board fastener spacing
requirements in Clause B.8.2 are met and the fasteners used to attach the furring penetrate the wood structural
elements aminimum of 25 mm.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 34: B.8.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.8.3 Joints
The values in Clause B.8.1 shall only apply where the exposed joints ofthe gypsum board are taped and
finished. When multiple layers of 15.9 mm Type Xgypsum board described in Clause B.8.1 are used, the
joints shall be offset between the base layer and face layer.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 35: B.9 
--------------------------------------------------
B.9 Connections
Connections that are critical to support the gravity loads acting on the structure shall be designed to
have atleast the same fire-resistance rating as the elements they support. Connections in which the
steel islocated within the effective cross-section ofthe wood element shall be considered properly
protected.
Note: Additional information can be found in the American Wood Council’s Technical Report 10 and in
EN 1995-1-2.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 36: B.10.1 
--------------------------------------------------
B.10.1 Double tongue-and-groove
Double tongued-and-grooved decking shall be designed as an assembly of wood beams fully exposed on
one face.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 37: B.10.2 
--------------------------------------------------
B.10.2 Single tongue-and-groove orinternal spline
Single tongued-and-grooved orsingle internal splined decking shall be designed as an assembly of wood
beams fully exposed on one face, provided the loss in depth ofthe effective cross-section has not yet
reached the tongue-and-groove orinternal spline.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 38: B.10.3 
--------------------------------------------------
B.10.3 Butt-jointed
Butt joints shall be designed as an assembly of wood beams partially exposed on the sides and fully
exposed on one face. To compute the effects of partial exposure ofthe decking elements on their sides,
the char rate for this partial exposure shall be reduced to 1/3 ofthe char rate ofthat used on the
exposed face.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 39: B.10.4 
--------------------------------------------------
B.10.4 Unexposed surface protection
The methodology in Clauses B.10.1 to B.10.3 shall apply only to solid wood decks that have the
unexposed (top) surface ofthe decking protected by:
a) tongued-and-grooved wood flooring not less than 19 mm thick laid crosswise or diagonally;

b) tongued-and-grooved plywood or OSB not less than 12.5 mm thick;
c) concrete topping of minimum 38 mm thickness; or
d) gypsum-concrete topping of minimum 25 mm thickness.
Note: These prescriptive requirements are intended to address the fire performance criteria for evaluating the
separating function ofbuilding assemblies related to the passage offlames or hot gases and transmission of heat
through the assembly as defined in CAN/ULC-S101. Additional information can befound in Section 3.1.4.7 and
Appendix D-2.4 ofthe National Building Code of Canada for solid wood floors and roofs.
--------------------------------------------------

Clause 40: B.11 
--------------------------------------------------
B.11 Fire performance criteria for evaluating separating function of
building assemblies
The fire performance criteria for evaluating the separating function of building assemblies related to the
passage offlames or hot gases and transmission of heat through the assembly, as defined in
CAN/ULC-S101, shall be considered when required by the applicable building code.
--------------------------------------------------
